Definition and Purpose of Adab in Prayer
Defines adab linguistically and terminologically, explains its purpose.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi terminological definition of adab and explain its role in the hierarchy of prayer actions.

Core Idea
Adab in prayer are occasional prophetic actions that perfect the sunnah, which perfects the wajib, which perfects the fard.

Many students think adab is just 'good manners' in prayer, but the Hanafi school defines it technically. This passage clarifies the linguistic and technical meaning, gives concrete examples, and shows how adab fits into a layered system of obligation. Understanding this hierarchy is key to knowing when an action is merely recommended versus required.

Guided Path
1
Linguistic definition
Identify the Arabic root and general meaning of adab as discipline and study, quoting al-Jawhari.
This step grounds the technical term in everyday language.
2
Terminological definition
Focus on the istilah: actions the Prophet (ﷺ) performed once or twice without persistence. Know the examples: extra tasbihat in ruku/sujud, extra qira'ah.
The key is the lack of persistence, not just recommendation.
3
Purpose (hikmah)
Understand the chain: adab perfects sunnah, sunnah perfects wajib, wajib perfects fard. Each lower layer enhances the higher.
This hierarchy explains why adab is not obligatory but still valuable.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل من آداب الصلاة
أشرنا بمن التبعيضية إلى أننا لم نستقص أفراد الأدب، بل ذكرنا ما تيسر منه. والأدب في اللغة معلوم، قال الجوهري: الأدب أدب النفس والدرس، تقول منه: أدب الرجل، فهو أديب. وأدبته فتأدب. وفي الاصطلاح هو كل ما فعله الرسول ﷺ مرة أو مرتين، ولم يواظب عليه، كزيادة التسبيحات في الركوع والسجود، والزيادة على القراءة المسنونة، كما في (العناية)، و (الدراية)، وغيرهما. والأدب شرع لإكمال السنة، والسنة لإكمال الواجب، والواجب لإكمال الفرض. كما في (البزازية)
Chapter on the etiquette of prayer. We indicated with 'min' (partitive) that we did not exhaust all individual etiquettes, but rather mentioned what was easy from it. And 'adab' in language is known. Al-Jawhari said: Adab is the discipline of the soul and study; you say from it: 'aduba al-rajulu' (the man was well-mannered), so he is 'adib'. And 'addabtuhu' (I taught him), so he 'ta'addaba'. And in terminology, it is everything that the Messenger (peace be upon him) did once or twice, and did not persist upon, like the increase of tasbihat in bowing and prostration, and the increase over the prescribed recitation, as in al-'Inayah, al-Dirayah, and others. And the etiquette was legislated to complete the sunnah, and the sunnah to complete the obligatory, and the obligatory to complete the fard, as in al-Bazzaziyyah.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage is a definition and purpose statement for the term 'adab' in the context of prayer. The author explains that the word 'adab' has a linguistic meaning related to good manners and discipline, and quotes al-Jawhari. In the technical fiqh terminology (istilah), adab refers to actions that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) performed only occasionally, not consistently. Examples given are increasing the number of tasbihat (glorifications) in ruku' and sujud beyond the sunnah amount, or reciting more than the prescribed recitation (al-qira'ah al-masnunah). The purpose of adab is to perfect (ikmal) the sunnah, which in turn perfects the wajib (obligatory but less than fard), which perfects the fard (definitive obligation). Thus adab is the outermost layer of recommended practice that supports higher obligations. The author cites several sources (al-'Inayah, al-Dirayah, al-Bazzaziyyah) to establish this hierarchy.

Key Terms
الأدب (al-adab): In istilah: actions performed by the Prophet occasionally, not regularly, which are recommended to perfect the sunnah.
السنة (al-sunnah): Actions the Prophet did regularly or encouraged; here it is a category between adab and wajib.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, what is the terminological definition of 'adab' in prayer?
A) Any action done by the Prophet in every prayer
B) Actions done by the Prophet once or twice without persistence
C) Any recommended action in prayer
D) Actions that complete the fard directly

Key Takeaway
Adab in prayer are occasional prophetic actions legislated to perfect the sunnah, forming the outermost layer of recommendation.

Men Removing Hands from Sleeves at Takbir: An Adab of Prayer
Ruling on men removing hands from sleeves at takbir

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for men, women, and khuntha regarding removing hands from sleeves at takbir al-ihram, and explain the rationale.

Core Idea
Removing hands from sleeves at takbir is an adab for men; women and khuntha keep them inside to avoid exposing 'awrah.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains an etiquette of prayer: the handling of one's hands at the opening takbir. While men are encouraged to remove their hands from sleeves as a sign of humility and to facilitate proper finger spreading, women and those of ambiguous gender are instructed to keep their hands inside to maintain concealment. Understanding this distinction helps us appreciate how the Sharia balances ritual form with modesty.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling category
The act is removing hands from sleeves at takbir al-ihram. The text calls it 'from the etiquettes of prayer' (min adab al-salah), making it a sunnah/adab, not fard or wajib.
Adab are recommended acts that enhance the prayer but are not obligatory.
2
Understand the rationale for men
The reasons given: closer to humility (tawadu'), avoids resembling tyrants (jababira), and enables spreading fingers. An exception is made for necessity like extreme cold.
Spreading fingers is part of the sunnah posture during takbir.
3
Understand the exception for women
Women should not remove hands because it would expose their forearms, which are 'awrah. Their state in prayer is based on concealment (satr).
Forearms are part of the woman's 'awrah in prayer according to the Hanafi school.
4
Apply to khuntha
The hermaphrodite (khuntha) is treated like a woman out of precaution (ihtiyat) to avoid any possibility of exposing 'awrah.
Precaution dictates treating ambiguous gender as female for concealment rulings.
5
Recognize the scope
The ruling applies specifically at takbir al-ihram (the initial takbir), not necessarily at other takbirs in the prayer.
Some later Hanafi texts extend this to all takbirs, but the primary focus is the opening takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمن آداب الصلاة (إخراجُ الرَّجُلِ كَفَيْهِ مِنْ كُمَّيْهِ عِنْدَ التَّكْبير) أي: تكبير الإحرام؛ لأنه أقرب إلى التواضع، وأبعد من التشبه بالجبابرة، وأمكن من نشر الأصابع إلا لضرورة برد ونحوه. ولا تخرج المرأة كفيها، لأنه يؤدي إلى كشف ساعديها، وهما عورة ومبنى حالها على الستر، والخنثى كالمرأة احتياطاً.
So from the etiquettes of prayer: (A man removing his two hands from his two sleeves at the takbir), i.e., takbir al-ihram; because it is closer to humility, further from resembling tyrants, and more enabling for spreading fingers except for necessity of cold and the like. And the woman does not remove her two hands, because it leads to exposing her two forearms, and they are 'awrah and her state is based on concealment. And the hermaphrodite is like a woman as a precaution.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage states the ruling (hukm) that it is an adab (etiquette) for a man to remove his hands from his sleeves when making the opening takbir (takbir al-ihram). This is recommended because it demonstrates humility, avoids resemblance to arrogant tyrants (jababira), and makes it easier to spread the fingers as part of the takbir posture. However, if there is a necessity like extreme cold, it is excused. For women, the ruling is the opposite: she should not remove her hands from her sleeves, because doing so would expose her forearms, which are part of her 'awrah (body parts that must be covered in prayer). Since a woman's primary state in prayer is concealment (satr), she keeps her hands inside. A hermaphrodite (khuntha) is treated like a woman out of precaution (ihtiyat) to avoid any possibility of exposing 'awrah. The commentary notes that this is for the opening takbir specifically because that is the moment when hands are raised.

Key Terms
تكبير الإحرام (takbir al-ihram): The first 'Allahu Akbar' that begins the prayer.
الخنثى (al-khuntha): A person with ambiguous gender characteristics; treated as woman in this ruling out of precaution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it recommended for a man to remove his hands from his sleeves at takbir al-ihram?
A) To show his hands are clean
B) To avoid resembling tyrants and facilitate spreading fingers
C) To keep his sleeves from touching the ground
D) To ensure his palms are visible

Key Takeaway
Men remove hands from sleeves at takbir as an adab; women and khuntha keep them covered to protect 'awrah.

Gaze Directions in Prayer: Posture-by-Posture Guidance
Rules for gaze directions in prayer postures

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended gaze direction for each posture of prayer according to the Hanafi madhhab and explain the underlying rationale of khushu'.

Core Idea
The gaze follows the posture, always aiming to enhance khushu' and avoid distraction.

Prayer is an act of profound devotion, and the physical postures are accompanied by inner focus. One way the Hanafi school helps maintain this focus is by prescribing specific directions for the worshipper's gaze at each stage of the prayer. This lesson unpacks those recommendations, explains the reason behind them, and addresses a debate about whether one should look at the Ka'bah if visible.

Guided Path
1
Identify each prayer posture
The passage mentions five postures: standing, bowing, prostrating, sitting between prostrations (or during tashahhud), and the final salam.
These cover the main positions of the obligatory prayer.
2
Note the prescribed gaze for each
For standing: look at the place of prostration. For bowing: the top of the feet. For prostration: the tip of the nose. For sitting: the lap. For salam: the right shoulder first, then left.
The text explicitly states these for men and women alike.
3
Understand the reason: khushu'
Each direction is chosen because it is 'ad’ā ilā al-khushū‘' (more conducive to calmness and focus). The goal is to prevent the mind from wandering by fixing the gaze on a humbling spot.
Khushu' involves both calmness of limbs and presence of heart.
4
Examine the debate about looking at the Ka'bah
Some scholars (e.g., al-Muhibb al-Ṭabarī) permitted looking at the Ka'bah if it enhances khushu', but the relied-upon Hanafi view (al-madhhab) is to always look at the place of prostration, because one cannot be sure of not being distracted.
This shows how the school prioritises minimizing potential distraction.
5
Apply the principle to special cases
The passage extends the rule: if it is dark or the worshipper is blind, the focus should be on the meaning of the hadith 'Worship Allah as if you see Him…' and maintaining mindfulness of Allah's greatness.
Thus the external gaze is secondary to inner concentration.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَنَظَرُ المُصَلِّي) سواء كان رجلاً أو امرأة (إلى مَوْضِعِ سُجُودِهِ قَائِمَاً) حفظاً له عن النظر إلى ما يشغله عن الخشوع، وسنذكر أن الخشوع محله القلب وهو: تسكين الجوارح، أو هما جميعاً. وفي إطلاق النظر إلى موضع السجود شمول المشاهد للكعبة، وقال الجلال السيوطي في (الينبوع): قال الأوزاعي: حكى المحب الطبري وجهاً أنه إن كان يشاهد الكعبة، فينظر إليها مع توفر الخشوع واستحسنه. ثم قال: والمذهب النظر إلى موضع سجوده مطلقاً، لأنه لا يأمن ما يلهيه. انتهى. (وَ) نظره (إلى ظَاهِرِ القَدَمِ رَاكِعَاً) لأنه أدعى إلى الخشوع. (و) نظره (إلى أَرْنَبَةِ أَنْفِهِ سَاجَداً) لأن تصويب النظر إليها أقرب إلى الخشوع. (وإلى حجره جَالِسَاً) لئلا ينظر إلى ما يشغله عما هو فيه من الخشوع استحضاراً لعظمة مولاه، ويكون ملاحظاً قوله: (اعْبُدِ اللَّهَ كَأَنَّكَ تَرَاهُ فَإِنْ لَمْ تَكُنْ تَرَاهُ فَإِنَّهُ يَرَاكَ). (وَ) نظره (إلى المَنْكِبَيْن مُسَلَّماً) فينظر إلى أيمنه في الأول، وإلى أيسره في الثاني، لأن المقصود الخشوع، وترك التكلف. فإذا تركه صار ناظراً إلى هذه المواضع قصداً ولم يقصد، وإذا كان في الظلام أو كان بصيراً يلاحظ مؤدى الحديث، ويحافظ على مراقبة عظمة الله، لأن المدار عليها.
(And the worshipper's looking, whether man or woman, at his place of prostration while standing) to preserve him from looking at what distracts him from khushu'. And we will mention that khushu' has its place in the heart, and it is: calming the limbs, or both together. And in the unconditionality of looking at the place of prostration is the inclusion of one who sees the Ka'bah. And al-Jalal al-Suyuti said in al-Yanbu': al-Awza'i said: al-Muhibb al-Tabari narrated a view that if he sees the Ka'bah, he should look at it while maintaining khushu', and he approved it. Then he said: The madhhab is to look at his place of prostration absolutely, because he is not secure from what distracts him. End. (And his looking at the apparent part of the foot while bowing) because it is more conducive to khushu'. (And his looking at the tip of his nose while prostrating) because directing the gaze to it is closer to khushu'. (And at his lap while sitting) so that he does not look at what distracts him from what he is in regarding khushu', summoning the greatness of his Lord, and he should be heedful of his saying: 'Worship Allah as if you see Him, for if you do not see Him, He sees you.' (And his looking at the two shoulders while saying the salam) so he looks to his right on the first and to his left on the second, because the objective is khushu' and avoiding affectation. So if he does that, he becomes looking at these places intentionally and unintentionally. And if he is in darkness or is blind, he observes the import of the hadith and maintains mindfulness of Allah's greatness, because the focus is upon that.
Source pages p. 284

Commentary
This passage details the recommended (adab) directions of gaze for each posture of prayer. For all worshippers (men and women alike), when standing, one should look at the place of prostration to aid concentration. The commentary notes that there is a difference of opinion regarding one who can see the Ka'bah: some, like al-Muhibb al-Tabari, suggest looking at it if it enhances khushu', but the relied-upon Hanafi position (al-madhhab) is to always look at the prostration spot to avoid any distraction. In bowing (ruku'), look at the top of the feet. In prostration (sujood), look at the tip of the nose. When sitting (jalsah), look at one's lap. When saying the salam (taslim), first look at the right shoulder, then the left. The underlying principle is to maximize khushu' (reverent focus) and avoid looking around unnecessarily. For a person who is blind or in darkness, the instruction is to reflect on the meaning of the hadith 'Worship Allah as if you see Him...' and remain mindful of Allah's greatness.

Key Terms
الخشوع (al-khushu'): Calmness of the limbs and focus of the heart; the aim of these gaze directions.
المذهب (al-madhhab): The relied-upon legal opinion of the Hanafi school, as opposed to other views.
السجود (al-sujūd): Prostration; one of the pillars of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, where should a worshipper look while standing in prayer?
A) At the Ka'bah if visible
B) At his hands
C) At his place of prostration
D) Straight ahead

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the worshipper's gaze is directed to the place of prostration (standing), top of feet (bowing), tip of nose (prostrating), lap (sitting), and shoulders (taslim), all to cultivate khushu'.

Suppressing Cough and Yawning in Prayer: Etiquettes and Proofs
Etiquettes of suppressing cough and yawning in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on suppressing cough and yawning in prayer, identify the hadith proofs, and explain the reason for these etiquettes.

Core Idea
Suppressing cough and yawning protects prayer validity; Satan laughs at yawning.

In the Hanafi school, the perfection of prayer is not only about fulfilling obligations but also observing etiquettes (adab). This lesson focuses on two such etiquettes: suppressing cough as much as possible and closing the mouth during yawning. These actions preserve the integrity of the prayer and prevent invalidation from unintentional letters. The proofs are from the Prophet's ﷺ warnings about Satan's involvement in yawning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage states that suppressing cough and closing the mouth during yawning are from the etiquettes (adab) of prayer. In Hanafi fiqh, these are recommended (sunnah) actions, not obligations.
Adab implies that performing them is rewarded but omission is not sinful, though may be disliked.
2
Understand the reason for suppression
Coughing or yawning can produce letters (e.g., 'ah') that, if intentional or without excuse, may invalidate prayer. Suppression minimizes this risk.
The text says 'تحرزاً عن المفسد' (out of caution against what invalidates).
3
Analyze the hadith proofs
Two hadiths are cited: one stating 'yawning in prayer is from Satan' and ordering suppression, and another warning that Satan laughs at the yawner. These establish the disliked nature of yawning in prayer.
The hadiths are from standard collections; their lesson is to avoid giving Satan an opportunity.
4
Differentiate between similar actions
The passage mentions belching (al-jasha') alongside cough, indicating the same ruling. For yawning, covering with hand or sleeve is an alternative if lips cannot be pressed.
If the yawn is uncontrollable, the prayer remains valid; the etiquette is to minimize it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) من الأدب (دَفْعُ السُّعَالِ مَا اسْتَطَاعَ) تحرزاً عن المفسد، لأنه لو كان بغير عذر فسدت صلاته بما يحصل من الحروف، كأح، فيحترز ما أمكن، وكذا الجشاء. (وَ) من الأدب (كَظْمُ فَمِهِ عِنْدَ التَّثَاؤُبِ) فيطبق فمه، فإن لم يقدر غطاه بيده أو كمه؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: التثاؤب في الصلاة من الشيطان، فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليكظم ما استطاع. ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: إذا تشاءب أحدكم فليردده ما استطاع، فإن أحدكم إذا تثاءب ضحك منه الشيطان.
(And) from the etiquette (suppressing cough as much as possible) out of caution against what invalidates, because if it is without excuse, his prayer becomes invalidated by the letters that result, like 'ah', so he should be cautious as much as possible, and likewise belching. (And) from the etiquette (closing his mouth at the time of yawning) so he closes his mouth, and if he cannot, he covers it with his hand or sleeve; because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Yawning in prayer is from Satan, so if one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible.' And because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'When one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as possible, for if one of you yawns, Satan laughs at him.'
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage covers two connected etiquettes for prayer: suppressing cough and handling yawns. The worshipper should try to suppress a cough as much as possible, because if a cough produces intelligible letters (like 'ah') without a valid excuse (like illness), it may invalidate the prayer. Similarly, belching (jasha') is to be avoided. For yawning, the worshipper should close his mouth by pressing lips together. If unable, he should cover his mouth with his hand or sleeve. The proof is from two hadiths: one stating that yawning in prayer is from Satan and should be suppressed, and another warning that Satan laughs at a person when they yawn. These actions are adab (recommended etiquettes) aimed at preserving the validity and perfection of prayer.

Key Terms
الجشاء (al-jasha'): Belching; considered similar to cough in requiring suppression.
التثاؤب (al-tatha'ub): Yawning; an act associated with Satan in prayer, to be suppressed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What should a worshipper do if he yawns during prayer according to the hadith cited?
A) Say 'Alhamdulillah' immediately
B) Suppress it as much as possible
C) Stop praying and restart
D) Cover his mouth with his hand only

Key Takeaway
Suppressing cough and yawning in prayer are recommended etiquettes to preserve validity and avoid Satan's influence.

When to Stand During Iqamah
Ruling on when the congregation should stand for prayer during iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on when the congregation should stand during the iqamah, applying the appropriate condition based on the imam's location and role.

Core Idea
Standing during iqamah is sunnah at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', but timing adjusts if the imam is absent or if he calls the iqamah himself.

This lesson examines a passage from Imdad al-Fattah that details the recommended timing for the congregation to stand when the iqamah is being called. While the default adab is to stand upon hearing 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', the text presents several nuanced scenarios depending on the imam's location and whether he is the mu'adhdhin. Understanding these details ensures proper mosque etiquette and helps avoid missing the sunnah of starting prayer simultaneously with the imam.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
Determine the basic Hanafi position: the congregation should stand when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' during the iqamah, because it is a command implying haste.
This is the general adab for prayer.
2
Note the exceptions based on imam's location
Observe how the ruling changes if the imam is not present near the mihrab: the congregation waits until he arrives, then stands when they see him or when he reaches their row.
The preferred view is that each row stands when the imam reaches that row (al-azhar).
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute
Read the reflection from al-Bahr: if the mu'adhdhin is the imam himself, some say the congregation should not stand until he finishes the iqamah. However, this may cause missing muqaranat al-ihram, so the stronger view is to stand at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'.
The author notes this contradiction and leans toward preserving simultaneous takbir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) من الأدب (القِيَامُ) أي: قيام القوم، والإمام إذا كان حاضراً بقرب المحراب (حينَ قِيلَ) أي: وقت قول المقيم (حَيَّ عَلَى الفلاح)؛ لأنه أمر به فيستحب المسارعة إليه. وإن لم يكن الإمام حاضراً لا يقومون حتى يصل إليهم. ويقف مكانه في رواية، وفي أخرى يقومون إذا اختلط بهم، وقيل: يقوم كل صف حين ينتهي إليه الإمام وهو الأظهر. وإذا دخل من قدام وقفوا حين يرونه. قال في (البحر) عن (الظهيرية): هذا إذا كان المؤذن غير الإمام، فإن كان هو وأقام في المسجد، فالقوم لا يقومون حتى يفرغ من إقامته. انتهى. وفيه تأمل: لأنه يؤدي إلى فوات مقارنة الإحرام بإحرام الإمام.
(And) from the etiquette (standing), i.e., standing of the people, and the imam if he is present near the mihrab (when it is said), i.e., at the time of the mu'adhdhin's saying ('Hayya 'ala al-falah'), because it is a command, so it is recommended to hasten to it. And if the imam is not present, they do not stand until he reaches them. And he stands in his place in one narration, and in another they stand when he mixes with them. And it is said: every row stands when the imam reaches them, and that is the most apparent. And if he enters from the front, they stand when they see him. He said in al-Bahr from al-Zuhayriyyah: This is when the mu'adhdhin is other than the imam; if he himself calls the iqamah in the mosque, then the people do not stand until he finishes his iqamah. End. And there is reflection in this: because it leads to losing the simultaneous joining of ihram with the ihram of the imam.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended timing for the congregation to stand up when the iqamah is being called. The default adab is to stand when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' (the second call in the iqamah). However, there are several considerations depending on the imam's location. If the imam is already present near the mihrab (prayer niche), the congregation stands at that point. If the imam has not yet arrived, they wait until he comes to them. If the imam enters from the front, they stand upon seeing him. The commentary cites al-Bahr al-Ra'iq and al-Zuhayriyyah that if the mu'adhdhin is also the imam (i.e., he calls the iqamah himself), the congregation should not stand until he finishes the entire iqamah. However, the author notes a possible issue with this: it might cause them to miss joining the ihram with the imam's ihram (i.e., starting prayer together). The preferred view (al-azhar) is that each row stands when the imam reaches that row.

Key Terms
المقيم (al-muqim): The person calling the iqamah (second call to prayer).
مقارنة الإحرام (muqaranat al-ihram): The simultaneous starting of the prayer by the imam and followers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When should the congregation stand if the imam is present near the mihrab?
A) At the beginning of the iqamah
B) When the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'
C) When the imam enters the mosque
D) After the iqamah is completed

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah is to stand during the iqamah upon hearing 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', unless the imam is absent, in which case stand when he reaches you, and if the imam calls the iqamah himself, the preferred view is still to stand at 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'.

Imam Starting at Qad Qamat al-Salah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam's timing during iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two Hanafi positions on when the imam begins prayer during iqamah and explain the reasoning behind the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
The imam should start praying at 'Qad qamat al-salah' to protect the mu'adhdhin's truthfulness, not after the full iqamah.

This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi disagreement about the recommended timing for the imam to commence his prayer (ihram) during the iqamah. It is not a matter of obligation but of proper conduct (adab). The author presents the views of the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) versus Abu Yusuf, along with their justifications, and then offers subtle critiques. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate reasoning within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Determine the specific point of disagreement: when should the imam begin his ihram during the iqamah? Note that it is a recommended practice (adab), not a fard or wajib.
The ruling here is about etiquette, not obligation.
2
State the two positions
Summarize the view of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two) and that of Abu Yusuf. The two say at 'Qad qamat al-salah'; Abu Yusuf says after the entire iqamah.
These are all within the Hanafi school.
3
Examine the reasoning of each
Understand the dalil for each position: The two argue that the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy and starting at that phrase prevents his statement from being false; Abu Yusuf argues it preserves the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin and helps him start with the imam.
The two emphasize truthfulness and hastening; Abu Yusuf emphasizes following and assisting.
4
Analyze the critiques
Read how the author (and al-Zayla'i) critique both arguments: Abu Yusuf's reasoning is inconsistent because he himself considers following better; the two's reasoning about falsehood is weak because 'qad qamat' refers to imminent establishment, not the exact moment.
The critique is subtle and shows the depth of Hanafi legal reasoning.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude which position is relied upon in the school. Despite the critiques, the view of the two is the operative position in practice.
Tarjih based on common practice and majority preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) من الأدب (شُرُوعُ الإِمَامِ) أي: إحرامه (مُذْ قِيلَ) أي: عنـــد قول المقيم (قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلاةُ)، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف: يشرع إذا فرغ من الإقامة محافظة على فضيلة متابعة المؤذن، أي إجابته، وإعانة للمؤذن على الشروع معه. ولهما: أن المؤذن أمين وقد أخبر بقيام الصلاة فيشرع عنده صوناً لكلامه عن الكذب وفيه مسارعة إلى المناجاة، وقد تابع المؤذن في الأكثر، فيقوم مقام الكل على أنهم قالوا: المتابعة في الأذان دون الإقامة، كذا قال الزيلعي. وفي التعليل لأبي يوسف بإعانة المؤذن على الشروع معه تأمل، لأن عنده الأفضل متابعته، لأن مقارنته لإحرام الإمام كما تقدم. وفي تعليله لهما بصون كلامه عن الكذب تأمل أيضاً، لأن ما قرب من الشيء يطلق عليه كقوله: (لقنوا موتاكم لا إله إلا الله).
(And) from the etiquette (the imam's starting) i.e., his ihram (when it is said), i.e., at the mu'adhdhin's saying ('Qad qamat al-salah'). And this is according to them (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). And Abu Yusuf said: He starts when he finishes the iqamah, preserving the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin, i.e., responding to him, and helping the mu'adhdhin to start with him. And for them (the two): that the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy and has informed of the establishment of prayer, so he (imam) starts at that to protect his words from lying, and in it is hastening to intimate conversation with Allah. And he has followed the mu'adhdhin in most [of the iqamah], so it stands in place of all, based on their statement: The following is in the adhan not the iqamah. Thus said al-Zayla'i. And in Abu Yusuf's reasoning of helping the mu'adhdhin to start with him there is reflection, because in his view the better is following him, because his (the mu'adhdhin's) simultaneous joining with the imam's ihram is as previously mentioned. And in their reasoning of protecting his words from lying there is also reflection, because something close to the thing is referred to it, like his saying: 'Prompt your dying ones to say La ilaha illa Allah.'
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute (ikhtilaf) regarding the recommended time for the imam to begin his prayer (ihram) during the iqamah. The two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that the imam should start his prayer at the phrase 'Qad qamat al-salah' (The prayer has been established). Their reasoning is that the mu'adhdhin is a trustworthy person; by saying that phrase he is informing that the prayer is ready, so for the imam to delay would make the mu'adhdhin's statement seem false. Also, it allows hastening to prayer. Abu Yusuf, on the other hand, says the imam should start only after the entire iqamah is finished. He argues that this preserves the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin (by not starting before he finishes) and helps the mu'adhdhin by allowing him to start with the imam. The commentary (from al-Zayla'i) notes that following the mu'adhdhin is recommended in the adhan (first call) but not in the iqamah. The author then critiques both positions: Abu Yusuf's reasoning is problematic because he himself considers it better to follow the mu'adhdhin, which would mean starting together, not after. And the two's reasoning about protecting from lying is weak because the phrase 'qad qamat' refers to the imminent establishment, not the exact moment. Despite the criticism, the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, as it is the more common practice.

Key Terms
عندهما (indahuma): According to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani).
متابعة المؤذن (mutaba'at al-mu'adhdhin): The recommended practice of repeating the mu'adhdhin's words during adhan and iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) At the beginning of the iqamah
B) When the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'
C) When the mu'adhdhin says 'Qad qamat al-salah'
D) After the iqamah is completely finished

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi holds that the imam should begin his prayer at the phrase 'Qad qamat al-salah' to uphold the mu'adhdhin's truthfulness and hasten worship.

The Five Recommended Acts (Adab) in Prayer
Summary listing of five recommended acts in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five recommended acts (adab) in prayer and explain why they are not obligatory.

Core Idea
Suppressing cough, yawning etiquette, standing at 'Hayya al-falah', imam starts at 'Qad qamati al-salah', and awe of Allah—all are adab, not fard.

This passage from Nur al-Idah lists five specific acts that the Hanafi school considers recommended (adab) during prayer. Understanding these helps distinguish between what is required and what is simply virtuous, ensuring your prayer is both valid and excellent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
Recognize that these five acts are classified as 'adab' (recommended conduct). In Hanafi fiqh, adab is below sunnah; omission does not invalidate the prayer or require compensation.
The term 'adab' appears in the passage implicitly; the heading or context indicates recommendation.
2
List the five acts
Memorize each act: 1) suppress cough, 2) keep mouth shut when yawning, 3) stand when 'Hayya 'ala al-falah' is called, 4) imam begins when 'Qad qamati al-salah' is said, 5) maintain awareness of Allah's greatness.
3
Understand the evidence
Note the phrase 'الحديث' (the hadith) – these adab are based on prophetic practice, but they are not obligations.
The exact hadith is not cited in this passage; it is a reference to the sunna.
4
Apply the category
Know that omitting any adab does not break the prayer; the prayer remains valid and no sin is incurred.
This is key to avoid unnecessary doubt.

The Ruling on Suppressing Cough in Prayer
Ruling on suppressing cough in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on suppressing cough in prayer and explain when a cough invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
Suppressing cough in prayer is sunnah; if two letters are uttered without excuse, the prayer becomes invalid.

In prayer, certain involuntary actions like coughing may inadvertently produce sounds that resemble speech. Hanafi fiqh provides guidance on when such sounds break the prayer and how to avoid invalidation. This lesson examines the ruling regarding suppressing cough and belching during salah, based on the text from Nur al-Idah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the adab
Notice that the text says suppressing cough is 'from the adab' (من الأدب) of prayer. In Hanafi terminology, adab refers to recommended acts (sunnah) that enhance the prayer.
2
Understand the mufsid (corruptor)
The text warns that coughing without excuse may produce letters, like 'ah' (أح), which if two consecutive letters are uttered, the prayer becomes invalid. Identify that producing two distinct letters intentionally or inexcusably breaks the prayer.
This is based on the principle that speaking (كلام) in prayer invalidates it.
3
Apply to cough and belch
Both cough (سعال) and belch (جشاء) are treated similarly. The ruling is that one should suppress them as much as possible, but if unavoidable due to genuine excuse, the prayer remains valid.
The excuse excuses the invalidation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) من الأدب (دَفْعُ السُّعَالِ مَا اسْتَطَاعَ) تحرزاً عن المفسد، لأنه لو كان بغير عذر فسدت صلاته بما يحصل من الحروف، كأح فيحترز ما أمكن، وكذا الجشاء.
And from the adab: suppressing cough as much as possible, as a precaution against the corruptor, because if it is without excuse, his prayer becomes corrupt due to the letters produced, like 'ah', so he takes precaution as much as possible, and similarly belching.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage explains the ruling on suppressing a cough during prayer. It is from the adab (recommended acts) because if one coughs without a valid excuse, the prayer may become invalid if the cough produces distinct letters such as 'ah' (أح). The same applies to belching (جشاء). The precaution is to suppress it as much as possible. However, if one cannot help it due to a genuine excuse, the prayer is not invalidated.

Key Terms
سعال (su'al): Cough; a sound made from the throat.
أدب (adab): Recommended etiquette; a sunnah act in prayer.
مفسد (mufsid): Something that corrupts or invalidates the prayer.
جشاء (jasha'): Belching; the act of releasing gas from the mouth.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Suppressing Yawn in Prayer: Recommended Adab
Proof and ruling on covering mouth during yawn in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on yawning in prayer and apply the recommended action of suppressing it or covering the mouth.

Core Idea
Suppressing a yawn in prayer is recommended; if unable, cover the mouth.

In this passage, the author of Nur al-Idah explains the recommended adab (etiquette) for yawning during prayer, supported by two hadiths that link yawning to shaytan and command suppression. We will examine the ruling, the evidence, and the practical steps to follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is yawning during prayer. The text says it is from adab to keep the mouth shut, indicating a recommended (mustahabb) action. The ruling is not obligation (wajib) because of the nature of the dalil and usul principles.
The imperative form 'فليكظم' is interpreted as recommendation by Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the primary evidence
Two hadith are cited: the first states that yawning in prayer is from shaytan and commands suppression; the second warns that shaytan laughs at the one who yawns openly.
Hadith references: Muslim (2994), Tirmidhi (370), Bukhari (3289), Abu Dawud (5028).
3
Examine the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليكظم' (let him suppress) is a command but understood to indicate recommendation (nadb) rather than obligation (wujub) because it pertains to involuntary actions and prayer adab. The underlying reason (illah) is that yawning is from shaytan, and suppressing it avoids his laughter.
This is consistent with Hanafi principle: al-amr yufidu al-nadb idha qarantahu qarinah.
4
Note the alternative action
If one cannot suppress the yawn, the text instructs to cover the mouth with the hand or sleeve. This is a practical fallback to block the yawn and maintain decorum.
Covering is also recommended, not obligatory.
5
Understand the underlying reason
The hadiths indicate that yawning is from shaytan, and shaytan laughs when one yawns openly. Therefore, suppressing or covering is a way to avoid pleasing shaytan and to maintain focus in prayer.
This does not mean yawning invalidates prayer; it only affects the completeness of adab.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) من الأدب (كَظْمُ فَمِهِ عِنْدَ التَّنَاوُبِ ) فيطبق فمه، فإن لم يقدر غطاه بيده أو كمه؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام ) التثاؤب في الصلاة من الشيطان، فإذا تثاءب أحدكم فليكظـم مـا استطاع » (١) ، ولقوله عليه الصلاة و والسلام: « إِذَا تَشَاءبَ أَحَدُكُمْ فليردَّهُ مَا اسْتَطَاعَ، فَإِنَّ أَحَدَكم إذا تثاءب ضَحِكَ مِنْهُ الشَّيطانُ» (۳).
And from the adab: keeping his mouth shut at the time of yawning. He closes his mouth, and if he cannot, he covers it with his hand or sleeve. Because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'Yawning in prayer is from the shaytan, so when one of you yawns, let him suppress it as much as he can.' And because of his saying, peace be upon him: 'When one of you yawns, let him repel it as much as he can, for when one of you yawns, the shaytan laughs at him.'
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage provides the Islamic ruling on yawning during prayer. It is from the adab to close the mouth when yawning. If one cannot, he should cover it with his hand or sleeve. The evidence is two hadiths: the first states that yawning in prayer is from shaytan and instructs to suppress it; the second warns that shaytan laughs at the one who yawns openly. These hadiths establish the recommended nature of suppressing the yawn.

Key Terms

Standing for Iqamah: Timing for the Congregation
Ruling on when to stand for prayer during the iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on when the congregation should stand during the iqamah and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The congregation should stand when the imam reaches their row—this is the most apparent Hanafi view.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah discusses the recommended etiquette (adab) of standing during the iqamah. While it is not obligatory, multiple narrations exist about the precise moment to stand, especially when the imam is not initially present. Understanding these variants helps a muqtadi align with the sunnah and avoid missing the opening takbir.

Guided Path
1
State the basic Hanafi ruling
When the imam is present near the mihrab, the congregation should stand when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', as it is a command to hasten to prayer.
This is the default when the imam is already in place.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
When the imam is not initially present, there are three narrations: (a) stand in place, (b) stand when the imam mingles with them, (c) each row stands when the imam reaches it.
The third view is preferred (al-azhar).
3
Note the exception for imam giving iqamah
If the imam himself gives the iqamah, the congregation does not stand until he finishes.
But the author notes this may cause missing the simultaneous takbir.
4
Evaluate the practical application
The mufta bihi is: stand when the imam reaches your row, except if the imam gives the iqamah himself, then stand after he finishes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(وَ) من الأدب ( القِيَامُ)، أي: قيام القوم، والإمام إذا كان حاضراً بقرب المحراب ( حينَ قِيلَ ) أي : وقت قول المقيم ( حيَّ عَلَى الفلاح)؛ لأنه أمر به فيستحب المسارعة إليه، وإن لم يكن الإمام حاضراً لا يقومون حتى يصل إليهم. ويقف مكانه في رواية، وفي أخرى يقومون إذا اختلط بهم، وقيل: يقوم كل صف حين ينتهي إليه الإمام وهو الأظهر، وإذا دخل من قدام وقفوا حين يرونه. قال في ( البحر » عن « الظهيرية : هذا إذا كان المؤذن غير الإمام، فإن كان هو وأقام في المسجد، فالقوم لا يقومون حتى يفرغ من إقامته. انتهى. وفيـه تـأمل: لأنـه يـؤدي إلى فوات مقارنة الإحرام بإحرام الإمام.
And from the adab: standing, meaning the people's standing, and the imam if he is present near the mihrab, when it is said, i.e., at the time of the mu'adhdhin's saying 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', because he is commanded with it, so hastening to it is recommended. And if the imam is not present, they do not stand until he reaches them. And in one narration, they stand in their places. In another, they stand when he mingles with them. And it is said: each row stands when the imam reaches it, and that is the most apparent. And if he enters from the front, they stand when they see him. He said in al-Bahr from al-Zahiriyyah: This is when the mu'adhdhin is not the imam; if he is the one and gives the iqamah in the mosque, the people do not stand until he finishes his iqamah. End. But there is contemplation in this, because it leads to missing the simultaneous takbir al-ihram with the imam.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended timing for standing during the iqamah. The basic ruling is that when the mu'adhdhin says 'Hayya 'ala al-falah', the congregation should stand if the imam is present near the mihrab. This is because it is a command, so hastening is recommended. However, there are multiple narrations regarding the exact time when the imam is not initially present: some say they stand in place, others say when the imam mingles with them, and the preferred view is that each row stands when the imam reaches it. Additionally, if the imam himself gives the iqamah, the people do not stand until he finishes. The author notes a potential problem with this last view: it may cause missing the simultaneous takbir with the imam.

Key Terms
إقامة (iqamah): The call to begin prayer, said inside the mosque.
قيام (qiyam): Standing, here referring to the act of standing during the iqamah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) As soon as the iqamah begins
B) When they hear 'Hayya 'ala al-falah'
C) When the imam reaches their row (the most apparent view)
D) When the imam finishes the iqamah

Key Takeaway
The most apparent Hanafi view is that each row stands when the imam reaches it, except when the imam gives the iqamah himself, in which case they stand after he finishes.

Imam's Takbir During Iqamah: A Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam's timing during iqamah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf on when the imam begins the prayer during iqamah, and evaluate the reasoning behind each.

Core Idea
The imam's takbir: at 'Qad qamati' (Abu Hanifa & Muhammad) or after iqamah (Abu Yusuf).

When the mu'adhdhin says 'Qad qamati al-salah' during the iqamah, should the imam immediately begin the prayer? The Hanafi school has an internal difference. This lesson examines the reasoning of the three founding imams and the practical implications for the congregation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
State the views of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad (the two), and Abu Yusuf as presented in the text.
The two: begin at 'Qad qamati'; Abu Yusuf: begin after iqamah.
2
Analyze the proofs of the two
Understand the two's reasoning: the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy, delaying would make his statement false, and the congregation has followed sufficiently.
They also argue that responding to iqamah is not required for the imam's start.
3
Analyze Abu Yusuf's proof
Abu Yusuf argues that starting after iqamah preserves the virtue of responding to the mu'adhdhin and helps him.
He prioritizes the follower's response over the imam's immediate start.
4
Examine the critical responses
Note the author's comments: both reasonings are questioned ('ta'ammul') – the two's 'falsehood' claim is weak because near-term actions are often spoken of as imminent; Abu Yusuf's 'help' claim is weak because he himself prefers following the imam.
The text also cites al-Bahr that responding to iqamah is recommended, and delay is permissible overall.
5
Determine the practical outcome
Conclude that delay is permissible per all three, so the imam has flexibility.
The mufta bihi (operative position) allows delay until after iqamah.

(وَ) من الأدب (شُرُوعُ الإِمَامِ) أي: إحرامه (مُدْ قِيلَ) أي: عنـــد قول المقيم (قَدْ قَامَتِ الصَّلاةُ)، وهذا عندهما، وقال أبو يوسف يشرع إذا فرغ من الإقامة محافظة على فضيلة متابعة المؤذن، أي إجابته، وإعانة للمؤذن على الشروع معه و ، ولهما: أن المؤذن أمين وقد أخبر بقيام الصلاة فيشرع عنده صوناً لكلامه عن الكذب وفيه مسارعة إلى المناجاة، وقد تــابـع المؤذن في الأكثر ، فيقوم مقام الكل على أنهم قالوا المتابعة في الأذان دون الإقامة، كذا قــال الزيلعي، وفي التعليل لأبي يوسف بإعانة المؤذن على الشروع معه تأمل، لأن عنده الأفضل متابعته، لأن مقارنته لإحرام الإمام كما تقدم، وفي تعليله لهما بصون كلامه عن الكذب تأمل أيضاً، لأن ما قرب من الشيء يطلق عليه كقوله : (لقنوا موتاكم (۳) (3) أخرجه مسلم في الجنائز، باب: تلقين الموتى لا إله إلا الله (٩١٦)، والنسائي في الجنائز، باب: تلقين الميت (١٨٢٦). وقوله تعالى: أَتَى أَمْرُ اللَّهِ فَلَا تَسْتَعْجِلُونَ) [النحل: ١] انتهى. وقال صاحب « البحر» في قول الزيلعي: على أنهم قالوا: المتابعة في الأذان دون الإقامة نظر لما قلناه في باب الأذان: إن إجابة الإقامة مستحبة، وفي الظهيرية: ولو أخر حتى يفرغ المؤذن من الإقامة لا بأس به في قولهم جميعاً. انتهى.
And from the adab: the imam's beginning, i.e., his takbir al-ihram, when it is said, i.e., at the mu'adhdhin's saying 'Qad qamati al-salah'. This is according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: he begins when he finishes the iqamah, preserving the virtue of following the mu'adhdhin, i.e., responding to him, and helping the mu'adhdhin to begin with him. And for the two: the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy and has informed of the standing for prayer, so he begins at his saying to safeguard his speech from lying, and in it is haste to communion. And he has followed the mu'adhdhin in the most part, so he takes the place of all. According to them, they said: following is in the adhan, not the iqamah. Thus said al-Zayla'i. And in Abu Yusuf's reasoning of helping the mu'adhdhin to begin with him, there is contemplation, because according to him the best is to follow him, since his accompanying the imam's takbir is as stated. And in his reasoning for the two of safeguarding his speech from lying, there is also contemplation, because what is close to the thing is called by it, as his saying: 'Prompt your dying ones' (Muslim, Nasa'i). And the Almighty's saying: 'The command of Allah has come, so do not seek to hasten it' (Quran 16:1). End. And the author of al-Bahr said regarding al-Zayla'i's statement that they said following is in adhan not iqamah: there is consideration for what we said in the chapter of adhan that responding to the iqamah is recommended. And in al-Zahiriyyah: if he delays until the mu'adhdhin finishes the iqamah, there is no harm in it according to all of them. End.
Source pages p. 285

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute about the exact moment the imam should start the prayer (say takbir al-ihram) during the iqamah. According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (the two), the imam should start when the mu'adhdhin says 'Qad qamati al-salah'. Abu Yusuf holds that the imam should start after the iqamah is completed, to preserve the virtue of responding to the mu'adhdhin and to help him. The reasoning of the two is that the mu'adhdhin is trustworthy and if the imam delays, his report about the prayer being started would be false. They also argue that the congregation has followed the mu'adhdhin for most of the iqamah, so the imam's starting at that point suffices. Al-Zayla'i noted that following applies to adhan, not iqamah. The author of al-Bahr points out that responding to iqamah is actually recommended, and delaying is permissible. The text ultimately notes that delaying is not blameworthy.

Key Terms
متابعة المؤذن (mutaba'at al-mu'adhdhin): Responding to the mu'adhdhin by repeating his words.
تأمل (ta'ammul): Contemplation or critiquing a reasoning as questionable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if the imam delays his takbir until after the iqamah is finished?
A) It is makruh and should be avoided.
B) It is haram because it delays the prayer.
C) There is no harm in it according to all of them.
D) It invalidates the prayer because the imam missed the recommended timing.

Key Takeaway
The imam's timing during iqamah is a matter of adab with flexibility; the default is that delay is permissible.

Weeping in Sujud: Sunnah with Quranic Proof
Ruling that weeping in sujud is sunnah with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of weeping in sujud according to the Hanafi school and explain its Quranic evidence.

Core Idea
Weeping in sujud is sunnah, not fard or wajib, as indicated by Allah's praise in the Quran.

In this short passage from Imdad al-Fattah, the author establishes that weeping during prostration is a recommended act. The ruling is based on a Quranic verse where Allah praises those who fall down prostrating and weeping. This lesson will help you understand the basis for this sunnah and its place in the Hanafi fiqh of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being discussed? What is the hukm (sunnah)?
The act is weeping (buka') during sujud.

What proof is cited? (Quran 19:58)
The verse: 'They fall down in prostration and weeping.'
3

How does this verse indicate the ruling?
Allah praises the act, and praise indicates desirability (nadb) in Hanafi usul.
4

Which sources transmit this ruling? (Jami' al-Nawazil, al-Dirayah)
These are later Hanafi compilations, but the ruling is standard.

6 min
The Manner of Raising Hands and Saying the Opening Takbir
Describes the fiqh of opening takbir with hand positions and proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands during the opening takbir (sunnah muakkadah), describe the proper hand and finger positions for men and women, and apply the principle of necessity adjustments based on the hadith 'do as much as you are able.'

Core Idea
Raising hands to the ears (men) or shoulders (women) is a confirmed sunnah, not wajib, adjusted for necessity.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, presents the Hanafi fiqh of the opening takbir. It details the sunnah manner of raising hands, the correct finger position (nashr, not forced separation), the difference between men and free women, and the ruling for those who cannot fully raise their hands. The author also clarifies a common misunderstanding about the meaning of 'nashr' and provides evidence from the Quran and hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the passage is ruling on: the opening takbir and the raising of hands. Note that the ruling is 'sunnah muakkadah' (confirmed sunnah), not wajib. The author explicitly states 'raising is sunna for every worshipper.'
The 'fasl' heading indicates a new section of related rulings.
2
Note the hand and finger positions
For men: raise hands to ears, thumbs touching earlobes, fingertips at top of ears, palms facing qibla, fingers naturally spread (nashr) — not forced apart or clenched. For free women: raise to shoulders. For female slaves: same as men.
The author rejects the interpretation that 'nashr' means forced separation; it means outstretched but natural.
3
Understand the sunnah status and its proof
The proof includes the Quranic command 'And your Lord magnify' (Al-Muddaththir: 3) and the hadith 'its prohibition is the takbir.' The imperative form in usul indicates obligation, but here it is interpreted as sunnah due to the Prophet's actual practice and the exceptions (women, necessity).
Wisdom behind the sunnah (e.g., informing followers for the imam) is general, not individual.
4
Recognize the exceptions and adjustments
Necessity (e.g., injury, cold) permits raising less than the sunnah amount, even one hand, based on 'do as much as you are able.' If raising to the ears requires exceeding the sunnah (e.g., a cast), raising fully becomes the sunnah for that person.
The principle: 'do as much as you are able' (hadith) overrides the normal position.
5
Apply the principle of 'do as much as you are able'
Test your understanding by considering scenarios: a man with a bandaged arm, a woman in a hijab, or someone in a crowd. Determine the correct sunnah for each.
The ruling adjusts based on ability, not on type of prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل في كيفية تركيب أفعال الصلاة
فصل: هو في اللغة ما بين الشيئين، وفي الاصطلاح طائفة من المسائل الفقهية تغيرت أحكامها بالنسبة إلى ما قبلها، غير مترجمة بالكتاب والباب في كيفية تركيب أفعال الصلاة. ( إذا أَرَادَ الرّجُلُ الدّخول في الصَّلاة أي صلاة كانت أخرجَ كَفَّيْهِ مِنْ كُمَّيْهِ)، بخلاف المرأة وحــال الضرورة كما بيناه، ثمَّ رَفَعَهُما حِدَاءَ أُذُنَيْهِ)، حتى يحاذي بإبهاميه شحمتي أذنيه، وبــرؤوس الأصابع فروع أذنيه، ويجعل باطن كفيه نحو القبلة، وقال « قاضي خان» : ويمس بإبهاميــه شـحمتي أذنيه، وينشر أصابعه، وهو : أن لا يفرجها كل التفريج ولا يضمها، بل يتركها على حالها، وظن البعض فيما روي عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم « أنَّه كَبَّرَ نَاشِرَاً أصابعَهُ ) () أن المراد بالنشر التفريج، وهو غلط، بــل المراد: النشر على طي، يعني: يرفعهما منصوبتين لا مضمومتين، لتكون الأصـابـع مــع الكـف مستقبلة القبلة، كما في ( الدراية ) عن ( مبسوط شيخ الإسلام والمرأة الحرة ترفع حذاء منكبيها على الصحيح، والأمة كالرجل في الرفع، وقدمناه بدليله)، والرفع سنة لكل مصل، وإن كــان مـن حكمته في حق الإمام إعلام المقتدين، لأن الحكمة تراعى في الجنس لا في كل فرد، وما روي مـن أنَّه كَانَ يرفع يديه إلى مَنْكِبَيْهِ ) (۳) فمحمول على حالة العذر، ولهذا إذا لم يمكنه [ الرفع ] إلى الموضع المسنون يرفع قدر ما يمكنه، وإن أمكنه رفع واحدة فقط رفعها لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « إِذا أَمَرْتُكُمْ بِأَمْرِ فَأْتُوا مِنْهُ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ ). وإن لم يمكنه الرفع إلا بالزيادة على المسنون رفعهما، لأنـه المسنون في حقه لعدم استطاعة الامتناع عن الزائد، (ثُمَّ) إذا رفع إلى المحل المسنون (كبر) لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبِّرْ [الملل : ٣] ولما روينا من قوله : ( وتحريمُهَا التَّكبير إلا إذا كان
Chapter on the manner of composing the actions of prayer. Fasl: lexically it means what is between two things; terminologically, it is a group of fiqh rulings whose legal statuses change relative to what precedes, not labeled as kitab or bab, on the manner of composing the actions of prayer. (When a man intends to enter into prayer—whatever prayer it may be—he takes his palms out of his sleeves), contrary to the woman and the state of necessity as we have explained. Then he raises them level with his ears, until his thumbs are parallel to his earlobes and the tips of his fingers are parallel to the upper parts of his ears, and he makes the palms of his hands facing the qibla. Qadi Khan said: He touches his earlobes with his thumbs and spreads his fingers, meaning he does not spread them fully nor clenches them, but leaves them as they are. Some thought, from what is narrated that the Prophet ﷺ said the takbir spreading his fingers, that 'spreading' means separating [the fingers], but this is a mistake. Rather, what is meant is 'spreading' upon folding, i.e., he raises them outstretched, not clenched, so that the fingers together with the palm face the qibla, as in al-Diraya from the Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam. The free woman raises level with her shoulders according to the correct view, and the female slave is like a man in raising, and we have presented it with its proof. Raising is sunna for every person praying, even if its wisdom regarding the imam is to inform the followers, because wisdom is considered generically, not in every individual. What is narrated that he used to raise his hands to his shoulders is interpreted as a case of excuse. Hence, if he cannot raise to the sunna position, he raises as much as he can; and if he can raise only one, he raises it due to his saying ﷺ: 'When I command you with a matter, do as much of it as you are able.' If he can only raise with an increase beyond the sunna, he raises them, because that is the sunna for him due to his inability to abstain from the excess. (Then) after raising to the sunna position, he says the takbir due to His saying: 'And your Lord magnify' [Al-Muddaththir: 3] and because of what we narrated of his saying: 'And its prohibition is the takbir except when...'
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof from Imdad al-Fattah, commenting on Nur al-Idah. It opens by defining the term 'fasl' (section) lexically and terminologically, indicating that this is a distinct set of rulings. The main ruling covers the opening takbir: a man must first remove his hands from his sleeves, then raise them to his ears, with thumbs touching earlobes and fingertips at the top of the ears, palms facing the qibla. The passage clarifies the proper position of fingers: they should be naturally spread (not forced apart nor clenched), contrary to a misunderstanding that 'nashr' means separating the fingers. It cites Qadi Khan to support this. The raising of hands is a sunnah for every worshipper, and the wisdom for the imam (informing followers) does not change the ruling; wisdom is considered generally. For those who cannot raise to the ears due to incapacity or being in a state of necessity (e.g., women in some views), the ruling is adjusted: raise as much as possible, even one hand, based on the hadith 'do as much as you are able.' If raising to the ears requires exceeding the sunna (e.g., for a person with a cast), they still raise because that becomes the sunna for them. The takbir itself is mandated by the Quranic command 'And your Lord magnify.' This passage follows the Hanafi method of presenting the ruling, then its evidence (dalil), and then resolving misunderstandings (like the finger spread).

Key Terms
نَشْر (nashr): Spreading the fingers naturally, neither fully separated nor clenched, as opposed to 'tafriq' (forced separation).
حِذاء (hidha'): Level with; parallel to the ears.
شَحْمَتَا الأُذُن (shahmata al-udhun): The earlobes, the soft lower part of the ear.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) To his shoulders
B) To his ears, with thumbs touching the earlobes
C) To his chest
D) Above his head

Key Takeaway
The opening takbir involves a confirmed sunnah of raising hands to the ears for men (shoulders for free women), with fingers naturally spread, adjusted for necessity based on ability.

Rulings on Raising Hands and Takbir at the Start of Prayer
Commentary on opening prayer actions: ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on raising hands and takbir at the start of prayer, identify the correct sequence, and explain the condition of bila madd.

Core Idea
Raising hands is sunnah muakkadah; takbir is fard with bila madd as a validity condition.

The opening actions of prayer are foundational to its validity. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the sunnah of raising hands, the obligatory takbir, and the critical requirement of pronouncing it without elongation. We'll examine the correct method, the sequence debate within the Hanafi school, and what invalidates the takbir.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opening actions for a man
Determine what a man must do when entering prayer: remove hands from sleeves, raise them opposite ears, then say takbir.
The text specifies these steps in order.
2
Understand the ruling on hand raising
Classify the ruling (sunnah muakkadah) and note the difference for women and slaves.
Wisdom for imam is to inform followers, but ruling applies to all.
3
Analyze the sequence debate
Examine the preferred view (raising first, then takbir) and Abu Yusuf's view (simultaneous). Understand the rationale of negation and affirmation.
Majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad) prefer precedence; al-ashah is the relied view.
4
Apply the condition of bila madd
Explain why elongation invalidates the takbir: it changes meaning to interrogative. Distinguish between elongation of hamza vs ba.
Intentional elongation may lead to disbelief; accidental does not necessarily.
5
Summarize the practical takeaway
Consolidate the correct method and conditions for starting prayer according to the Hanafi school.
This is the mufta bihi position.

رفع واحدة فقط رفعها لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم: « إِذا أَمَرْتُكُمْ بِأَمْرِ فَأْتُوا مِنْهُ مَا اسْتَطَعْتُمْ ). وإن لم يمكنه الرفع إلا بالزيادة على المسنون رفعهما، لأنـه المسنون في حقه لعدم استطاعة الامتناع عن الزائد، (ثُمَّ) إذا رفع إلى المحل المسنون (كبر) لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَرَبَّكَ فَكَبَر﴾ [الملل : ٣] ولما روينا من قوله : ( وتحريمُهَا التَّكبير } إلا إذا كان أخرساً، أو أمياً لا يحسن شيئاً، فإنه يصح شروعهما بالنية فقط لإتيانهما بأقصى ما في وسعهما، وهذا أي: الرفع أولاً، ثم التكبير بعده هو الأصح، وفي ( المبسوط » : وعليه عامة المشايخ، لأن في فعله وقوله معنى النفي والإثبات [ فإنه ] برفع اليدين ينفي الكبرياء عن غير الله تعالى، وبالتكبير يثبته الله تعالى فيكون النفي مقدماً على الإثبات كما في كلمة الشهادة كذا في «معراج الدراية». وقال في مجمع الروايات : رفع اليدين بمنزلة النفي. قال شمس الأئمة « الكردري » رحمه الله : معنى رفع اليدين نبذ ما سوى الله وراء ظهره، فاليد اليمنى كالآخرة، واليسرى كالعاجلة، والله أكبر بمنزلة الإثبات والنفي مقدم على الإثبات كما في كلمة الشهادة انتهى. إلا أن أبا يوسف يقول: يثبت التقدم في كلمة الشهادة ضرورة التكلم ولا ضرورة هنا فيقارن، والأولى أن لا يخلو فعل من أفعال الصلاة عن ذكر فعلى هذا قيل ينبغي أن يكون ابتداء التكبير مع ابتداء الرفع، وانتهاؤه مع انتهاء إرسال اليدين، وذكر البقالي في صلاته » : هذا القول علمائنا جميعاً، ولم يذكــر الخـلاف كذا في ( الدراية ( انتهى قلت: وهذا ظاهر على القول بأن التحريمة من الصلاة، وأما على المذهب فلا إذ لا يكون حالة الصلاة إلا بعد الدخول فيها وهي فيما بعد التحريمة انتهى. وقال الزيلعي لو كبر ولم يرفع يديه حتى فرغ من التكبير لا يأتي به لفوات محله، وإن ذكره في أثناء التكبير رفع، لأنه لم يفت محله انتهى وقوله : ( بِلا مد شرط لصحة التكبير، لما روي أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم « كان لا يتم التكبير » أي: لا يمد. وكان إبراهيم النخعي يقول: التكبير جزم، وروي حذم بالحاء والذال، أي: سريع، فإن مد همزة الجلالة، أو همزة أكبر، لا يكون شارعاً في الصلاة وتفسد به إن فعله في أثنائها، لأنه استفهام، وإن تعمده يكفر للشك في الكبرياء. انتهى. كما في ( التبيين»، وهذا من حيث الظاهر، فإن الهمزة للإنكار وصفاً ولكن من حيث أن الهمزة يجوز أن تكون لتقريره، فلا يلزم الكفر، وما قاله في « الهداية » : أنه خطأ من حيث الدين فهو حسن، كذا في ( الدراية» ، وإن كان في باء أكبر، فقد قيل: تفسد لأنه خطأ من حيث اللغة، لأن أفعل التفضيل لا يحتمل المدَّ لغةً، ولأن إكبار جمع كبر وهــو : الطبل، فيخرج من معنى التكبير، وكان فيه إثبات الشركة. قيل: إكبار اسم الشيطان، وقال بعضهم: لا تفسد لأن الألف واللام نشأت من الإشباع وهذا بعيد، لأن الإشباع لا يجوز إلا في ضرورة
Section on the composition of the actions of prayer. When a man intends to enter prayer, he takes out his palms from his sleeves, then raises them opposite his ears, then says the takbir. Section: On the composition of the actions of prayer. (Section) linguistically: is what is between two things; terminologically: a group of fiqh rulings whose rules change relative to what precedes them, not titled as chapter or book on the composition of the actions of prayer. (When a man intends to enter prayer, any prayer, he takes out his palms from his sleeves), contrary to a woman and in a state of necessity as we explained. Then he raises them opposite his ears, so that his thumbs align with his earlobes, and the tips of his fingers with the tops of his ears, and he makes the inner side of his palms facing the qibla. Qadi Khan said: He touches his earlobes with his thumbs, and spreads his fingers, meaning: he does not spread them fully nor does he clench them, rather he leaves them as they are. Some thought that in the narration from the Prophet (peace be upon him) that 'he said the takbir while spreading his fingers', they understood spreading to mean separating, and this is a mistake. Rather, the meaning is 'spread out' in the sense of being extended, i.e., he raises them stretched out not clenched, so that the fingers along with the palm face the qibla, as in al-Diraya from the Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam. A free woman raises opposite her shoulders according to the correct view, and a slave woman is like a man in raising, and we have presented it with its proof. Raising (the hands) is sunnah for every person praying, even if its wisdom regarding the Imam is to inform the followers, because wisdom is considered for the general case not for every individual. What is narrated that he used to raise his hands to his shoulders is interpreted as being in a state of excuse. For this reason, if he cannot raise to the sunnah position, he raises as much as he can; and if he can raise only one, he raises it due to the Prophet's saying: 'When I command you with a matter, do of it what you are able.' And if he cannot raise except by exceeding the sunnah position, he raises them both, because that is the sunnah for him due to his inability to refrain from the extra. (Then) when he has raised to the sunnah place, he says the takbir due to the saying of Allah: 'And your Lord magnify' (Surah al-Muddaththir: 3) and because of what we narrated from his saying: 'And its prohibition (i.e., the prayer's) is the takbir' except if he is mute or illiterate who knows nothing, then their commencement is valid only by intention because they have done the utmost of what is in their capacity. That is: raising first, then takbir after it, is the most correct. In al-Mabsut: and upon it are the majority of scholars, because in his action and speech there is the meaning of negation and affirmation. By raising hands he negates greatness from other than Allah, and by takbir he affirms it for Allah, so negation precedes affirmation, as in the word of shahada. Likewise in Miraj al-Diraya. And it is said in Majma' al-Riwayat: Raising hands is like negation. Shams al-A'imma al-Kardari said: The meaning of raising hands is discarding everything other than Allah behind his back; the right hand is like the hereafter, the left like the present world; 'Allahu Akbar' is like affirmation, and negation precedes affirmation as in the shahada. End quote. However, Abu Yusuf says: The precedence is established in the shahada out of necessity of speech, and there is no necessity here, so they are simultaneous. The preferable view is that no action of prayer should be devoid of remembrance. Upon this, it is said that the beginning of the takbir should be with the beginning of raising, and its end with the end of lowering the hands. Al-Baqqali mentioned in his Salat: This is the statement of all our scholars, and he did not mention the disagreement. Likewise in al-Diraya. End quote. I say: This is apparent according to the view that the tahrimah is part of prayer, but according to the madhhab, it is not, because the state of prayer is only after entering into it, and it (the takbir) is after the tahrimah. End quote. Al-Zayla'i said: If he says the takbir and does not raise his hands until he has finished the takbir, he does not come with (the raising) because its time has passed. If he remembers during the takbir, he raises, because its time has not passed. End quote. And his saying: (without elongation) is a condition for the validity of the takbir, because it is narrated that the Prophet (peace be upon him) 'would not complete the takbir' meaning he would not elongate. Ibrahim al-Nakha'i used to say: The takbir is with jamming (quickly), and it is narrated 'hadhm' with ha and dhal meaning quick. If he elongates the hamza of the word 'Allah' or the hamza of 'Akbar', he does not become one commencing prayer and it invalidates it if he does it during it, because it becomes an interrogative, and if he does it intentionally he disbelieves due to doubting the greatness (of Allah). End quote, as in al-Tabyin. This is from the apparent perspective, because the hamza is for denial as a description, but from the perspective that the hamza could be for affirmation, disbelief does not necessarily follow. And what is said in al-Hidayah that it is an error from the perspective of religion is good. Likewise in al-Diraya. And if the elongation is in the ba of 'Akbar', it is said it invalidates because it is an error from the language perspective, because the superlative (af'al al-tafdil) does not accept elongation linguistically, and because 'ikbar' is a plural of 'kabr' which is a drum, so it departs from the meaning of takbir, and it involves affirming partnership. It is said: 'Ikbar' is the name of a devil. Some said: It does not invalidate because the alif and lam arise from overstretching, and this is far-fetched because overstretching is not permissible except in necessity.
Source pages p. 287

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, details the sunnah actions for starting the prayer. It is a ruling-with-proof passage. The commentary first explains the meaning of 'fasl' (section), then follows the matn's order: the obligation for a man to remove his hands from sleeves, raise them to the ears, then say takbir. It clarifies that a woman raises to her shoulders, a slave woman like a man. The hand-raising itself is sunnah, not obligatory. The author emphasizes the correct interpretation of 'nashr' (spreading) as extending fingers naturally, not separating them — a common mistake. The commentary then discusses the sequence: raising first, then takbir. It cites the wisdom of negation and affirmation and notes that this is the position of the majority, though Abu Yusuf held they can be simultaneous. The preferred view remains raising first. Finally, it addresses the condition of 'bila madd' (no elongation) for the takbir. Elongating the hamza changes the meaning to an interrogative, invalidating the prayer and potentially causing disbelief. Elongating the ba of 'Akbar' is also problematic. The author discusses the nuances of intentional vs. unintentional elongation. Overall, this passage provides detailed guidance on the opening actions of prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands at the beginning of prayer as a sunnah act
التكبير (al-takbir): Saying 'Allahu Akbar' to commence prayer; it is the tahrimah (prohibition of worldly actions)
بلا مد (bila madd): Without elongation of the vowels; the takbir must be pronounced without lengthening the hamza or other letters
حداء الأذنين (hida' al-udhunain): Opposite the ears; for men, the hands should be level with the earlobes
نشر الأصابع (nashr al-asabi'): Spreading/extending the fingers naturally, not clenched nor fully separated

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, where should a man raise his hands to when starting the prayer?
A) To his shoulders
B) To his chest
C) Opposite his ears (thumbs to earlobes)
D) To his face

Key Takeaway
Raising hands at the start of prayer is a sunnah muakkadah, while the takbir must be performed without elongation; the correct sequence is raising first, then takbir.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Conditions of the Opening Takbir: No Prolongation and Intention
Ruling on conditions of opening takbir with proof from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions of the opening takbir and explain why prolongation invalidates the prayer.

Core Idea
The takbir must be pronounced without prolongation; prolongation changes the meaning and invalidates prayer.

The opening takbir (takbirat al-ihram) is a pillar of prayer, but its validity depends on specific conditions. The two primary conditions are that it be pronounced without prolongation (madd) and with the proper intention (niyyah). Additionally, the preferred order is to raise the hands first before uttering the takbir. This lesson examines these conditions and their proofs from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The opening takbir is a fard (pillar) of prayer. Its validity requires that it be pronounced correctly without prolongation and with intention.
The takbir itself is the act of exalting Allah; the specific wording is not fard but its correctness matters.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith 'The Prophet (peace be upon him) did not complete the takbir' (لم يكن يتم التكبير) is cited to prove that prolongation is not allowed.
This hadith is ahad but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrase 'la yutimmu al-takbir' indicates he did not prolong the pronunciation, implying a stop (jazzm). Prolonging the hamza changes it to an interrogative, invalidating prayer.
Prolonging the ba of 'Akbar' changes it to 'ikbar' (plural of drum), departing from exaltation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars held that prolonging the lam of 'Allah' is permissible, while others disagreed on the ba of 'Akbar'. The relied-upon view is that intentional prolongation that changes meaning invalidates prayer and may lead to disbelief if doubting Allah's majesty.
If done ignorantly, the prayer is invalid but no disbelief.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is that the takbir must be pronounced with a stop without madd. Intention is also a condition. For mute/illiterate persons, intention alone suffices.
The preferred order of raising hands before takbir is the most correct opinion.
