Ruling on Tasmiyah Between al-Fātiḥah and the Sūrah
Intra-Ḥanafī dispute on basmalah between Fātiḥah and sūrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Ḥanafī positions on saying basmalah between al-Fātiḥah and the sūrah and identify the muftā bihī.

Core Idea
Saying basmalah between Fātiḥah and sūrah is ḥasan (recommended) according to Abū Ḥanīfah; the two disciples differ.

This passage clarifies the ruling on tasmiyah (saying Bismillāh) in prayer. While all agree it is sunnah mu’akkadah before al-Fātiḥah, a nuanced disagreement arises about reciting it between al-Fātiḥah and the following sūrah. The text presents the views of Abū Ḥanīfah, Abū Yūsuf, and Muḥammad al-Shaybānī, and explains why later authorities considered it ḥasan (recommended) rather than disliked or obligatory. Understanding this ikhtilāf helps avoid unnecessary rigidity and shows how the madhhab accommodates valid differences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its basic ruling
The act is saying 'Bismillāhir-raḥmānir-raḥīm' in prayer. Determine the agreed-upon ruling before al-Fātiḥah and the disputed ruling between al-Fātiḥah and the surah.
The matn states 'only before al-Fātiḥah', but the commentary expands.
2
Locate the point of disagreement
The dispute is whether to recite basmalah between al-Fātiḥah and the following surah. Note the positions of Abū Ḥanīfah, Abū Yūsuf, and Muḥammad.
3
Analyze each position and its proof
For each imam, identify the ruling they assign and the evidence or reasoning behind it. Abū Ḥanīfah says it is ḥasan; the two say it is not recited aloud; Muḥammad allows it in silent prayers.
The key proof: basmalah is considered a verse of al-Fātiḥah (in one qirā'ah).
4
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah)
What is the effect on the validity of the prayer? Does leaving it require sujūd al-sahw? The text confirms no sujūd al-sahw is required.
The thamarah: saying it is good; omitting it is not sinful.
5
Identify the muftā bihī (relied-upon position)
Later authorities like Ibn al-Humām and al-Ḥalabī preferred Abū Ḥanīfah's view. State why and cite the tarjih mechanism.
The author also refutes the claim that basmalah is only said in the first rak‘ah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ يُسَمِّي سِراً) وقدمنا الكلام عليها، (وَيُسَمِّي) كل من يقرأ في صلاته، (في كُلِّ رَكْعَةٍ سواء كانت صلاة فــرض أو غيره (قبـل الفَاتِحَةِ) بأن يقول: بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم، وأما في الوضوء والذبيحة ونحوهما فلا يتقيد بخصوص البسملة، بل أي ذكر أتى به كفاه، وأشار بقوله (فقط) إلى أنه لا الفاتحة يسمي بين ثم قرأ الفاتحة، وأمَّنَ الإمام والمأموم سراً، ثم قرأ سورةً، أو ثلاث آيات، ثم كبر راكعاً، مطمئناً، مسوياً رأسَهُ بعجزه أحداً رَكْبَتَيْهِ بيديهِ، مُفرجاً أصابعه، وسبح فيه ثلاثاً، وذلك أدناه ثم رفع رأسه، واطمأن قائلاً: سمِعَ اللهُ لِمَن حَمِدَهُ. والسورة مطلقاً، وهذا عندهما وقال محمد: يسمي . إذا خافت لا إن جهر، لئلا يلزم الإخفاء بين الجهرين، وهو شنيع كذا قاله الزيلعي، والخلاف في السنية، وأما عدم الكراهة فمتفق عليه، ولهذا صرح في « الذخيرة وغيرها بأنه إن سمى بين الفاتحة والسورة كان حسناً عند أبي حنيفة، سواء كانت السورة مقروءة جهراً أو سراً، ورجحه المحقق ابن الهمام وتلميذه الحلبي، لشبهة الاختلاف في كونها آية من الفاتحة، وما في القنية من أنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها بين الفاتحة والســورة فبعيد جداً. كما أنَّ قول من قال: لا يسمي إلا في الركعة الأولى قول غير صحيح، بـل قـال الزاهدي: إنه غلط عن أصحابنا غلطاً فاحشاً
Then he says the basmalah silently, and we have already discussed it. And everyone who recites in his prayer says the basmalah in every rak'ah, whether the prayer is obligatory or otherwise, before the Fatiha, by saying: Bismillāhir-raḥmānir-raḥīm. As for in wuḍū', slaughter, and the like, it is not restricted to specifically the basmalah, rather any dhikr he comes with suffices. And he indicated by his saying 'only' that he does not say basmalah between the Fatiha and the surah. Then he recited al-Fātiḥah, and the imam and the follower said Āmīn silently, then he recited a surah, or three verses, then he said takbīr while bowing, with tranquility, making his head level with his back, taking his knees with his hands, spreading his fingers, and glorified in it three times, and that is the minimum. Then he raised his head and stood up saying: Sami'a Allāhu liman ḥamidah. And the surah absolutely, and this is according to the two (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad), and Muḥammad said: he says the basmalah, if he recites silently, not if aloud, lest there be concealment between two loud recitations, and it is repugnant. Thus said al-Zayla'ī. And the difference is in its being sunnah. As for the absence of karāhah, it is agreed upon. Therefore it is stated in al-Dhakhīrah and others that if he says basmalah between the Fatiha and the surah, it is good according to Abū Ḥanīfah, whether the surah is recited loudly or silently. Al-Muḥaqqiq Ibn al-Humām and his student al-Ḥalabī gave preponderance to this, due to the doubt regarding its being a verse of al-Fātiḥah. And what is in al-Qunyah that sijdah al-sahw is required for leaving it between the Fātiḥah and the surah is very far-fetched. Similarly, the statement of those who say: he only says basmalah in the first rak'ah is an incorrect statement, rather al-Zāhidī said: it is a clear error from our companions.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling of tasmiyah (saying 'Bismillāh') in prayer. The author first reiterates the general rule: one says the basmalah before al-Fātiḥah in every rak'ah, silently, in both obligatory and supererogatory prayers. However, he notes that in other acts like wuḍū' and slaughter, any dhikr suffices, not specifically the basmalah. The text then shifts to a detailed intra-Ḥanafī dispute about saying basmalah between al-Fātiḥah and the surah. The matn (as indicated by 'fī kulli rak'ah ... qabla al-fātiḥah') implies it is only before Fātiḥah. But the commentary explains that according to Abū Ḥanīfah, it is recommended (ḥasan) to say basmalah between Fātiḥah and the surah as well, because basmalah is considered a verse of al-Fātiḥah (in one reading). The two students (Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad) hold that it is not said aloud in loud prayers to avoid a break between two loud recitations. Muḥammad has a further nuance: he allows it in silent prayers but not loud. The overall consensus is that it is not makrūh, but the sunnah status differs. Later authorities like Ibn al-Humām and al-Ḥalabī preferred Abū Ḥanīfah's view. The author strongly refutes the opinion that basmalah is only in the first rak'ah, calling it a grievous error.

Key Terms
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): Saying 'Bismillāhir-raḥmānir-raḥīm'.
الحسن (al-ḥasan): Recommended but not emphasized; between sunnah and mubāḥ.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abū Ḥanīfah, what is the ruling on saying basmalah between al-Fātiḥah and the surah?
A) Wājib, and leaving it requires sujūd al-sahw
B) Makrūh taḥrīmī
C) Ḥasan (recommended), whether the prayer is loud or silent
D) Only allowed in the first rak'ah

Key Takeaway
Saying basmalah between al-Fātiḥah and the surah is ḥasan (recommended) in the Ḥanafī school, following Abū Ḥanīfah, and no sujūd al-sahw is required if omitted.

Recitation After Tasmiyah: Obligation of Sūrah and Consequences
Rulings on recitation after tasmiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rulings for recitation after tasmiyah in Hanafi salah, including the obligatory status of sūrah/three verses, the consequences of intentional and forgetful omission, and the distinction between tahrīmī and tanzīhī karāhah.

Core Idea
Reciting a sūrah or three verses after Fātiḥah is wājib; leaving it intentionally invalidates the prayer, forgetfully requires sujūd al-sahw.

In the Hanafi school, recitation after tasmiyah follows a precise structure: Fātiḥah is recited, then Āmīn is said silently, and then a sūrah or equivalent verses are recited. This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ clarifies the obligatory nature of the sūrah recitation, the consequences of omission, and a subtle intra-Hanafi disagreement. Understanding these details ensures your salah is valid and free from deficiency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligatory recitation after Fātiḥah
The passage states that after Fātiḥah, one recites a sūrah or three verses (short or one long verse). This recitation is wājib (obligatory) in the first two rak'ahs of fard prayers and in all rak'ahs of other prayers.
The ruling is derived from the matn's phrase 'ثم قرأ سورة' and the commentary's emphasis on wujūb.
2
Determine the consequences of omission
Forgetful omission requires sujūd al-sahw. Intentional omission requires repeating the prayer (i'ādah). This applies whether the omission is of Fātiḥah or the sūrah, as both are wājib.
The text explicitly states: 'fayusjadu lil-sahw bi-tarkihā sāhiyan' and 'yu'maru bi-i'ādat al-salāh bi-tarkihā 'amdan'.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute with al-Zayla'ī
Al-Zayla'ī held that i'ādah is required only for leaving Fātiḥah, not for leaving the sūrah. The author rejects this, affirming that both are wājib and intentional omission of either requires repetition.
The author calls al-Zayla'ī's view 'غير متبع' (not followed).
4
Understand the concept of ākadiyyah (emphasis)
Ākadiyyah refers to the strength of obligation. Although both Fātiḥah and sūrah are wājib, the emphasis differs: omission of Fātiḥah incurs greater sin. However, the ruling of i'ādah is the same for any wājib omitted intentionally.
The text explains that ākadiyyah affects sin, not the need for repetition.
5
Distinguish tahrīmī and tanzīhī karāhah
Reciting only the obligatory minimum (sūrah or three verses) removes tahrīmī karāhah. Reciting additional sunnah recitation also removes tanzīhī karāhah. If one recites less than the obligatory, he commits tahrīmī karāhah; if he recites the obligatory but not the sunnah, he commits only tanzīhī karāhah.
The text clarifies the difference between the two levels of karāhah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قرأ الفاتحة إلا أن يكون مقتدياً، إذ لا قراءة له، (وَ) إذا قال الإمام ولا الضالين أمنَ الإمام والمأموم، سراً وتقدم الكلام عليه )، (ثم قرأ سورة)، وتقدم تفصيلها من المفصل) ، (أو) قرأ ثلاث آيات) ، قصاراً أو آية طويلة وجوباً فيسجد للسهو بتركها ساهياً، ويؤمر بإعادة الصلاة بتركها عمداً، وقول الزيلعي يؤمر بالإعادة لترك الفاتحة دون السورة غير متبع والآكدية لا تظهر إلا في الإثم، لأنه مقول بالتشكيك لا في الإعادة وعدمها، لأن الإعادة حكم ترك الواجب مطلقاً لا الواجب المتأكد، وإذا قرأ الواجب خرج عن كراهة التحريم، وإن قرأ المسنون خرج عن كراهة التنزيه أيضاً، وإلا فقد ارتكبها فمن قال: يخرج عن الكراهة إذا قرأ الواجب أراد التحريمية، ومن قال: لا يخرج عنها أراد التنزيهية
Then he recited al-Fātiḥah, unless he is a muqtadī (follower), for he has no recitation. And when the imam says 'and not the astray', the imam and the follower say Āmīn silently, and discussion on it has preceded. Then he recited a sūrah, and its details have preceded from al-Mufaṣṣal. Or he recited three verses, short or one long verse, and it is obligatory, so he performs sujūd al-sahw for leaving it forgetfully, and he is ordered to repeat the prayer for leaving it intentionally. And the statement of al-Zayla'ī that he is ordered to repeat for leaving al-Fātiḥah but not for the sūrah is not followed. And the emphasis (ākadiyyah) is only apparent in sin, because it is said with tashkīk not in repetition and its lack, because repetition is the ruling of leaving an obligatory act absolutely, not the emphasized obligatory. And if one recites the obligatory, he leaves the tahrīmī karāhah, and if one recites the sunnah, he also leaves the tanzīhī karāhah, otherwise he has committed it. So whoever says: he leaves the karāhah if he recites the obligatory means the tahrīmī, and whoever says: he does not leave it means the tanzīhī.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage details the recitation after tasmiyah. The matn states: 'Then he recited al-Fātiḥah' with the exception of a muqtadī (follower) who does not recite behind the imam. Then 'and when the imam says 'walā al-ḍāllīn', the imam and follower say Āmīn silently'. Then 'then he recited a sūrah' or 'three verses' (short or one long verse). The commentary clarifies that reciting a sūrah or equivalent is wājib in every rak'ah after Fātiḥah. Leaving it forgetfully requires sujūd al-sahw; leaving it intentionally requires repeating the prayer. The author then addresses a nuance from al-Zayla'ī, who distinguished between leaving Fātiḥah (which requires repeat) and leaving sūrah (which does not). The author rejects this, arguing that both are wājib, and the ruling of repetition applies to leaving any wājib intentionally. However, there is a degree of emphasis: the 'ākadiyyah' (emphasis) of wujūb for sūrah is less than for Fātiḥah, but this only affects sin, not the ruling of repetition. The discussion on karāhah explains that if one recites the obligatory (i.e., the minimum sūrah), he avoids tahrīmī karāhah (disliked prohibition), and if he recites the sunnah amount, he also avoids tanzīhī karāhah (disliked offensiveness).

Key Terms
الآكدية (al-ākadiyyah): The degree of emphasis of an obligation; a stronger wājib carries greater sin for omission but same ruling of i'ādah.
كراهة التحريم (karāhah al-taḥrīm): Disliked prohibition, close to ḥarām, but not as strong; usually requires i'ādah if done in prayer.
سجود السهو (sujūd al-sahw): Prostration of forgetfulness, required when a wajib is omitted or an extra act is added unintentionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on leaving the recitation of a sūrah after al-Fātiḥah forgetfully in a rak'ah where recitation is required?
A) No compensation needed
B) Sujūd al-sahw is required
C) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated
D) One must recite it after the prayer

Key Takeaway
Reciting a sūrah or three verses after Fātiḥah is wājib; intentional omission invalidates the prayer, while forgetful omission requires sujūd al-sahw.

Rukū' and Its Rulings: Takbīr, Posture, Tasbīh, and Standing
Details the sequence and rulings of rukū' actions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the pillars, wajibat, and sunan of rukū' according to the Hanafi school, and apply the rulings on takbīr, tranquility, tasbīh, and the prohibition of Quran recitation.

Core Idea
Rukū' has a specific posture and dhikr; tranquility (ṭuma'nīnah) is a pillar, and reciting Quran is forbidden while bowing.

The prayer is a structured act of worship, and each posture has precise requirements. The matn of Nur al-Idah details the actions of rukū', from the opening takbīr to the return to standing. This lesson unpacks those details, clarifying what is a pillar (rukn), what is obligatory (wajib), and what is a sunnah, so that your rukū' is legally sound and spiritually complete.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sequence of Rukū' Actions
Read the passage and list the actions in order: takbīr, bowing posture, tranquility, tasbīh, and rising. Note which actions are explicitly mentioned and which are implied.
The passage follows the natural sequence of performance.
2
Classify Each Action's Ruling Level
For each action, determine whether it is a rukn (pillar), wajib (obligatory), sunnah, or makruh. Use the text's descriptions and the hadith to support your classification.
Pay special attention to tranquility (ṭuma'nīnah) as a rukn, and the tasbīh as a sunnah (with a minimal recommended number).
3
Analyze the Gender Difference in Posture
The passage restricts 'spreading fingers' to men. Identify the gender-specific rule and understand why it differs for women (previously mentioned in the text).
Women are instructed to keep fingers together, reflecting modesty.
4
Examine the Prohibition of Quran Recitation
The hadith prohibits Quran recitation in rukū'. Classify this ruling using the consensus of the four imams. Note the dalil and its epistemological weight (zanni al-thubut but qat'i al-dalala).
The prohibition is considered makruh tahrimi by some, but the text says 'makruh' by consensus.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم كبر كل مصل راكعاً فيبتدئ مع ابتداء الانحناء ويختمه بختمة، ليشرع في التسبيح، فلا تخلو حالة من حالات الصلاة عن ذكر مطمئناً، مسوياً رأسَهُ بعجزه، آخذاً رُكْبَتَيْهِ بيديهِ، ويكون الرجل مفرجاً أصابعه ناصباً ساقيه، وإحناؤهما شبه القوس مكروه عند أهل العلم، كما في ( الدراية ). وقيدنا بالرجل، لأن المرأة لا تفرج أصابعها كما تقدم، وسبَّحَ فِيهِ، أي: الركوع كل مصل فيقول: سبحان ربي العظيــم مــرات ثلاثاً، وَذَلِكَ العدد أدْنَاهُ، أي: أدنى كمال الجمع المسنون كما قدمناه، ويكــــره قـراءة القرآن في الركوع والسجود والتشهد بإجماع الأئمة الأربعة، لقوله عليه السلام: « نُهِيتُ أَنْ أَقْرَأ الْقُرْآنَ رَاكِعا أوْ سَاجِدًا ) رواه مسلم ( ثم) رفعَ رَأْسَه وَاطْمَأَنَّ قائماً قائلاً: سَمِعَ اللهُ لِمَن حَمِدَهُ)، أي: بالتكرير
Then every person praying says takbīr while bowing, so he begins with the beginning of inclining and ends it with a completion, to start the glorification. So no state of the prayer is devoid of dhikr. With tranquility, making his head level with his back, taking his knees with his hands. And for the man, he spreads his fingers, straightens his shins, and bending them like a bow is disliked (makrūh) according to the people of knowledge, as in al-Dirāyah. And we restricted it to the man, because the woman does not spread her fingers as previously mentioned. And he glorifies in it (i.e., in rukū'), every person praying says: Subḥāna rabbiya al-'aẓīm three times, and that number is the minimum, i.e., the minimum of the recommended completion as we have mentioned. And reciting the Quran in rukū' and sujūd and tashahhud is disliked (makrūh) by the consensus of the four imams, due to his saying: 'I was forbidden to recite the Quran while bowing or prostrating' narrated by Muslim. Then he raised his head and stood up saying: Sami'a Allāhu liman ḥamidah, i.e., with repetition.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage describes the actions of rukū' in detail. The matn states: 'Then he says takbīr while bowing' – the commentary explains that the takbīr for rukū' should accompany the movement, starting as one begins to bow and ending when one is settled. The posture of rukū' includes: tranquility (ṭuma'nīnah), leveling the head with the back, placing hands on knees with fingers spread (for men), and keeping shins straight (not bending the knees). Bending the knees like a bow is makrūh. The minimum tasbīh in rukū' is saying 'Subḥāna rabbiya al-'aẓīm' three times, which is the minimal recommended completion. Reciting Quran in rukū' (or sujūd or tashahhud) is makrūh by consensus, based on the hadith from Muslim: 'I was forbidden to recite the Quran while bowing or prostrating.' After rukū', one raises the head and stands with tranquility, saying 'Sami'a Allāhu liman ḥamidah', which may be repeated.

Key Terms
الطمأنينة (al-ṭuma'nīnah): To pause and be still for at least the duration of saying 'Subḥānallāh' in rukū' and sujūd, and between movements.
التسبيح (al-tasbīh): Saying 'Subḥāna rabbiya al-'aẓīm' in rukū' and 'Subḥāna rabbiya al-a'lā' in sujūd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Proper rukū' requires tranquility as a pillar, the recommended tasbīh three times, and reciting Quran is prohibited; gender differences in hand positioning apply.

The Recitation After Al-Fatiha: Obligation of Surah and the Basmalah Dispute
Expanded commentary on the requirements of recitation after Fatiha.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on reciting a surah after Al-Fatiha, identify the conditions for its obligation, and explain the Hanafi dispute on the basmalah.

Core Idea
Reciting a surah after Al-Fatiha is wajib; omitting it intentionally invalidates the prayer.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah clarifies the rulings on the recitation that follows Al-Fatiha in prayer. It establishes that reciting a surah or three verses is a wajib (obligatory) act for the imam and the one praying alone, while the follower is exempt from all recitation. The passage also delves into the intra-Hanafi disagreement over saying the basmalah between Al-Fatiha and the surah, weighing the different positions and providing the relied-upon view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is reciting a surah (or three verses) after Al-Fatiha. According to the text, this is wajib for the imam and the one praying alone (munfarid).
The follower does not recite.
2
Note the exception for the follower
The text explicitly states that the follower has no recitation (la qira'ata lahu), based on the Quranic verse 'When the Quran is recited, listen to it.'
3
Understand the consequence of omission
Forgetful omission of the surah requires sajda sahw; intentional omission requires repeating the prayer. The text corrects al-Zayla'i's view that only omission of Fatiha requires repetition.
The ruling is based on the principle that omission of any wajib invalidates the prayer if intentional.
4
Recognize the dispute on the basmalah
Three Hanafi positions: Abu Hanifa holds it is hasan (good) but not obligatory; Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it sunnah; Muhammad restricts it to silent prayers. All agree it is not disliked.
The dispute is over its sunniyyah, not its permissibility.
5
Know the mufta bihi
The relied-upon view is that reciting basmalah between Fatiha and surah is sunnah (recommended), not wajib. The commentator rejects the notion that omitting it requires sajda sahw.
Ibn al-Humam and al-Halabi preferred Abu Hanifa's view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم قرأ الفاتحة، وأمَّنَ الإمام والمأموم سراً، ثم قرأ سورةً، أو ثلاث آيات، ثم كبر راكعاً، مطمئناً، مسوياً رأسَهُ بعجزه أحداً رَكْبَتَيْهِ بيديهِ، مُفرجاً أصابعه، وسبح فيه ثلاثاً، وذلك أدناه ثم رفع رأسه، واطمأن قائلاً: سمعَ اللهُ لِمَن حَمِدَهُ.
والسورة مطلقاً، وهذا عندهما وقال محمد: يسمي . إذا خافت لا إن جهر، لئلا يلزم الإخفاء بين الجهرين، وهو شنيع كذا قاله الزيلعي، والخلاف في السنية، وأما عدم الكراهة فمتفق عليه، ولهذا صرح في « الذخيرة وغيرها بأنه إن سمى بين الفاتحة والسورة كان حسناً عند أبي حنيفة، سواء كانت السورة مقروءة جهراً أو سراً، ورجحه المحقق ابن الهمام وتلميذه الحلبي، لشبهة الاختلاف في كونها آية من الفاتحة، وما في القنية من أنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها بين الفاتحة والســورة فبعيد جداً. كما أنَّ قول من قال: لا يسمي إلا في الركعة الأولى قول غير صحيح، بـل قـال الزاهدي: إنه غلط عن أصحابنا غلطاً فاحشاً، ثم قرأ الفاتحة إلا أن يكون مقتدياً، إذ لا قراءة له، (وَ) إذا قال الإمام ولا الضالين أمنَ) الإمام والمأموم، سراً) وتقدم الكلام عليه ) ، (ثم قرأ سورة)، وتقدم تفصيلها من المفصل) ، (أو) قرأ ثلاث آيات) ، قصاراً أو آية طويلة وجوباً فيسجد للسهو بتركها ساهياً، ويؤمر بإعادة الصلاة بتركها عمداً ، وقول الزيلعي يؤمر بالإعادة لترك الفاتحة دون السورة غير متبع والآكدية لا تظهر إلا في الإثم، لأنه مقول بالتشكيك لا في الإعادة وعدمها، لأن الإعادة حكم ترك الواجب مطلقاً لا الواجب المتأكد، وإذا قرأ الواجب خرج عن كراهة التحريم، وإن قرأ المسنون خرج عن كراهة التنزيه أيضاً، وإلا فقد ارتكبها فمن قال: يخرج عن الكراهة إذا قرأ الواجب أراد التحريمية، ومن قال: لا يخرج عنها أراد التنزيهية
( ثم كبر ) كل مصل (رَاكِعَا) فيبتدئ مع ابتداء الانحناء ويختمه بختمة، ليشرع في التسبيح، فلا تخلو حالة من حالات الصلاة عن ذكر (مطمئناً، مسوياً رأسَهُ بعجزه، آخذاً رُكْبَتَيْهِ بيديهِ)، ويكون الرجل (مفرجاً أصابعه) ناصباً ساقيه، وإحناؤهما شبه القوس مكروه عند أهل العلم، كما في ( الدراية » . وقيدنا بالرجل، لأن المرأة لا تفرج أصابعها كما تقدم، وسبَّحَ فِيهِ)، أي: الركوع كل مصل فيقول: سبحان ربي العظيــم مــرات (ثَلاثاً، وَذَلِكَ) العدد (أدْنَاهُ)، أي: أدنى كمال الجمع المسنون كما قدمناه ، ويكــــره قـراءة القرآن في الركوع والسجود والتشهد بإجماع الأئمة الأربعة، لقوله عليه السلام: « نُهِيتُ أَنْ أَقْرَأ الْقُرْآنَ رَاكِعا أوْ سَاجِدًا ) رواه مسلم
ثم رفعَ رَأْسَه وَاطْمَأَنَّ قائماً قائلاً: سَمِعَ اللهُ لِمَن حَمِدَهُ)، أي: رَبَّنَا لك الحمد، لو إماماً.. قبل الله حمد من حمده، قال في « الدراية » : السماع يُذكر ويراد به القبول مجازاً، كما يقال: سمع الأمير كلام فلان إذا قبله، ويقال: ما سمع كلامه أي: ردَّه ولم يقبله، وإن سمعه حقيقة، وفي الحديث: أعوذُ بِكَ مِنْ دُعَاء لا يُسْمَعُ ) (أي: لا يستجاب، وفي « الفوائد الحميدية : الهـاء فـي حـمـده للسكتة والاستراحة، لا للكناية) ، كذا نقل عن الثقات، وفي المستصفى : واللام لعود المنفعة، والهاء للكناية لا للاستراحة، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاشْكُرُوا لَه (سبا: ١٥] (رَبَّنَا لَكَ الحَمْدُ) فيجمع بين التسميع والتحميد (لو) كان ( إمَاماً ) ، هذا قولهما وهو رواية عن الإمام، والظاهر عنه أن الإمام يكتفي بالتسميع، وعليه مشى صاحب «الكنز» بقوله : واكتفى الإمام بالتسميع، والمؤتم والمنفرد بالتحميد، لقوله : « إِذَا قَالَ الإِمَامُ: سَمِعَ اللهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ فَقُولُوا: رَبَّنَا لَكَ الْحَمْدُ، يَسْمَع ا لَكُمْ» (۳) رواه مسلم وأبو داود وابن ماجه، والنسائي، والطحاوي، لأن ظاهر الحديث يقتضي القسمة وأنها تنافي الشركة، ووجه قولهمـا وهـو رواية عن الإمام، واختارها في « الحاوي القدسي»، وفي « الدراية»، عن « الظهيرية » ، كان الفضلي، والطحاوي، وجماعة من المتأخرين، يميلون إلى قولهما، وهو قول أهل المدينة، فاختاروا قولهما الموافق لتلك الرواية عن الإمام فاتبعناها، وقلنا: إن الإمام يجمع بينهما لقول أبي هريرة : (كان رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حينَ يفرغ مِنَ صَلَاةِ الفَجْرِ مِنَ القِرَاءَةِ يُكَبِّر
الله
ويَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنَ الرُّكُوعِ ويقول: سَمِعَ اللَّهَ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ رَبَّنَا وَلَكَ الحَمْدُ اللَّهمَّ أَنْجِ الوَلِيدَ بنَ الوَلِيـدِ... الحديث وقوله : « أنا أشبهكُم صَلاةٌ برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكانَ إِذَا قَالَ: سَمِعَ اللَّهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ، قال: اللَّهُمَّ رَبَّنَا لَكَ الحَمْدُ ). وقول عائشة : « خُسِفَت الشَّمْسُ في حياةِ رسولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَصَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ، فَلَمَّا
Then he recited Al-Fatiha, and the imam and follower said Ameen silently, then he recited a surah or three verses, then he said Allahu Akbar while bowing, with tranquility, making his head level with his back, grasping his knees with his hands, spreading his fingers, and he glorified (Subhanallah) three times, and that is the minimum. Then he raised his head and stood with tranquility saying: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah.' And the surah absolutely, and this according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Muhammad said: he says the basmalah. If he is praying silently, not if aloud, to avoid hiding between two loud recitations, which is ugly, as said by al-Zayla'i. The dispute is over its being sunnah, but the absence of dislike is agreed upon. Hence it is stated in al-Dhakhira and others that if he recites the basmalah between Al-Fatiha and the surah, it is good according to Abu Hanifa, whether the surah is recited aloud or silently, and the verifying scholar Ibn al-Humam and his student al-Halabi preferred it due to the dispute over whether it is a verse of Al-Fatiha. What is in al-Qunyah that requires sajda sahw for omitting it between Fatiha and surah is very far-fetched. Likewise, the statement of one who says he should not say basmalah except in the first rak'ah is incorrect; rather al-Zahidi said it is a glaring mistake from our companions. Then he recited Al-Fatiha unless he is a follower, for there is no recitation for him. And when the imam says 'ghayri al-maghdubi 'alayhim', the imam and follower say Ameen silently, and the discussion has preceded. Then he recited a surah, and its details from al-Mufassal have preceded, or read three verses, short ones, or one long verse, as an obligation. So he does sajda sahw for omitting it forgetfully, and he is commanded to repeat the prayer if he omits it intentionally. Al-Zayla'i's statement that he is commanded to repeat for omitting Fatiha but not the surah is not followed. The emphasis appears only in sin, not in repetition or its lack, because repetition is the ruling for abandoning an obligatory act absolutely, not the highly emphasized obligatory act. If one recites the obligatory, he leaves the prohibition of tahrime, and if he recites the sunnah, he leaves the prohibition of tanzih as well; otherwise he has committed it. So whoever says he leaves prohibition when reciting the obligatory meant the tahrime, and whoever says he does not leave prohibition meant the tanzihi. Then every worshipper says Takbir while bowing; he begins with the start of bending and ends with its completion so as to begin the tasbih; no state of prayer is empty of dhikr. With tranquility, leveling his head with his back, taking his knees with his hands. The man spreads his fingers, straightening his legs; bending them like a bow is disliked according to the scholars, as in al-Diraya. We specified the man because the woman does not spread her fingers as mentioned. And he glorifies in it, i.e., in bowing, every worshipper says: 'Subhana Rabbi al-'Azeem' three times, and that number is its minimum, i.e., the minimum perfection of the recommended. Reciting the Quran during bowing, prostration, and tashahhud is disliked by consensus of the four imams, because of his saying: 'I have been forbidden to recite the Quran while bowing or prostrating' narrated by Muslim. Then he raised his head and stood with tranquility saying: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', i.e., 'Rabbana laka al-hamd', if he is an imam... 'Qabala Allahu hamda man hamidah'. He said in al-Diraya: 'Sami'a' is used figuratively to mean acceptance, as it is said: 'The amir heard the speech of so-and-so' if he accepted it, and it is said: 'He did not hear his speech' meaning he rejected it, even if he heard it literally. In the hadith: 'I seek refuge with You from a supplication that is not heard', meaning not answered. In al-Fawa'id al-Hamidiyya: the ha in hamidah is for pause and rest, not for pronoun. This is transmitted from reliable authorities. In al-Mustasfa: the lam is for benefit and the ha is a pronoun, not for rest, as in the verse 'wa ishkuru lahu'. (Rabbana laka al-hamd) so he combines tasmi' and tahmid if he is an imam. This is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and a narration from Abu Hanifa. The apparent view from him is that the imam suffices with tasmi', and the author of al-Kanz followed him, saying: the imam suffices with tasmi', and the follower and individual with tahmid, because of his saying: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, say Rabbana laka al-hamd, Allah will hear you' narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, and al-Tahawi. Because the apparent meaning of the hadith entails division and precludes joint performance. The proof of the two (and the narration from Abu Hanifa) is selected by al-Hawi al-Qudsi and in al-Diraya from al-Zahiriyya. Al-Fadli, al-Tahawi, and a group of later scholars inclined to their view, which is the view of the people of Medina. So they chose their view, which agrees with that narration from Abu Hanifa, and we followed it. We say the imam combines both because of the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'When the Messenger of Allah finished the recitation of the Fajr prayer, he would say Takbir and raise his head from bowing and say: Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana wa laka al-hamd, O Allah, save al-Walid ibn al-Walid...' and his saying: 'I am the one among you whose prayer most resembles that of the Messenger of Allah. When he said Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, he said: Allahumma Rabbana laka al-hamd.' And the saying of Aisha: 'The sun eclipsed in the lifetime of the Messenger of Allah, and he prayed with the people. When'
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah. It covers the actions of the prayer from the recitation after Al-Fatiha through the tasmi' after bowing, and includes several important subsidiary rulings and intra-Hanafi disputes. The author first presents the matn describing the sequence: the imam and follower say Ameen silently, then the imam recites a surah or three verses (obligatory for imam and individual, not for follower). He then comments on the basmalah between Fatiha and surah, presenting the three Hanafi positions: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, basmalah is recited absolutely; Muhammad adds that if praying aloud, it is not recited to avoid inconsistency; Abu Hanifa's view is that it is not obligatory but recommended. The dispute is over its sunniyyah (whether it is sunnah), not over its permissibility—all agree it is not disliked. The commentator refutes the view that sajda sahw is required for omitting it, calling that very far-fetched, and rejects the opinion that basmalah is only said in the first rak'ah, calling it a glaring mistake. Next, he discusses the ruling for the follower: no recitation at all behind the imam (a Hanafi position). Then the obligation of reciting a surah or three verses after Fatiha: this is wajib (obligatory) such that omitting it forgetfully requires sajda sahw, and omitting it intentionally means the prayer must be repeated. He corrects al-Zayla'i's statement that only omission of Fatiha requires repetition, not the surah, stressing that the obligation of the surah is established even if not emphasized. Then he moves to the takbir for bowing, describing the recommended posture: the man spreads his fingers, straightens his legs, and the woman does not spread fingers. The tasbih in ruku' is sunnah, and the minimum for perfection is three. Reciting the Quran in ruku' or sujud is makruh (disliked) by consensus, with a hadith from Muslim as evidence. Finally, the most detailed discussion is on the tasmi' and tahmid (saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana laka al-hamd') when rising from bowing. The dispute is between Abu Hanifa (apparent view) and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on whether the imam should say both or only tasmi'. The commentator notes that the Sahibayn' view is supported by a narration from Abu Hanifa and is preferred by many later scholars, including the author of al-Kanz, and he adopts it. Multiple hadith are adduced: the hadith ordering the follower to say tahmid when the imam says tasmi' (which suggests division, but the Sahibayn interpret it to allow combination), the practice of the Prophet reported by Abu Huraira and others combining both, and the practice of companions. The reliance on the Sahibayn' view is explained as considering the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position, though the individual worshipper (munfarid) says only tahmid.

Key Terms
الفاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, obligatory to recite in every rak'ah of prayer.
التسمية (al-tasmiyah): The recitation of 'Bismillah al-Rahman al-Rahim' between Al-Fatiha and a surah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling for the imam and the one praying alone regarding reciting a surah after Al-Fatiha?
A) It is sunnah mu'akkadah
B) It is wajib
C) It is fard
D) It is optional (mubah)

Key Takeaway
Reciting a surah after Al-Fatiha is wajib for the imam and the one praying alone; its intentional omission requires repetition, and the basmalah between them is sunnah, not wajib.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
Ruku' and Tasmi': Posture, Tasbih, and the Imam's Utterance
Expanded commentary on the actions of bowing and the imam's utterance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the recommended posture in ruku', state the ruling on tasbih, identify the prohibition of Quranic recitation in ruku', and explain the Hanafi dispute on the imam's utterance when rising from bowing.

Core Idea
The imam should combine tasmi' and tahmid when rising; reciting Quran in ruku' is makruh tahrimi.

This passage continues the description of the prayer actions after the recitation. It details the proper posture in bowing (ruku'), the sunnah of tasbih, and the consensus-based prohibition of reciting the Quran in that position. The main focus is the dispute over the imam's utterance when rising: should he say only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' or combine it with tahmid? The commentator settles on the view that the imam combines both, relying on the practice of the Prophet and the preference of later Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Study the recommended posture in ruku'
The text describes tranquility, leveling head with back, grasping knees with hands, spreading fingers for men, and straightening legs. Bending legs like a bow is disliked.
Women do not spread their fingers.
2
Note that tasbih is sunnah
The minimum perfection of tasbih is three times. It is not wajib.
The text says 'wa dhalika adnahu' referring to three.
3
Understand the ruling on Quranic recitation in ruku'
It is makruh tahrimi (disliked near prohibition) by consensus of the four imams, based on the hadith 'I have been forbidden to recite the Quran while bowing or prostrating.'
The hadith is narrated by Muslim.
4
Identify the dispute on tasmi' and tahmid
Abu Hanifa's apparent view is that the imam says only tasmi'; the Sahibayn and a narration from Abu Hanifa say the imam should combine both. The opposing view is based on the hadith dividing the phrases.
5
Apply the tarjih
The commentator adopts the Sahibayn's view that the imam combines, citing the Prophet's practice and the preference of later scholars. This is the mufta bihi.
The follower and munfarid say only tahmid.

والسورة مطلقاً، وهذا عندهما وقال محمد: يسمي . إذا خافت لا إن جهر، لئلا يلزم الإخفاء بين الجهرين، وهو شنيع كذا قاله الزيلعي، والخلاف في السنية، وأما عدم الكراهة فمتفق عليه، ولهذا صرح في « الذخيرة وغيرها بأنه إن سمى بين الفاتحة والسورة كان حسناً عند أبي حنيفة، سواء كانت السورة مقروءة جهراً أو سراً، ورجحه المحقق ابن الهمام وتلميذه الحلبي، لشبهة الاختلاف في كونها آية من الفاتحة، وما في القنية من أنه يلزمه سجود السهو بتركها بين الفاتحة والســورة فبعيد جداً. كما أنَّ قول من قال: لا يسمي إلا في الركعة الأولى قول غير صحيح، بـل قـال الزاهدي: إنه غلط عن أصحابنا غلطاً فاحشاً، ثم قرأ الفاتحة إلا أن يكون مقتدياً، إذ لا قراءة له، (وَ) إذا قال الإمام ولا الضالين أمنَ) الإمام والمأموم، سراً) وتقدم الكلام عليه ) ، (ثم قرأ سورة)، وتقدم تفصيلها من المفصل) ، (أو) قرأ ثلاث آيات) ، قصاراً أو آية طويلة وجوباً فيسجد للسهو بتركها ساهياً، ويؤمر بإعادة الصلاة بتركها عمداً ، وقول الزيلعي يؤمر بالإعادة لترك الفاتحة دون السورة غير متبع والآكدية لا تظهر إلا في الإثم، لأنه مقول بالتشكيك لا في الإعادة وعدمها، لأن الإعادة حكم ترك الواجب مطلقاً لا الواجب المتأكد، وإذا قرأ الواجب خرج عن كراهة التحريم، وإن قرأ المسنون خرج عن كراهة التنزيه أيضاً، وإلا فقد ارتكبها فمن قال: يخرج عن الكراهة إذا قرأ الواجب أراد التحريمية، ومن قال: لا يخرج عنها أراد التنزيهية
( ثم كبر ) كل مصل (رَاكِعَا) فيبتدئ مع ابتداء الانحناء ويختمه بختمة، ليشرع في التسبيح، فلا تخلو حالة من حالات الصلاة عن ذكر (مطمئناً، مسوياً رأسَهُ بعجزه، آخذاً رُكْبَتَيْهِ بيديهِ)، ويكون الرجل (مفرجاً أصابعه) ناصباً ساقيه، وإحناؤهما شبه القوس مكروه عند أهل العلم، كما في ( الدراية » . وقيدنا بالرجل، لأن المرأة لا تفرج أصابعها كما تقدم، وسبَّحَ فِيهِ)، أي: الركوع كل مصل فيقول: سبحان ربي العظيــم مــرات (ثَلاثاً، وَذَلِكَ) العدد (أدْنَاهُ)، أي: أدنى كمال الجمع المسنون كما قدمناه ، ويكــــره قـراءة القرآن في الركوع والسجود والتشهد بإجماع الأئمة الأربعة، لقوله عليه السلام: « نُهِيتُ أَنْ أَقْرَأ الْقُرْآنَ رَاكِعا أوْ سَاجِدًا ) رواه مسلم
ثم رفعَ رَأْسَه وَاطْمَأَنَّ قائماً قائلاً: سَمِعَ اللهُ لِمَن حَمِدَهُ)، أي: رَبَّنَا لك الحمد، لو إماماً.. قبل الله حمد من حمده، قال في « الدراية » : السماع يُذكر ويراد به القبول مجازاً، كما يقال: سمع الأمير كلام فلان إذا قبله، ويقال: ما سمع كلامه أي: ردَّه ولم يقبله، وإن سمعه حقيقة، وفي الحديث: أعوذُ بِكَ مِنْ دُعَاء لا يُسْمَعُ ) (أي: لا يستجاب، وفي « الفوائد الحميدية : الهـاء فـي حـمـده للسكتة والاستراحة، لا للكناية) ، كذا نقل عن الثقات، وفي المستصفى : واللام لعود المنفعة، والهاء للكناية لا للاستراحة، كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَاشْكُرُوا لَه (سبا: ١٥] (رَبَّنَا لَكَ الحَمْدُ) فيجمع بين التسميع والتحميد (لو) كان ( إمَاماً ) ، هذا قولهما وهو رواية عن الإمام، والظاهر عنه أن الإمام يكتفي بالتسميع، وعليه مشى صاحب «الكنز» بقوله : واكتفى الإمام بالتسميع، والمؤتم والمنفرد بالتحميد، لقوله : « إِذَا قَالَ الإِمَامُ: سَمِعَ اللهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ فَقُولُوا: رَبَّنَا لَكَ الْحَمْدُ، يَسْمَع ا لَكُمْ» (۳) رواه مسلم وأبو داود وابن ماجه، والنسائي، والطحاوي، لأن ظاهر الحديث يقتضي القسمة وأنها تنافي الشركة، ووجه قولهمـا وهـو رواية عن الإمام، واختارها في « الحاوي القدسي»، وفي « الدراية»، عن « الظهيرية » ، كان الفضلي، والطحاوي، وجماعة من المتأخرين، يميلون إلى قولهما، وهو قول أهل المدينة، فاختاروا قولهما الموافق لتلك الرواية عن الإمام فاتبعناها، وقلنا: إن الإمام يجمع بينهما لقول أبي هريرة : (كان رسولُ الله صلى الله عليه وسلم حينَ يفرغ مِنَ صَلَاةِ الفَجْرِ مِنَ القِرَاءَةِ يُكَبِّر
الله
ويَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ مِنَ الرُّكُوعِ ويقول: سَمِعَ اللَّهَ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ رَبَّنَا وَلَكَ الحَمْدُ اللَّهمَّ أَنْجِ الوَلِيدَ بنَ الوَلِيـدِ... الحديث وقوله : « أنا أشبهكُم صَلاةٌ برسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم وكانَ إِذَا قَالَ: سَمِعَ اللَّهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ، قال: اللَّهُمَّ رَبَّنَا لَكَ الحَمْدُ ). وقول عائشة : « خُسِفَت الشَّمْسُ في حياةِ رسولِ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم وَصَلَّى بِالنَّاسِ، فَلَمَّا
Then he recited Al-Fatiha, and the imam and follower said Ameen silently, then he recited a surah or three verses, then he said Allahu Akbar while bowing, with tranquility, making his head level with his back, grasping his knees with his hands, spreading his fingers, and he glorified (Subhanallah) three times, and that is the minimum. Then he raised his head and stood with tranquility saying: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah.' And the surah absolutely, and this according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Muhammad said: he says the basmalah. If he is praying silently, not if aloud, to avoid hiding between two loud recitations, which is ugly, as said by al-Zayla'i. The dispute is over its being sunnah, but the absence of dislike is agreed upon. Hence it is stated in al-Dhakhira and others that if he recites the basmalah between Al-Fatiha and the surah, it is good according to Abu Hanifa, whether the surah is recited aloud or silently, and the verifying scholar Ibn al-Humam and his student al-Halabi preferred it due to the dispute over whether it is a verse of Al-Fatiha. What is in al-Qunyah that requires sajda sahw for omitting it between Fatiha and surah is very far-fetched. Likewise, the statement of one who says he should not say basmalah except in the first rak'ah is incorrect; rather al-Zahidi said it is a glaring mistake from our companions. Then he recited Al-Fatiha unless he is a follower, for there is no recitation for him. And when the imam says 'ghayri al-maghdubi 'alayhim', the imam and follower say Ameen silently, and the discussion has preceded. Then he recited a surah, and its details from al-Mufassal have preceded, or read three verses, short ones, or one long verse, as an obligation. So he does sajda sahw for omitting it forgetfully, and he is commanded to repeat the prayer if he omits it intentionally. Al-Zayla'i's statement that he is commanded to repeat for omitting Fatiha but not the surah is not followed. The emphasis appears only in sin, not in repetition or its lack, because repetition is the ruling for abandoning an obligatory act absolutely, not the highly emphasized obligatory act. If one recites the obligatory, he leaves the prohibition of tahrime, and if he recites the sunnah, he leaves the prohibition of tanzih as well; otherwise he has committed it. So whoever says he leaves prohibition when reciting the obligatory meant the tahrime, and whoever says he does not leave prohibition meant the tanzihi. Then every worshipper says Takbir while bowing; he begins with the start of bending and ends with its completion so as to begin the tasbih; no state of prayer is empty of dhikr. With tranquility, leveling his head with his back, taking his knees with his hands. The man spreads his fingers, straightening his legs; bending them like a bow is disliked according to the scholars, as in al-Diraya. We specified the man because the woman does not spread her fingers as mentioned. And he glorifies in it, i.e., in bowing, every worshipper says: 'Subhana Rabbi al-'Azeem' three times, and that number is its minimum, i.e., the minimum perfection of the recommended. Reciting the Quran during bowing, prostration, and tashahhud is disliked by consensus of the four imams, because of his saying: 'I have been forbidden to recite the Quran while bowing or prostrating' narrated by Muslim. Then he raised his head and stood with tranquility saying: 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah', i.e., 'Rabbana laka al-hamd', if he is an imam... 'Qabala Allahu hamda man hamidah'. He said in al-Diraya: 'Sami'a' is used figuratively to mean acceptance, as it is said: 'The amir heard the speech of so-and-so' if he accepted it, and it is said: 'He did not hear his speech' meaning he rejected it, even if he heard it literally. In the hadith: 'I seek refuge with You from a supplication that is not heard', meaning not answered. In al-Fawa'id al-Hamidiyya: the ha in hamidah is for pause and rest, not for pronoun. This is transmitted from reliable authorities. In al-Mustasfa: the lam is for benefit and the ha is a pronoun, not for rest, as in the verse 'wa ishkuru lahu'. (Rabbana laka al-hamd) so he combines tasmi' and tahmid if he is an imam. This is the view of the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and a narration from Abu Hanifa. The apparent view from him is that the imam suffices with tasmi', and the author of al-Kanz followed him, saying: the imam suffices with tasmi', and the follower and individual with tahmid, because of his saying: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, say Rabbana laka al-hamd, Allah will hear you' narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, al-Nasa'i, and al-Tahawi. Because the apparent meaning of the hadith entails division and precludes joint performance. The proof of the two (and the narration from Abu Hanifa) is selected by al-Hawi al-Qudsi and in al-Diraya from al-Zahiriyya. Al-Fadli, al-Tahawi, and a group of later scholars inclined to their view, which is the view of the people of Medina. So they chose their view, which agrees with that narration from Abu Hanifa, and we followed it. We say the imam combines both because of the hadith of Abu Huraira: 'When the Messenger of Allah finished the recitation of the Fajr prayer, he would say Takbir and raise his head from bowing and say: Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana wa laka al-hamd, O Allah, save al-Walid ibn al-Walid...' and his saying: 'I am the one among you whose prayer most resembles that of the Messenger of Allah. When he said Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, he said: Allahumma Rabbana laka al-hamd.' And the saying of Aisha: 'The sun eclipsed in the lifetime of the Messenger of Allah, and he prayed with the people. When'
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah. It covers the actions of the prayer from the recitation after Al-Fatiha through the tasmi' after bowing, and includes several important subsidiary rulings and intra-Hanafi disputes. The author first presents the matn describing the sequence: the imam and follower say Ameen silently, then the imam recites a surah or three verses (obligatory for imam and individual, not for follower). He then comments on the basmalah between Fatiha and surah, presenting the three Hanafi positions: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, basmalah is recited absolutely; Muhammad adds that if praying aloud, it is not recited to avoid inconsistency; Abu Hanifa's view is that it is not obligatory but recommended. The dispute is over its sunniyyah (whether it is sunnah), not over its permissibility—all agree it is not disliked. The commentator refutes the view that sajda sahw is required for omitting it, calling that very far-fetched, and rejects the opinion that basmalah is only said in the first rak'ah, calling it a glaring mistake. Next, he discusses the ruling for the follower: no recitation at all behind the imam (a Hanafi position). Then the obligation of reciting a surah or three verses after Fatiha: this is wajib (obligatory) such that omitting it forgetfully requires sajda sahw, and omitting it intentionally means the prayer must be repeated. He corrects al-Zayla'i's statement that only omission of Fatiha requires repetition, not the surah, stressing that the obligation of the surah is established even if not emphasized. Then he moves to the takbir for bowing, describing the recommended posture: the man spreads his fingers, straightens his legs, and the woman does not spread fingers. The tasbih in ruku' is sunnah, and the minimum for perfection is three. Reciting the Quran in ruku' or sujud is makruh (disliked) by consensus, with a hadith from Muslim as evidence. Finally, the most detailed discussion is on the tasmi' and tahmid (saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana laka al-hamd') when rising from bowing. The dispute is between Abu Hanifa (apparent view) and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on whether the imam should say both or only tasmi'. The commentator notes that the Sahibayn' view is supported by a narration from Abu Hanifa and is preferred by many later scholars, including the author of al-Kanz, and he adopts it. Multiple hadith are adduced: the hadith ordering the follower to say tahmid when the imam says tasmi' (which suggests division, but the Sahibayn interpret it to allow combination), the practice of the Prophet reported by Abu Huraira and others combining both, and the practice of companions. The reliance on the Sahibayn' view is explained as considering the mufta bihi (relied-upon) position, though the individual worshipper (munfarid) says only tahmid.

Key Terms
التسميع (al-tasmi'): The phrase 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' said by the imam when rising from bowing.
التحميد (al-tahmid): The phrase 'Rabbana laka al-hamd' or 'Rabbana wa laka al-hamd' said by the follower and individual, and optionally by the imam.
الركوع (al-ruku'): Bowing in prayer, a pillar (rukn) of salah.
التسبيح (al-tasbih): Glorification of Allah, specifically saying 'Subhana Rabbi al-'Azeem' in ruku'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what should the imam say when rising from bowing?
A) Only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'
B) Only 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'
C) Both 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana laka al-hamd'
D) Nothing, it is only for the follower

Key Takeaway
The imam should combine tasmi' and tahmid when rising from bowing, while the follower and individual say only tahmid; reciting Quran in ruku' is makruh.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Ruling of Tasmi' and Tahmid: Intra-Hanafi Dispute and the Preferred View
Intra-Hanafi dispute on imam combining tasmi' and tahmid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school's preferred position is that the imam combines tasmi' and tahmid, while the follower says only tahmid, and the munfarid combines, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
The imam combines tasmi' and tahmid; the follower says only tahmid; the individual combines—this is the mufta bihi.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the words said when rising from bowing (ruku') in prayer. The imam's role includes both saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana lakal hamd', while the follower only responds with praise. We will explore the proofs from hadith and the reasoning that led later Hanafi scholars to prefer the combination for the imam over the apparent view that the imam says only tasmi'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three roles and their default rulings
State the well-known Hanafi positions for the imam, munfarid, and muqtadi regarding tasmi' and tahmid.
The muqtadi says only tahmid by consensus; the munfarid combines in the mufta bihi.
2
State the apparent Hanafi position and its proof
The apparent view (zahir al-riwayah) from Abu Hanifa is that the imam says only tasmi'. The main proof is the hadith: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say Rabbana lakal hamd.' This seems to divide the roles.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and its proof
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the imam combines both. Their evidence includes multiple hadith where the Prophet (ﷺ) combined both, and the rational argument that the imam is a caller to praise so should not withhold it.
4
Analyze the rebuttal of the opposing proof
The proponents argue that the hadith only commands the follower, not the imam; it is silent about the imam. Thus, it does not preclude the imam from combining. This is why multiple narrations from Abu Hanifa exist.
The tarjih favors the Sahibayn's view.
5
Understand the tarjih and the mufta bihi
Later scholars like al-Fadli and at-Tahawi inclined to the Sahibayn's view. The author of this commentary follows that. The mufta bihi is that the imam combines.
This is a valid ikhtilaf within the school.

حَمِدَهُ، رَبَّنَا لَكَ الحَمْـدُ ) رواه الطحاوي، ولأنــه داع إلى الحمد فلا يتأخر عنه بنفسه تحرزاً عن دخوله تحت قوله تعالى: أَتَأْمُرُونَ النَّاسَ بِالْبِرِّ وَتَنسَوْنَ أَنفُسَكُمْ [الثقة: ٤٤] وقوله تعالى: لِمَ تَقُولُونَ مَا لَا تَفْعَلُونَ ﴾ [الصف : ۲]، وليس في حقيقة الحديث قسمة ونفي شركة، بل غايته أنه أمر المقتدي بالتحميد عند تسميع الإمام، وسكت عن الإمام، ولهذا تعددت الروايات عنه فيه. وقول من قال فيه قلب موضوع الإمامة حيث يصير تحميـد الإمـام بـعـد المأموم ممنوع، وقوله ( أوْ مُنْفَردَاً) متفق عليه على الأصح عن الإمام موافقة لهما بحملـه الـمـروي فيما ذكرناه، ومن الجمع بينهما على المنفرد ، وعن الإمام رواية ثانية أن المنفرد يكتفي بالتسميع لاستقلاله كالإمام، ورواية ثالثة: يكتفي بالتحميد لأن التسميع للتحريض، وهـو مفقود حالـة الانفراد ( والمُقْتَدِي يَكْتَفِي بِالتَّحْمِيدِ) اتفاقاً لقوله : ( إذا قال الإمامُ سَمِعَ اللَّهُ لِمَنْ حَمِدَهُ، فَقُولُوا: رَبَّنَا لَكَ الحَمْدُ ) (۲) رواه البخاري ومسلم. وقد اختلفت الأخبار في لفظ التحميد، فقال في بعضها: يقول: ربنا لك الحمد، وفي بعضها: اللهم ربنا لك الحمد، وفي بعضها: ربنا ولك الحمد. قال في المحيط » : اللهم ربنا لك الحمد أفضل لزيادة الثناء، وقال أبو جعفر : لا فرق بين قولك: ربنا لك الحمد، وبين قولك ربنا ولك الحمد، واختلفوا في هذه الواو، قيل زائدة، وقيل: عاطفة تقديره: ربنا حمدناك ولك الحمد ، كذا في التبيين ، والأول أظهر كما في « الدراية»، وفي « البحر » عــن المجتبى » : أفضلها اللهم ربنا ولك الحمد، ويليه اللهم ربنا لك الحمد، ويليه ربنا لك الحمد. تنبيه: شرع الحمد في آخر القيام، كما شرع في ابتدائه بقولنا : الحمد لله رب العالمين، فلذا اتجه التحميد في حق الإمام كما قدمناه
Our Lord, to You is praise, if (he is) an imam... May Allah accept the praise of whoever praises Him. He said in ad-Dirayah: 'Listening is mentioned and intended figuratively as acceptance, just as it is said: The amir listened to so-and-so's speech if he accepted it, and it is said: He did not listen to his speech meaning he rejected it and did not accept it, even if he heard it literally. In the hadith: I seek refuge in You from a supplication that is not heard, meaning not answered.' And in al-Fawa'id al-Hamidiyyah: The ha in 'hamdihi' is for pausing and resting, not for pronoun (kinayah). So it is transmitted from the reliable ones. In al-Mustasfa: The lam is for return of benefit, and the ha is for pronoun not for rest, as in His saying: 'And be grateful to Him' (Saba: 15). (Our Lord, to You is praise) so he combines tasmi' and tahmid if he is an imam. This is the view of the two (Sahibayn) and a narration from Abu Hanifah. The apparent view from him is that the imam suffices with tasmi'. Upon this the author of al-Kanz proceeded by his saying: 'The imam suffices with tasmi', and the follower and the individual with tahmid' due to his statement: 'When the imam says: Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say: Rabbana lakal hamd, may Allah hear you.' Narrated by Muslim, Abu Dawud, Ibn Majah, an-Nasa'i, and at-Tahawi. Because the apparent meaning of the hadith necessitates division and that it precludes partnership. The proof of their view (the Sahibayn) — and it is a narration from Abu Hanifah, chosen in al-Hawi al-Qudsi and ad-Dirayah from az-Zahiriyyah — was that al-Fadli, at-Tahawi, and a group of later scholars inclined to their view, and it is the saying of the people of Medina. So they chose their view which agrees with that narration from Abu Hanifah, and we followed it. We said: The imam combines both due to the saying of Abu Hurairah: 'When the Messenger of Allah finished the prayer of Fajr from recitation, he would say Allahu Akbar, raise his head from bowing and say: Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana wa lakal hamd, Allahumma anji al-Walid...' and his saying: 'I am the one among you most resembling the prayer of the Messenger of Allah; when he said: Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, he said: Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd.' And the saying of Aishah: 'The sun eclipsed in the lifetime of the Messenger of Allah, and he prayed with the people; when he raised his head from bowing he said: Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, Rabbana lakal hamd.' Narrated by at-Tahawi. And because he is a caller to praise, so he should not be delayed from it by himself, to avoid falling under His saying: 'Do you enjoin righteousness upon people while you forget yourselves?' (Al-Baqarah: 44) and His saying: 'Why do you say that which you do not do?' (As-Saff: 2). And there is not in the apparent meaning of the hadith a division and denial of partnership; rather its utmost is that it commands the follower to say tahmid when the imam says tasmi', and it is silent about the imam; thus the narrations from him are multiple in this. And the saying of those who say there is a reversal of the imam's position such that the imam's tahmid comes after the follower's is refuted. And his saying (or if he is an individual) is agreed upon according to the most correct view from Abu Hanifah in agreement with the two (Sahibayn) by carrying the transmitted hadith as we mentioned, and by combining both for the individual. And from Abu Hanifah there is a second narration that the individual suffices with tasmi' because of his independence like the imam, and a third narration: he suffices with tahmid because tasmi' is for encouragement, which is absent in the state of individuality. (And the follower suffices with tahmid) by agreement due to his saying: 'When the imam says Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah, then say: Rabbana lakal hamd.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. And the reports differ regarding the wording of tahmid. Some have: Rabbana lakal hamd, some: Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd, some: Rabbana wa lakal hamd. He said in al-Muhit: Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd is best for increasing praise. Abu Ja'far said: There is no difference between your saying Rabbana lakal hamd and your saying Rabbana wa lakal hamd. They differed regarding this waw: it is said to be redundant, and it is said to be conjunctive, the estimation being: Our Lord, we have praised You and to You is praise. So it is in at-Tabyin, and the first is more apparent as in ad-Dirayah. In al-Bahr from al-Mujtaba: The best is Allahumma Rabbana wa lakal hamd, then Allahumma Rabbana lakal hamd, then Rabbana lakal hamd. Note: Praise is legislated at the end of standing, just as it is legislated at its beginning by our saying al-hamdu lillahi Rabbil 'alamin. Therefore tahmid is appropriate for the imam as we have presented.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the tasmi' (Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah) and tahmid (Rabbana lakal hamd) for the imam, the individual (munfarid), and the follower (muqtadi). The author first clarifies that 'hearing' in the tasmi' can mean acceptance figuratively. Then he presents the positions: The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and a narration from Abu Hanifa hold that the imam should combine both tasmi' and tahmid. The apparent view of Abu Hanifa is that the imam only says tasmi'. The author of al-Kanz followed the latter. The text presents the evidence from hadith, particularly the famous hadith ordering followers to say tahmid when the imam says tasmi'. The opponents of combining argue that this divides the actions (imam tasmi', follower tahmid) and precludes partnership. The proponents of combining respond that the hadith only commands the follower, not the imam, and that the imam's own practice (as per multiple authentic hadith) was to combine. They also argue that the imam, as a caller to praise, should not delay it himself, citing Quranic verses about commanding good and forgetting oneself. The passage then states that the relied-upon position in the school is the one supported by the Sahibayn and many later scholars, i.e., the imam combines. For the individual, the most correct position uses the same reasoning as the imam, so he combines. The follower says only tahmid by consensus. Finally, the passage discusses the preferred wording of tahmid, noting that the version with 'Allahumma' and 'wa' is best. This is a characteristic fiqhi analysis that examines proofs, examines linguistic nuances, and settles on a preferred view within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
تسميع (tasmi'): Saying 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' when rising from bowing.
تحميد (tahmid): Saying 'Rabbana lakal hamd' or similar after tasmi'. The preferred wording is 'Allahumma Rabbana wa lakal hamd'.
إمام (imam): The one who leads the congregational prayer.
مقتدي (muqtadi): The follower in prayer who prays behind the imam.
منفرد (munfarid): One who prays alone, not in congregation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the Hanafi school as presented in this passage, what should the imam say when rising from bowing?
A) Only 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah'.
B) Only 'Rabbana lakal hamd'.
C) Both 'Sami'a Allahu liman hamidah' and 'Rabbana lakal hamd'.
D) The imam should not say anything; he should wait for the followers.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon position is that the imam combines tasmi' and tahmid, the follower says only tahmid, and the individual combines.

The Sunnah Sequence of Sujud and the Wajib of Prostrating on Nose and Forehead
Ruling on the sequence of placing limbs when going into prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah sequence of placing limbs when going into sujud and identify the wajib requirement of prostrating on both the nose and forehead according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Prostration begins with the knees, then hands, then face — a sunnah order that mirrors the opening takbir.

This lesson explains the proper manner of going into prostration (sujud) as outlined in the Hanafi school. The text from Imdad al-Fattah details the recommended sequence of placing the limbs and emphasizes that prostration must be performed on both the nose and forehead together. You will learn the sunnah steps and the evidence behind them.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah sequence
The text commands: place knees first, then hands, then face between palms. Note the exception for those with an excuse (e.g., illness, old age).
This order is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Identify the wajib element
Prostration must be on both nose and forehead. There is an intra-Hanafi difference on whether the nose alone suffices; the preferred view (mufta bihi) requires both.
The text references a previous discussion on this ikhtilaf.
3
Understand the evidence
The sunnah sequence is supported by a hadith (referenced as 'as we have narrated') and by qiyas: as the head is placed between hands at the opening takbir, so it is at sujud.
The qiyas is explicit: 'the end of the rak'ah is considered like its beginning.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ كَبَّرَ كل مصل (خاراً لِلْسُجُودِ) ويختمه عند وضع جبهته للسجود؛ لئلا يخلو حال من الصلاة عن ذكر، وتقدم دليله (ثمّ: وَضَعَ رُكْبَتَيْهِ، ثُمَّ يَدَيْهِ) إذا لم يكن به عذر يمنعه من النزول على هذه الصفة كما تقدم)، (ثُمَّ) وضع (وَجْهَهُ بين كفَّيْهِ) لما رويناه)، ولأن آخر الركعة معتبر بأولها، فكما يجعل رأسه بين يديه عند التحريمـة، فكذا عند السجود، كما في «السراج» عن «المبسوط ) ، ( وسجدَ بأنفهِ وجَبهتِهِ) وتقدم أن الاكتفاء بالأنف
Then every worshipper says Allahu Akbar (going down for prostration) and completes it at the placement of his forehead for prostration, so that no moment of the prayer is devoid of remembrance; its proof has preceded. Then he places his knees, then his hands, if there is no excuse preventing him from descending in this manner as has preceded. Then he places his face between his palms, as we have narrated, and because the end of the rak'ah is considered like its beginning: just as he places his head between his hands at the takbirat al-ihram, so too at prostration, as in as-Siraj from al-Mabsut. And he prostrates on his nose and forehead; and it has preceded that sufficing with the nose
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage states the sunnah method of going into prostration (sujud). The text instructs that every worshipper (imam, follower, or individual) should say Allahu Akbar when going down for sujud and complete the takbir when the forehead touches the ground. The reason given is that no moment of prayer should be empty of remembrance. Then the sequence is: first place the knees on the ground, then the hands, and then the face between the palms. This is the recommended order unless there is an excuse (such as illness or old age) that prevents it. The basis for placing the face between the hands is a hadith and also an analogy: just as one places his head between his hands at the beginning of prayer (takbirat al-ihram), similarly at sujud. Finally, the text affirms that prostration must be on the nose and forehead together; however, it references a previous discussion that sufficing with the nose alone is disputed. This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Nur al-Idah, explaining the proper form with supporting evidence.

Key Terms
ركبة (rukbah): The knee; one of the body parts to be placed first when going into prostration.
سجود (sujud): Prostration, an integral part of the prayer.
جبهة (jabhat): The forehead; a required part of the body for valid sujud along with the nose.
أنف (anf): The nose; must also touch the ground in sujud according to the preferred view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the recommended order of placing limbs when going into prostration?
A) Hands, knees, face.
B) Knees, hands, face.
C) Face, hands, knees.
D) All simultaneously.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah in sujud is to place knees first, then hands, then face, and the wajib is to prostrate on both the nose and forehead together.

Manner of Going into Sujood: Takbir and Placement of Limbs
Describes the proper sequence and rulings for entering prostration

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the proper sequence of entering sujood and explain the Hanafi ruling that both the forehead and nose must touch the ground.

Core Idea
In sujood, the forehead is the fard, the nose is wajib; both must touch the ground.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah Sharh Nur al-Idah details the correct method of descending into sujood. It outlines the recommended order of placing limbs and clarifies the obligatory and necessary parts of the face that must touch the ground. Understanding this ruling is essential for performing sujood validly according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Sequence
Read the passage to determine the order in which the worshipper places his limbs when going into sujood: knees, hands, then face.
This order is based on analogy with the initial takbir and is sunnah, not fard.
2
Recognize the Ruling on Face Parts
The passage states that sujood is performed with both the nose and forehead. The forehead is the fard, while the nose is wajib (necessary).
There is a weak opinion that the nose alone suffices, but the correct view is that both must be placed.
3
Understand the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
The author notes that some held the nose alone is sufficient, but the Imam retracted that view. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that the nose must join the forehead.
This illustrates the process of tarjih within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ كَبَّرَ ) كل مصل (خاراً لِلْسُجُودِ) ويختمه عند وضع جبهته للسجود؛ لئلا يخلو حال من الصلاة عن ذكر، وتقدم دليله (ثمّ: وَضَعَ رُكْبَتَيْهِ، ثُمَّ يَدَيْهِ) إذا لم يكن به عذر يمنعه من النزول على هذه الصفة كما تقدم)، (ثُمَّ) وضع (وَجْهَهُ بين كفَّيْهِ) لما رويناه)، ولأن آخر الركعة معتبر بأولها، فكما يجعل رأسه بين يديه عند التحريمـة، فكذا عند السجود، كما في «السراج» عن «المبسوط ) ، ( وسجدَ بأنفهِ وجَبهتِهِ) وتقدم أن الاكتفاء بالأنف مرجوح وأن الأصح رجوع الإمام عنه، وقدم ذكر الأنف على الجبهة، لأن في الأنف المجرد عن ضم الجبهة اختلافاً، والصحيح أن ضمه إليها واجب، ومحل الفرض هو الجبهة كما قدمناه فيسجد بهما
Then every worshipper says takbir while going down for sujood, and completes it when placing his forehead for sujood, so that no moment of the prayer is without remembrance. Its proof preceded. Then he places his knees, then his hands, if there is no excuse preventing him from descending in this manner as previously. Then he places his face between his palms as we narrated, and because the end of the rak'ah is considered like its beginning, so just as he places his head between his hands at the takbir tahrimah, likewise at sujood, as in al-Siraj from al-Mabsut. And he performs sujood with his nose and forehead. It preceded that being satisfied with the nose is weak (marjuh) and that the correct view is the Imam retracted from it. He mentioned the nose before the forehead because there is a difference of opinion regarding the nose alone without joining the forehead, and the correct view is that joining it to the forehead is wajib, and the place of the fard is the forehead as we stated, so he does sujood with both.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage explains the proper method of going into sujood. First, the worshipper says takbir while descending, completing it just before placing the forehead on the ground. Then he places his knees first, then his hands, then his face (forehead and nose) between his hands. This order is based on the analogy with the initial takbir (tahrimah) where the hands are raised to the ears and the position of the head. The author notes that if one has a valid excuse (like weak knees), he may modify the order. Regarding the parts of the face used for sujood: the place of obligation (fard) is the forehead, but the nose is also wajib to include. There is a weak opinion that sujood is valid with just the nose, but the correct Hanafi position is that both the nose and forehead must touch the ground. The author emphasizes that the fard is the forehead, but joining the nose is wajib, so both should be placed down.

Key Terms
الجبين (al-jabheen): The forehead; the part of the face upon which the fard of sujood is performed.
الأنف (al-anf): The nose; it must be placed on the ground along with the forehead in sujood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, what is the ruling regarding touching the nose to the ground during sujood?
A) It is fard (obligatory)
B) It is wajib (necessary)
C) It is sunnah (recommended)
D) It is not required

Key Takeaway
In sujood, the forehead is fard and the nose is wajib; both must be placed on the ground, and the sunnah sequence is knees, hands, then face.
