Sunnah Postures in Sujood: Mujafah and Orientation
Details the recommended postures during sujood, including mujafah for men, posture for women, and direction of fingers and toes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended (sunnah) postures in sujood for men and women, including the conditions for mujafah and the direction of fingers and toes.

Core Idea
Men spread limbs in sujood; women keep close. Both face qibla with fingers and toes.

This passage explains the sunnah postures during sujood that enhance humility and proper form. It distinguishes the practices for men and women, with specific exceptions for crowded congregations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum required in sujood
The text states the minimal sujood includes being at rest (mutma'in) and saying tasbih three times. This is sunnah, not wajib.
Tasbih is a sunnah dhikr; mutma'in is a condition for validity.
2
Understand mujafah for men
Men should keep their belly away from thighs and upper arms away from armpits, unless in a crowd. This enhances humility and ensures proper contact of the forehead and nose.
In a crowd, one should draw limbs in to avoid harming neighbors.
3
Learn finger and toe orientation
Both men and women should direct the fingers of their hands and toes toward the qibla. Clenching the fingers in sujood is sunnah (unique to this posture).
Wisdom: mercy descends in sujood; clenching allows receiving more.
4
Note the woman's posture
A woman should keep her limbs close: draw upper arms to sides and stick belly to thighs. This is for concealment as her entire body is 'awrah.
This is opposite to the man's mujafah, due to modesty.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطمئناً، مسبحاً ثلاثاً، وذلك أدناه، وجافي بطنه عن فَخِذَيْهِ، وعَصْدَيْهِ عَنْ إِبْطَيْهِ، في غير زَحْمَةٍ، موجهاً أصابع يديه ورجليه نحو القبلة، والمرأةُ تَخْفِضُ، وتُلْزِقُ بطنَها بفخذيها، وجلس بين السجدتين، واضعاً يديه على فَخِذيه، مطمئناً، ثمّ كبّر، وسَجَدَ مطمئناً . ذلك أدناه على ما تقدم. وناسب وصف الرب بالعلي في السجود. وبالعظيم في الركوع، لأن الركوع انحناء وفيه مذلة العبد، فناسب وصف الرب بالعظمة، والعبد في سجوده يكون في غاية التسفل، وقد وضع أشرف أعضائه على أحقر موجود وهو التراب، فناسب وصفه تعالى بالعلو في الاقتدار لا المكان، تعالى الله. عن علواً كبيراً. (وَجَافَى) أي: باعد الرجل ( بطنَهُ عن فَخِذَيْهِ، وعَضُدَيْهِ عن إبْطَيْه)، لأنه أشبه بالتواضع وأبلغ في تمكين الجبهة والأنف من الأرض، ولكن هذا ( في غير زَحْمَةٍ) وينضم فيها حذراً عن إضرار الجار، والحكمة في الإبداء والمجافاة أن يظهر كل عضو بنفسه، ولا تعتمد الأعضـاء عـلـى بعضها بعضاً، وهذا ضد القيام في الصفوف، لأن المقصود فيه المساواة بين المصلين، ليصيروا كالجسد الواحد، فلا تبقى فيما بينهم فرجة يتخللها الشيطان، وفي المجافاة بعد عن صِفَةِ الكسالى، فإن المنبسط يشبه الكلب، وتشعر حالته بالتهاون وقلة الاعتناء بشأن الصلاة، ويكون المصلــي ولــو امرأة (موجهاً أصابع يديه) ويضمهما كل الضم، ولا يندب إلا هنا، والحكمة فيه: أن الـرحمــة تـنـزل عليه في السجود فبالضم ينال الأكثر ، (وَ) يكون موجهاً أصابع رجليه نحو القبلة، والمرأة تَخْفِضُ) فتضم عضديها لجنبيها، وتُلزق بطنَها بفخِذَيْها، لأنها عورة مستورة، وهذا أستر لهـا ثـم رفع رأسه مكبراً (وَجَلَسَ) كل مصَلِّ ( بين السجدتين، واضعاً يَدَيهِ عَلَى فَخِذيه، مُطْمَئِناً) وتقدم دليله، وليس فيه ذكر مسنون، وما ورد فيه)، في حال القيام من الركوع، فمحمول عـلـى التهجد عندنا ( ثمّ كبّر ) للسجود (وَسَجَدَ) بعده (مُطْمَئِناً)، وتقدم دليله ، وحكمة تكراره، وهو أي الجلوس بين السجدتين مسنون، ومقتضى الدليل من المواظبة عليها الوجوب، لكن المذهب خلافه، وما في شرح المنية ) من أن الأصح وجوبها إن كان بالنظر إلى الدراية فمسلم، لمـا عـلـمـت مـن المواظبة، وإن كان من وجه الرواية فلا، لأن الشراح مصرحون بالسنية، قاله في ا
While being at rest (mutma'in), saying tasbih three times, and that is the minimum. And he keeps his belly away from his thighs, and his upper arms away from his armpits, unless in a crowd (because then he should not cause harm to his neighbor). He directs the fingers of his hands and his toes towards the qibla. And the woman lowers herself (takhfish) and sticks her belly to her thighs. And he sits between the two prostrations, placing his hands on his thighs, being at rest. Then he says takbir and prostrates being at rest. That is the minimum as mentioned earlier. And it is appropriate to describe the Lord with 'The Most High' in sujood, and with 'The Magnificent' in ruku, because ruku is bowing and has humiliation of the slave, so it is appropriate to describe the Lord with greatness, and the slave in his sujood is at the utmost lowliness, having placed his noblest limb on the most contemptible existing thing, which is dust, so it is appropriate to describe the Almighty with highness in power, not in place. Exalted is Allah far above such. And mujafah means the man distances his belly from his thighs and his upper arms from his armpits, because it is more like humility and more effective in enabling the forehead and nose to reach the ground. But this is when not in a crowded situation, and he draws together in a crowd to avoid harming his neighbor. The wisdom in exposing and spacing is that each limb appears by itself, and the limbs do not lean on each other. This is the opposite of standing in rows, because the objective there is equality among the worshippers, so they become like one body, leaving no gap for the devil to enter. And in mujafah there is distance from the characteristics of lazy people, because the one who spreads out resembles a dog, and his state suggests negligence and lack of care for the prayer. And the worshipper, even if a woman, faces the fingers of his hands (and clenches them tightly, which is not recommended except here). The wisdom in that: mercy descends upon him in sujood, so by clenching he obtains more. And he faces the toes of his feet towards the qibla. And the woman lowers herself: she draws her upper arms to her sides and sticks her belly to her thighs, because she is a covered 'awrah, and this is more concealing for her. Then he raises his head saying takbir, and every worshipper sits between the two prostrations, placing his hands on his thighs, being at rest. Its proof preceded. There is no specific dhikr mentioned as sunnah; what is narrated (like 'Rabbighfir li') in the context of standing after ruku is interpreted as for tahajjud in our school. Then he says takbir for sujood and prostrates after it being at rest. Its proof preceded, and the wisdom of its repetition. And the sitting between the two sajdahs is sunnah. The apparent evidence from constancy (muwazabah) indicates obligation, but the madhhab is contrary. What is in Sharh al-Munyah that the most correct is its obligation, if considered from the perspective of dirayah, is acceptable, because you know from constancy; but if from the perspective of riwayah, then no, because the commentators declare it sunnah.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage details the recommended and obligatory postures during sujood and the sitting between the two sajdahs. The worshipper must be in a state of calm (mutma'in), and the minimum tasbih is three times 'Subhana Rabbiy al-A'la'. Men should keep their belly away from their thighs and arms away from their sides (mujafah), but only when not in a crowded congregation; in a crowd, they should stay close to avoid harming neighbors. The fingers and toes should face the qibla. Women have a different posture: they keep their limbs close to their bodies to conceal themselves. The sitting between the two sajdahs is sunnah, not wajib, although constant practice might suggest obligation; the madhhab is clear on sunnah. The author also explains the wisdom behind the different postures and the appropriateness of Allah's attributes in ruku and sujood.

Key Terms
المجافاة (al-mujafah): Keeping the belly away from the thighs and the arms away from the armpits during sujood (for men).
الجلوس بين السجدتين (al-juloos bayna al-sajdatayn): The brief sitting between the two prostrations in prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a man do if he is in a crowded sujood situation?
A) He should still practice mujafah to show humility.
B) He should draw his limbs close to avoid harming his neighbor.
C) He should raise his arms to avoid touching others.
D) He should skip sujood if crowded.

Key Takeaway
The sunnah postures in sujood are gender-specific: men spread limbs (except in crowds), women keep limbs close; both face the qibla with fingers and toes.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Ruling on Sitting Between the Two Sajdahs
Clarifies the sunnah status of sitting between the two sajdahs and the intra-madhhab debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that sitting between the two sajdahs is sunnah mu'akkadah and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view, citing the evidence from the passage.

Core Idea
Sitting between the two sajdahs is sunnah mu'akkadah in Hanafi, not wajib, despite constant practice.

This passage clarifies that the brief sitting between prostrations is a recommended sunnah in the Hanafi school, contrary to the apparent implication of the Prophet's constant practice (muwazabah). The madhhab relies on the majority of commentators, though some later scholars considered it wajib based on dirayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its described posture
The passage states that after raising from sujood, the worshipper sits between the two sajdahs placing hands on thighs, being at rest.
This posture is sunnah; no specific dhikr is prescribed except in tahajjud for 'Rabbighfir li'.
2
Recognize the explicit ruling: sunnah
The author says clearly: 'وهو أي الجلوس بين السجدتين مسنون' – it is sunnah.
This is the ruling of the madhhab.
3
Understand the evidence of constant practice
The Prophet always performed this sitting, which suggests obligation (muwazabah indicates wujub in usul). However, the madhhab does not take that position.
The passage notes this tension: 'مقتضى الدليل من المواظبة عليها الوجوب'.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi difference
Sharh al-Munyah states the most correct is wujub from dirayah (reasoning), but from riwayah (transmission), the commentators affirm sunnah.
The mufta bihi is the sunnah view; no sajdah sahw required if omitted.
5
Compare with cross-madhhab view
The Shafi'i school holds that sitting between sajdahs is wajib, and missing it requires sajdah sahw. The Hanafi school differs.
This is a practical difference: in Hanafi, if omitted intentionally, prayer is valid but makruh; in Shafi'i, sajdah sahw is required.

According to the passage, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling regarding the sitting between the two sajdahs in the Hanafi school?
A) Wajib – omission requires sajdah sahw.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Manner of Prostration and Sitting Between Prostrations: Rulings and Disputes
Explains the posture, tasbeeh, and sitting in prostration with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sunnah acts of prostration, explain the wisdom behind limb positioning, and analyze whether the sitting between prostrations is wajib or sunnah in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Prophet's practice in prostration establishes sunnah; the Hanafi school distinguishes between continuous practice (muwazabah) and obligation.

This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah details the recommended postures and recitation during prostration, as well as the sitting between prostrations. It also addresses a key intra-madhhab dispute about the ruling of that sitting, clarifying that although the Prophet continuously performed it, the Hanafi position is that it remains sunnah, not wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sunnah acts of prostration
List the required states and actions: tranquility (itminan), saying tasbeeh three times, limb positioning (men keep belly and arms away, women keep close), and pointing fingers and toes toward the qiblah.
These are sunnah mu'akkadah, meaning the Prophet consistently did them but did not command them as obligatory.
2
Analyze the evidence for the postures
The hadith cited (e.g., 'when he prostrated, he would keep his arms away until the whiteness of his armpits could be seen') shows the Prophet's practice. The Hanafi school interprets this as indicating recommendation, not obligation, because the evidence is zanni al-thubut and zanni al-dalalah.
The wisdom behind the posture is humility and ensuring each limb is independent.
3
Apply the gender distinction
Women are instructed to keep their limbs close together (takhfid) for modesty, as they are considered 'awrah. This applies even in non-crowded situations.
This distinction is based on the principle of satr al-'awrah.
4
Locate the dispute on sitting between prostrations
The text mentions that the apparent implication of the Prophet's continuous practice (muwazabah) would suggest obligation, but the established Hanafi position is that it is sunnah. Some later scholars (e.g., in Sharh al-Munyah) argued for obligation from a theoretical perspective.
The passage notes that from the perspective of riwayah (transmission), the commentators clearly state sunniyyah, so the relied-upon view is sunnah.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The majority of Hanafi commentators uphold the sunnah status. The tarjih is based on the weight of the zahir al-riwayah and the absence of a clear command making it wajib.
This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf where the mufta bihi is sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مطمئناً، مسبحاً ثلاثاً، وذلك أدناه، وجافي بطنه عن فَخِذَيْهِ، وعَصْدَيْهِ عَنْ إِبْطَيْهِ، في غير زَحْمَةٍ، موجهاً أصابع يديه ورجليه نحو القبلة، والمرأةُ تَخْفِضُ، وتُلْزِقُ بطنَها بفخذيها، وجلس بين السجدتين، واضعاً يديه على فَخِذيه، مطمئناً، ثمّ كبّر، وسَجَدَ مطمئناً، .
(1)
ذلك مرجوح وأن الأصح رجوع الإمام عنه، وقدم ذكر الأنف على الجبهة، لأن في الأنف المجرد عن ضم الجبهة اختلافاً، والصحيح أن ضمه إليها واجب، ومحل الفرض هو الجبهة كما قدمناه فيسجد بهما (مُطْمَئِنَا مُسَبِّحَاً) بأن يقول: سبحان ربي الأعلى مرات (ثَلاثَاً، وَذَلِكَ أدْنَاهُ) على ما تقدم". وناسب وصف الرب بالعلي في السجود. وبالعظيم في الركوع، لأن الركوع انحناء وفيه مذلة العبد، فناسب وصف الرب بالعظمة، والعبد في سجوده يكون في غاية التسفل، وقد وضع أشرف أعضائه على أحقر موجود وهو التراب، فناسب وصفه تعالى بالعلو في الاقتدار لا المكان، تعالى الله . عن علواً كبيراً. (وَجَافَى) أي: باعد الرجل ( بطنَهُ عن فَخِذَيْهِ، وعَضُدَيْهِ عن إبْطَيْه)، لأنه أشبه بالتواضع وأبلغ في تمكين الجبهة والأنف من الأرض، ولكن هذا ( في غير زَحْمَةٍ) وينضم فيها (۳) حذراً عن إضرار الجار، والحكمة في الإبداء والمجافاة أن يظهر كل عضو بنفسه، ولا تعتمد الأعضـاء عـلـى بعضها بعضاً، وهذا ضد القيام في الصفوف، لأن المقصود فيه المساواة بين المصلين، ليصيروا كالجسد الواحد، فلا تبقى فيما بينهم فرجة يتخللها الشيطان، وفي المجافاة بعد عن صِفَةِ الكسالى، فإن المنبسط يشبه الكلب، وتشعر حالته بالتهاون وقلة الاعتناء بشأن الصلاة، ويكون المصلــي ولــو امرأة (موجهاً أصابع يديه) ويضمهما كل الضم، ولا يندب إلا هنا، والحكمة فيه: أن الـرحمــة تـنـزل عليه في السجود فبالضم ينال الأكثر ، (وَ) يكون موجهاً أصابع رجليه نحو القبلة، والمرأة تَخْفِضُ) فتضم عضديها لجنبيها، وتُلزق بطنَها بفخِذَيْها، لأنها عورة مستورة، وهذا أستر لهـا ثـم رفع رأسه مكبراً (وَجَلَسَ) كل مصَلِّ ( بين السجدتين، واضعاً يَدَيهِ عَلَى فَخِذيه، مُطْمَئِناً) وتقدم دليله، وليس فيه ذكر مسنون، وما ورد فيه)، في حال القيام من الركوع، فمحمـول عـلـى التهجد عندنا ( ثمّ كبّر ) للسجود (وَسَجَدَ) بعده (مُطْمَئِناً)، وتقدم دليله ، وحكمة تكراره، وهو أي الجلوس بين السجدتين مسنون، ومقتضى الدليل من المواظبة عليها الوجوب، لكن المذهب خلافه، وما في شرح المنية ) من أن الأصح وجوبها إن كان بالنظر إلى الدراية فمسلم، لمـا عـلـمـت مـن المواظبة، وإن كان من وجه الرواية فلا، لأن الشراح مصرحون بالسنية، قاله في ا
With tranquility, saying tasbeeh three times, and that is the minimum, and he keeps his belly away from his thighs and his forearms away from his armpits, when not in crowding, pointing the fingers of his hands and feet toward the qiblah; and the woman lowers and sticks her belly to her thighs, and sits between the two prostrations, placing his hands on his thighs, with tranquility, then says takbir and prostrates with tranquility. That is the weaker view and the correct view is that the imam retracted it; and he mentioned the nose before the forehead because regarding the nose alone without including the forehead there is disagreement, and the correct view is that including it with the forehead is obligatory, and the place of the obligatory act is the forehead as we have mentioned, so he prostrates with both. (With tranquility, saying tasbeeh) by saying: 'Subhana rabbiyal a'la' three times, and that is the minimum, as previously mentioned. And it is appropriate to describe the Lord as the Most High in prostration, and as the Almighty in bowing, because bowing is bending and contains the humility of the servant, so it is appropriate to describe the Lord with might, while the servant in his prostration is in the utmost lowness and has placed his noblest organ on the most contemptible thing, which is dust, so it is appropriate to describe Him as Most High in power, not in place—exalted is Allah above that greatly. (And he keeps away) i.e., the man keeps his belly away from his thighs and his arms from his armpits, because it is more like humility and more effective in placing the forehead and nose on the ground, but this is when not in crowding, and in crowding he draws together, fearing harm to the neighbor. The wisdom in separating and keeping away is that each limb appears by itself and limbs do not rely on each other; this is opposite to standing in rows because the objective there is equality among the worshippers so that they become like one body, leaving no gaps between them for the devil to enter, and in keeping away there is distance from the characteristic of lazy people, for the stretched one resembles a dog, and his state indicates negligence and lack of care for prayer. And the worshipper, even if a woman, points the fingers of his hands and presses them together completely—recommended only here—and the wisdom is that mercy descends upon him in prostration, so by pressing he obtains more. And he points the toes of his feet toward the qiblah; and the woman lowers, so she presses her arms to her sides and sticks her belly to her thighs because she is a covered awrah and this is more concealing for her. Then he raises his head saying takbir and every worshipper sits between the two prostrations, placing his hands on his thighs, with tranquility, and its evidence has preceded; and there is no mention of recommended acts in it, and what has been reported regarding it (i.e., during standing from bowing) is taken as applying to tahajjud according to us. Then he says takbir for prostration and prostrates after it with tranquility, and its evidence and the wisdom of its repetition have preceded. And the sitting between the two prostrations is recommended; the implication of the evidence from continuity is obligation, but the madhhab is otherwise. And what is in Sharh al-Munyah that the correct view is its obligation from the perspective of knowledge is accepted because of the known continuity, but from the perspective of transmission it is not, because the commentators clearly state it is recommended, as he said in...
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah explains the sunnah acts of prostration and the sitting between prostrations. It opens by stating the requirement of tranquility (itminan) and the minimum tasbeeh of three times. Then it discusses the positioning of limbs: men should keep their bellies away from thighs and arms from sides, except in crowded congregational prayer where they should press together to avoid harming neighbors. Women are instructed to do the opposite—keep their limbs close—for modesty. The wisdom behind these postures is given: to show each limb independently as an act of humility, and to avoid resembling the lazy or animals. For the sitting between the two prostrations, the author notes that although the apparent implication of the Prophet's continuous practice might suggest obligation, the established Hanafi position is that it is merely recommended (sunnah). The author mentions a view from Sharh al-Munyah that considers it obligatory from a theoretical standpoint, but rejects it based on the clear statements of the commentators. The passage relies on hadith evidence (cited in footnotes) regarding the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
مطمئن (muṭmaʾinn): In a state of calm and stillness, with each limb settled in its place.
مسبح (musabbiḥ): One who says tasbeeh (subhan Allah).
جلسة الاستراحة (jalsat al-istirāḥah): A brief sitting after the second sajdah before standing for the next rak'ah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a man separating his belly from his thighs and arms from his sides during prostration when praying alone?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Wajib
C) Makruh tanzihi
D) Haram

Key Takeaway
The prostration postures and sitting between prostrations are sunnah acts; the Hanafi school distinguishes between the Prophet's practice and legal obligation.

Rising to the Second Rak'ah: Rulings on Jalsat al-Istirahah and Repetitions
Explains the recommended way to stand and what is omitted in the second rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on jalsat al-istirahah and identify which dhikr and actions are omitted in the second rak'ah, applying the cited evidence.

Core Idea
Jalsat al-istirahah is makruh; thana, ta'awwudh, and raising hands are not repeated in the second rak'ah.

When rising from the second prostration, there is a difference of practice among schools. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi position on leaning on hands, the brief sitting called jalsat al-istirahah, and what changes between the first and second rak'ah. Understanding these points ensures your prayer follows the established sunnah as transmitted by the Companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions and rulings for rising
The text describes rising without leaning on hands and without sitting. Determine the ruling (sunnah vs. makruh) for each action based on the Hanafi school.
Leaning is permissible only with an excuse.
2
Understand the evidence for the Hanafi position
Examine the hadith prohibiting leaning and the practice of 'Umar, 'Ali, and other Companions rising on the fronts of their feet. Note that jalsat al-istirahah is makruh because it contradicts this practice.
The evidence is zanni but relied upon due to companion consensus.
3
Compare with the Shafi'i position
The Shafi'i school considers jalsat al-istirahah sunnah and allows raising hands at multiple points. Contrast their evidence with the Hanafi response.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; both sides have proofs.
4
List the three omissions in the second rak'ah
From the text: no thana (opening supplication), no ta'awwudh (seeking refuge), and no raising hands during bowing and standing. Understand the reasoning: thana and ta'awwudh are only at the beginning of prayer.
The principle: acts prescribed at the start are not repeated unless the session changes.
5
Recognize the scope of raising hands
The Hanafi school restricts raising hands to the opening takbir only. The text cites a hadith that the Prophet only raised hands in the first takbir and then did not return.
Other occasions like qunut and 'Eid are separate; see the mnemonic 'Faq'as'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وسبَّحَ فِيهِ) أي: السجود (ثلاثاً، وجافي بطنه عن فخذيه، وأبدى عَضُدَيْهِ)، وهما ضبعـاه، والضبع بسكون الباء لا غير العضد، كذا في الصحاح ، وقال بعضهم يرفعها وهما لغتان كذا في مبسوط» شيخ الإسلام، وذلك سُنَّة لما روينا ) ، ( ثم رَفَعَ رأسَهُ مكبراً للنهوض ) أي: الـقـيـام للركعة الثانية (بلا اعْتِمَادٍ عَلَى الأرْضِ بِيَدِيهِ) إن لم يكن به عذر، (وبـلا قـعـود) قبـل القـيـام، يسمى جلسة الاستراحة - هو سنة عند الشافعي رحمه الله - لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم نَهَى أَنْ يَعْتَمِدَ الرَّجُلُ عَلَى يَدَيْهِ إِذَا نَهَضَ » (٢) وعن علي الله أنه قال: «مِنَ السُّنة إذا انتهضَتْ مِنَ الرَّكْعَتَين أنْ لا تَعْتَمِد عَلَى الأَرْضِ بِيَدَيْكَ إلا أن لا تستطيع ). وكان عمر، وعلي، وأصحاب رسول الله لينهضُونَ في الصَّلاة على صدور أقدامهم ) وفي « الدراية » عن «شرح الطحاوي : لا بأس بأن يعتمد بيده على الأرض شيخاً كان أو شاباً، وهـو قول عامة العلماء رحمهم الله، وما روي عن علي كان ينفرد به وفي جمل النوازل» : جلسة الاستراحة مكروهة عندنا، لأن المروي أن الصحابة كانوا ينهضون على صدور أقدامهم. (والرَّكْعَةُ الثَّانية) يفعل فيها (كالأولى)، وعلمت ما سَمِلَتْه ( إلا أنَّهُ) أي: المصلي ( لا يُثْنِي) في الركعة الثانية، لأنه شرع في أول العبادة دون أثنائها، ولهذا سمي دعاء الاستفتاح، ولا يتعـوذُ لأنه شرع في أول العبادة لدفع وسوسة الشيطان، فلا يتكرر إلا بتبدل المجلس، كما لو تعوذ وقرأ، ثم سكت قليلاً وقرأ. (و) لا يرفع يديه إذ لا يُسَنَّ رَفعُ اليَدَيْنِ ) في حالتي الركوع وقيامه ودليل القائل به وجوابه في محله، ولنــا مــا رواه الطحاوي عن عبد الله عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَرْفَعُ يَدَيْهِ فِي أَوَّلِ تَكْبِيرَةٍ ثُمَّ لَا يَعُودُ ) وقد جمعت المواطن التي يسن فيها رفع اليدين في فقعس وذكرتها مبسوطة مع زيادة تعلمها
And he says tasbeeh in it three times, and keeps his belly away from his thighs and exposes his arms, then he raises his head saying takbir for rising, without leaning on the ground with his hands, and without sitting, and the second rak'ah is like the first, except that he does not recite Thana nor does he seek refuge, and raising the hands is not recommended. And he says tasbeeh in it (i.e., prostration) three times, and keeps his belly away from his thighs and exposes his arms—they are his upper arms, and 'dhab' (forearm) with sukun is not 'adud (upper arm), as stated in al-Sihah; and some say he raises them and they are two dialects as in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam. That is sunnah according to what we have related. Then he raises his head saying takbir for rising (i.e., standing for the second rak'ah) without leaning on the ground with his hands if he has no excuse, and without sitting before standing, called jalsat al-istirahah—it is sunnah according to al-Shafi'i, because the Prophet prohibited a man from leaning on his hands when rising. And from 'Ali that he said: 'It is from the sunnah, when you rise from the two rak'ahs, that you do not lean on the ground with your hands unless you cannot.' And 'Umar, 'Ali, and the Companions of the Messenger of Allah would rise in prayer on the fronts of their feet. In al-Dirayah from Sharh al-Tahawi: there is no harm in a man leaning on his hand on the ground, whether old or young, and it is the saying of the generality of scholars. And what was related from 'Ali was unique to him. In Jami' al-Nawazil: jalsat al-istirahah is makruh according to us, because what is transmitted is that the Companions would rise on the fronts of their feet. And the second rak'ah is done like the first, and you have known what it contains, except that the worshipper does not recite Thana in the second rak'ah because it is prescribed at the beginning of the worship, not during it; hence it is called supplication of opening. And he does not seek refuge because it is prescribed at the beginning of the worship to repel the whispering of the devil; it is not repeated unless the session changes, as if he sought refuge and recited, then was silent for a while and recited. And he does not raise his hands because raising hands is not recommended in the states of bowing and standing. The evidence of the one who says it and its answer are in their place. We have the hadith narrated by al-Tahawi from 'Abdullah from the Prophet that he used to raise his hands in the first takbir and then not return. And I have collected the occasions where raising hands is recommended in 'Faq'as' and mentioned them in detail with additions for you to learn.
Source pages p. 298

Commentary
This passage explains the recommended actions when rising from the second sajdah to the second rak'ah and the differences between the first and second rak'ah. The author states that the worshipper should say tasbeeh three times in prostration, keep the belly away from thighs, and expose the arms—this is sunnah based on hadith. Then, when rising to stand for the second rak'ah, he should not lean on his hands and should not perform the brief sitting called jalsat al-istirahah. The Hanafi position is that jalsat al-istirahah is makruh, contrary to the Shafi'i school. Evidence is cited from hadith and the practice of the Companions. The second rak'ah is performed like the first, except three omissions: the thana (opening supplication) is not recited because it is only at the beginning of the prayer; the ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) is not repeated; and raising the hands during bowing and standing from bowing is not sunnah. The author cites a hadith from al-Tahawi that the Prophet only raised his hands in the first takbir. The text ends with a reference to a mnemonic 'Faq'as' for the occasions where raising hands is recommended (beginning of prayer, qunut, 'Eid, etc.).

Key Terms
جلسة الاستراحة (jalsat al-istirāḥah): A brief sitting after the second prostration before standing for the next rak'ah.
ثناء (thanāʾ): The opening supplication (e.g., 'Subhanakallahumma...').
تعوذ (taʿawwudh): Seeking refuge in Allah from the accursed devil (e.g., 'A'udhu billahi...').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing jalsat al-istirahah (sitting briefly before standing for the next rak'ah)?
A) Sunnah mu'akkadah
B) Mubah
C) Makruh
D) Wajib

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school emphasizes rising without leaning and without sitting, and restricts thana, ta'awwudh, and raising hands to the first rak'ah only.

Rising from Sujood: No Leaning, No Sitting
Rulings on sujood and standing for second rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on leaning on hands when rising from sujood and distinguish it from the Shafi'i position on jalsat al-istirahah.

Core Idea
Rise from sujood without leaning on your hands — the Hanafi school holds this as sunnah, but leaning is makruh tanzih.

In this lesson, we examine a detailed passage from Imdad al-Fattah that explains the sunnah actions during sujood and the proper method of standing for the second rak'ah. The text emphasizes avoiding reliance on the hands and refraining from the brief sitting known as jalsat al-istirahah. These actions are rooted in the practice of the Companions and are considered sunnah (or makruh tanzih when done unnecessarily) according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine the specific actions being ruled upon: leaning on hands when rising from sujood and the brief sitting (jalsat al-istirahah) before standing. The Hanafi ruling is that these are makruh tanzih (disliked but not sinful) unless there is an excuse.
The ruling is derived from hadith and the practice of the Companions.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: the hadith 'نهى أن يعتمد الرجل على يديه إذا نهض' (The Prophet forbade a man from leaning on his hands when rising). Also, the practice of 'Umar, 'Ali, and the Companions who rose on the fronts of their feet.
This hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) and thus yields a zanni ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Analyze how the dalil leads to the ruling: The explicit prohibition (nahy) in Hanafi usul indicates either haram or makruh. Because the hadith is ahad and the Companions’ practice is known, the ruling is makruh tanzih, not haram.
If there is an excuse (e.g., weakness), leaning becomes permissible, removing the makruh.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Identify the opposing view: Imam al-Shafi'i considers jalsat al-istirahah to be sunnah based on other hadiths. The Hanafi school disagrees and holds it is makruh.
The difference is a legitimate ikhtilaf, and the Hanafi view is mufta bihi.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Understand why the Hanafi school prefers not to lean or sit: They rely on the stronger evidence of the hadith prohibition and the consistent practice of the Companions, as reported by 'Ali and others.
The tarjih is based on the combination of hadith and amal al-sahabah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسبح فيه ثلاثاً، وجافى بطنه عن فخذيه، وأبدى عضديه، ثم رفع رأسه مكبراً للنهوض، بلا اعتماد على الأرض بيديه، وبلا قعود. قال: (وسبح فيه) أي: السجود (ثلاثاً، وجافي بطنه عن فخذيه، وأبدى عضديه)، وهما ضبعاه، والضبع بسكون الباء لا غير العضد، كذا في الصحاح، وقال بعضهم يرفعها وهما لغتان كذا في مبسوط شيخ الإسلام، وذلك سنة لما روينا. (ثم رفع رأسه مكبراً للنهوض) أي: القيام للركعة الثانية (بلا اعتماد على الأرض بيديه) إن لم يكن به عذر، (وبلا قعود) قبل القيام، يسمى جلسة الاستراحة - هو سنة عند الشافعي رحمه الله - لأنه صلى الله عليه وسلم نهى أن يعتمد الرجل على يديه إذا نهض. وعن علي رضي الله عنه أنه قال: من السنة إذا انتهضت من الركعتين أن لا تعتمد على الأرض بيديك إلا أن لا تستطيع. وكان عمر وعلي وأصحاب رسول الله ينهضون في الصلاة على صدور أقدامهم. وفي الدراية عن شرح الطحاوي: لا بأس بأن يعتمد بيده على الأرض شيخاً كان أو شاباً، وهو قول عامة العلماء رحمهم الله، وما روي عن علي كان ينفرد به. وفي جمل النوازل: جلسة الاستراحة مكروهة عندنا، لأن المروي أن الصحابة كانوا ينهضون على صدور أقدامهم.
And he said 'Subhanallah' in it three times, and kept his belly away from his thighs, and exposed his upper arms. Then he raised his head saying the takbir to stand up, without leaning on the ground with his hands, and without sitting. He said: (And he said 'Subhanallah' in it) i.e., the prostration (three times, and kept his belly away from his thighs, and exposed his upper arms), which are his two forearms, and 'dhab' (forearm) with a sukun on the ba is none other than 'adud (upper arm), as in al-Sihah, and some said he raises them, and there are two dialects as in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam; that is sunnah due to what we narrated. (Then he raised his head saying takbir for rising) i.e., standing for the second rak'ah (without leaning on the ground with his hands) if there is no excuse, (and without sitting) before standing, called jalsat al-istirahah - it is sunnah according to al-Shafi'i - because the Prophet forbade a man from leaning on his hands when rising. And from 'Ali that he said: 'It is from the sunnah when you rise from the two rak'ahs that you do not lean on the ground with your hands unless you cannot.' And 'Umar, 'Ali, and the Companions of the Messenger of Allah used to rise in prayer on the fronts of their feet. And in al-Dirayah from Sharh al-Tahawi: There is no harm in leaning with his hand on the ground, whether old or young, and it is the saying of the majority of scholars. What is narrated from 'Ali was his individual view. And in Jumal al-Nawazil: Jalsat al-istirahah is disliked in our school, because it is reported that the Companions used to rise on the fronts of their feet.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn rulings on the actions in sujood and standing up. It states that saying Subhanallah three times in sujood is sunnah, as is keeping the belly away from the thighs and exposing the arms. Then it explains that when rising from sujood for the second rak'ah, one should not lean on the ground with their hands unless they have an excuse, and one should not sit briefly (jalsat al-istirahah) before standing. The commentary cites hadith that the Prophet forbade leaning on hands when rising and that the Companions rose on the fronts of their feet. It then discusses the difference with al-Shafi'i who considers jalsat al-istirahah a sunnah. The Hanafi position, as stated in Jumal al-Nawazil, is that it is makruh. The author also notes that leaning on hands is permissible according to some scholars, but the preferred Hanafi view is to avoid it.

Key Terms
جلسة الاستراحة (jalsat al-istirahah): A brief sitting between sujood and standing in prayer, considered sunnah by al-Shafi'i but makruh in the Hanafi school.
ضبع (dhab'): The part of the arm between the shoulder and elbow, or specifically the forearm. In this context, the arms that are exposed during sujood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on jalsat al-istirahah (the brief sitting before standing in prayer)?
A) It is sunnah
B) It is makruh
C) It is obligatory
D) It is haram

Key Takeaway
Rising from sujood without leaning on hands and without sitting briefly is the sunnah practice; leaning without excuse is makruh tanzih in the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer

Raising Hands in Prayer: Places and the Ruku' Dispute
Lists seven places for raising hands and argues against raising at ruku'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven places where raising hands is sunnah in the Hanafi school, state the Hanafi ruling on raising at ruku', and explain the inter-madhhab dispute.

Core Idea
Raising hands in prayer is sunnah in seven specific places; raising at ruku' is makruh in the Hanafi school.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah explains the Hanafi position on raising hands (raf' al-yadayn) during prayer. It enumerates seven locations where the practice is sunnah, including the opening takbir, qunut, Eid takbirs, and several Hajj rituals. The author then delves into the well-known dispute with the Shafi'i school regarding raising hands at ruku', presenting the Hanafi evidence and refuting the opposing view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
The author states that raising hands is not sunnah at ruku' and then lists the places where it is sunnah. Note the initial statement: 'And he does not raise his hands because raising the hands is not sunnah in the two states of bowing and standing.'
2
Memorize the seven places using the mnemonic Faqa's
The mnemonic uses the letters Fa (Fatih – opening takbir), Qa (Qunut – takbir of qunut in witr), 'A ('Eid – additional takbirs in Eid), and Sin (remaining places: seeing Ka'bah, touching Black Stone, standing on Safa/Marwa, standing at 'Arafah and Muzdalifah, after first and middle jamarat). Internalize this to recall the list.
The mnemonic helps distinguish these seven from other occasions where hands are not raised.
3
Understand the dispute about ruku'
Two conflicting hadiths exist: one from Ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet only raised hands at the first takbir, and another from Ibn 'Umar that he also raised at ruku'. The Hanafi school prefers Ibn Mas'ud's report due to the principle of abrogation (naskh) – earlier practices were later abrogated.
The author argues that acts like raising hands were among many practices that were initially allowed but then abrogated.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The author provides a detailed argument: since both reports are transmitted, tarjih (preference) is needed. The Hanafi position is favored because (1) the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud explicitly negates returning to raising, (2) the opposing hadith can be explained as abrogated, and (3) the Hanafi evidence is free from the possibility of being non-shar'i.
5
Apply the ruling
The final ruling is that raising hands at ruku' is makruh tanzih (disliked) but does not invalidate the prayer. The author refutes those who claim it invalidates prayer, citing the fact that if it did, it would also invalidate Eid prayers where raising is agreed upon.
Thus, a Hanafi should avoid raising at ruku', but if done, the prayer is still valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرَّكْعَةُ الثَّانية كالأولى، إلا أنَّه لا يُثْنِي ولا يتعوَّذُ، ولا يُسَنُ رَفْعُ اليدين. قال: (والرَّكْعَةُ الثَّانية) يفعل فيها (كالأولى)، وعلمت ما سملته ( إلا أنَّهُ) أي: المصلي ( لا يُثْنِي) في الركعة الثانية، لأنه شرع في أول العبادة دون أثنائها، ولهذا سمي دعاء الاستفتاح، ولا يتعوذ لأنه شرع في أول العبادة لدفع وسوسة الشيطان، فلا يتكرر إلا بتبدل المجلس، كما لو تعوذ وقرأ، ثم سكت قليلاً وقرأ. (و) لا يرفع يديه إذ لا يُسَنَّ رفع اليدين في حالتي الركوع وقيامه ودليل القائل به وجوابه في محله، ولنا ما رواه الطحاوي عن عبد الله عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم: ( أنه كان يرفع يديه في أول تكبيرة ثم لا يعود ) وقد جمعت المواطن التي يسن فيها رفع اليدين في فقعس وذكرتها مبسوطة مع زيادة تعلمها، إلا عند افتتاح كل صلاة، وعند تكبير القنوت في الوتر، وتكبيرات الزوائد في العيدين، وحين يرى الكعبة، وحين يستلم الحجر الأسود، وحين يقوم على الصفا والمروة، وعند الوقوف بعرفة، ومزدلفة، وبعد الجمرة الأولى والوسطى. فقلت: لا يسن رفع اليدين إلا عند افتتاح كل صلاة. وعند تكبير القنوت في الوتر. وتكبيرات الزوائد في العيدين لاتفاق الأخبار والإجماع، وصفة الرفع في هذه كلها حذاء الأذنين، ويسن رفعهما مبسوطتين نحو السماء حين يرى الكعبة المشرفة أي وقت معاينتها، فتكون العين في فقعس للعيدين ومعاينة البيت المكرم، لأن الدعاء عند رؤيته مستجاب، وقد أوصى بعضهم بأن يدعو عندها باستجابة دعائه، لأنه إذا دعا بشيء مخصوص يفوت غيره، فإذا صار مجاب الدعوة كان محصلاً للمقصود في أي وقت أراده، ويسن رفعهما حين يستلم الحجر الأسود مستقبلاً بباطنهما الحجر، ويسن رفعهما مبسوطتين نحو السماء داعياً حين يقوم على الصفا وحين يقوم على المروة. ويسن كذلك عند الوقوف بعرفة، ووقوف مزدلفة. ويسن بعد رمي الجمرة الأولى والجمرة الوسطى. لما روى الطبراني بسنده عن ابن عباس عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: لا ترفع الأيدي إلا في سبع مواطن: حين يفتتح الصلاة، وحين يدخل المسجد الحرام فينظر البيت، وحين يقوم على الصفا، وحين يقوم على المروة، وحين يقف مع الناس عشية عرفة وبجمع، والمقامين حين يرمي الجمرة. وقد رواه الحاكم والبيهقي من غير أداء حصر بعدد، فيكون قرينة على عدم إرادته، فيجوز أن يزاد عليه غيره بدليل، وذكر في المبسوط والمحيط في الاستسقاء وعن أبي يوسف إن شاء رفع يديه بالدعاء، وإن شاء أشار بأصبعيه، لأن رفع اليد في الدعاء سنة انتهى. وأما الرفع عند الركوع فقد قال الكمال: اعلم أن الآثار عن الصحابة والطرق عنه كثيرة جداً، والكلام فيها واسع، والقدر المتحقق بعد ذلك كله ثبوت رواية كل من الأمرين عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام، الرفع عند الركوع وعدمه، فيحتاج إلى الترجيح لقيام المعارض، ويترجح ما صرنا إليه، بأنه قد علم أنه كانت أقوال مباحة في الصلاة وأفعال من جنس هذا الرفع، وقد علم نسخها فلا يبعد أن يكون هو أيضاً مشمولاً بالنسخ، خصوصاً وقد ثبت ما يعارضه ثبوتاً لا مرد له بخلاف عدمه فإنه لا يتطرق إليه احتمال عدم الشرعية انتهى. وفي هذا إشارة إلى رد ما قاله بعض المتأخرين من بطلان الصلاة بالرفع عند الركوع، وله رسالة في ذلك، ومما يرده لزوماً اتفاق الأئمة على رفع الأيدي في تكبيرات الزوائد، إذ لو كان الرفع مبطلاً للصلاة لأبطل صلاة العيدين، لأنه لا وجه لتخصيص إبطاله ما سوى العيدين، لكنه مكروه، كما سنذكره في باب ما يفسد الصلاة.
And the second rak'ah is like the first, except that he does not recite Thana (opening supplication) and does not seek refuge (Ta'awwudh), and raising the hands is not sunnah. He said: (And the second rak'ah) he does in it (like the first), and you know what it comprised (except that) i.e., the worshiper (does not recite Thana) in the second rak'ah, because it is prescribed at the beginning of the worship not during its middle, and therefore it is called the opening supplication; and he does not seek refuge because it is prescribed at the beginning of the worship to repel the whisper of the devil, so it is not repeated except with a change of place, as if he sought refuge and read, then paused a little and read. (And) he does not raise his hands because raising the hands is not sunnah in the two states of bowing and standing, and the proof of those who say it and its refutation are in their place. We have what al-Tahawi narrated from 'Abdullah from the Prophet that he used to raise his hands at the first takbir and then not return. And I have collected the places where raising the hands is sunnah in 'Fiqa's' and mentioned them in detail with an addition that you will learn, except at the opening of every prayer, and at the takbir of qunut in witr, and the additional takbirs in the two Eids, and when he sees the Ka'bah, and when he touches the Black Stone, and when he stands on Safa and Marwa, and at the standing at 'Arafah, Muzdalifah, and after the first and middle jamarat. So I say: It is not sunnah to raise the hands except at the opening of every prayer, and at the takbir of qunut in witr, and the additional takbirs in the two Eids, due to the agreement of reports and consensus; and the manner of raising in all these is at the earlobes. And it is sunnah to raise them spread out towards the sky when he sees the noble Ka'bah, i.e., at the time of seeing it, so the 'ayn is in Fiqa's for the two Eids and seeing the honored house, because supplication at seeing it is answered; and some have advised to supplicate for the acceptance of one's supplication, because if he prays for a specific thing, he may miss other things; so if he becomes one whose prayer is answered, he achieves his goal whenever he wishes. And it is sunnah to raise them when he touches the Black Stone, facing it with the inner sides of his hands; and it is sunnah to raise them spread out towards the sky supplicating when he stands on Safa and when he stands on Marwa; and likewise at the standing at 'Arafah and the standing at Muzdalifah; and it is sunnah after throwing the first jamrah and the middle jamrah. Because al-Tabarani narrated from Ibn 'Abbas from the Prophet that he said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places: when opening the prayer, when entering the Sacred Mosque and looking at the House, when standing on Safa, when standing on Marwa, when standing with the people on the evening of 'Arafah and at Jam' (Muzdalifah), and the two positions when throwing the jamrah.' Al-Hakim and al-Bayhaqi narrated it without exclusivity of number, so that indicates he did not intend limitation, so it is permissible to add others with evidence. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit about rain prayer, and from Abu Yusuf: If he wishes, he raises his hands in supplication, and if he wishes, he points with his fingers, because raising hands in supplication is sunnah. As for raising at bowing (ruku'), al-Kamal said: Know that the reports from the Companions and the narrations about it are very many, and the discussion about them is extensive, but the established fact after all that is the transmission of both actions from the Prophet: raising at ruku' and not raising. Therefore, a preference is needed because of the conflict; and what we adhere to is preferred, because it is known that there were permissible sayings and actions similar to this raising in prayer, and it is known that they were abrogated, so it is not far that this also is included in abrogation, especially since what opposes it is established beyond refute, unlike its absence, for the possibility of lack of legality does not apply. In this is an indication to refute what some later scholars said about the invalidation of prayer by raising at ruku', and he has a treatise on that. Among the things that refute it necessarily is the agreement of the imams on raising hands in the additional takbirs, because if raising invalidated prayer, it would invalidate the Eid prayer, for there is no basis to specify its invalidation for other than Eid prayer; but it is makruh, as we will mention in the chapter on what invalidates prayer.
Source pages p. 299

Commentary
This passage first explains that the second rak'ah is like the first except that thana' (opening supplication) and ta'awwudh (seeking refuge) are not repeated, and raising hands is not sunnah at ruku' or when rising from it. The commentator then provides a detailed list of the seven places where raising hands is sunnah: (1) opening takbir of prayer, (2) qunut takbir in witr, (3) additional takbirs in Eid, (4) when seeing the Ka'bah, (5) when touching the Black Stone, (6) when standing on Safa and Marwa, (7) at 'Arafah, Muzdalifah, and after the first and middle jamarat. The basis is a hadith from Ibn 'Abbas, albeit with some disagreement on limitation. The commentator then addresses the dispute about raising hands at ruku'. The Hanafi school, following the hadith of 'Abdullah ibn Mas'ud that the Prophet only raised hands at the first takbir, considers it not sunnah and makruh. The commentary argues that since both raising and not raising are reported, the Hanafi position is preferred because it aligns with the abrogation of previous practices. The commentator refutes the view of some later scholars that raising at ruku' invalidates prayer, noting that if it did, it would invalidate Eid prayers where raising is agreed upon. Thus, it is merely makruh.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Raising the hands during prayer; in this context, the specific act of raising to the ears or towards the sky at certain points.
فقعس (faqa's): A mnemonic device using the letters fa, qaf, 'ayn, sin to remember the places where raising hands is sunnah: Fatih (opening), Qunut, 'Eid, and then others like seeing Ka'bah etc.
القنوت (al-qunut): A special supplication recited in the witr prayer while raising hands; the takbir for qunut is one of the places where raising hands is sunnah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, how many places are considered sunnah for raising the hands, and which of the following is NOT one of them?
A) At the opening takbir of prayer
B) At the takbir for qunut in witr
C) At the bowing (ruku')
D) When seeing the Ka'bah

Key Takeaway
Raising hands is sunnah in seven specific places; at ruku' it is makruh according to the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer

Places Where Raising Hands Is Sunnah
Lists and proves places where hand-raising is sunnah, with a hadith and discussion on raising at ruku

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the specific places where raising the hands is sunnah in Hanafi fiqh and explain the Hanafi position on raising hands at ruku, including the evidence and tarjih.

Core Idea
Raising hands in prayer is limited to specific places; raising at ruku is makruh, not sunnah.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah details the locations where the Hanafi school holds that raising the hands (raf' al-yadayn) is sunnah. It provides a hadith from Ibn Abbas listing seven places, but also adds others based on evidence. The text then addresses the controversial issue of raising hands at ruku, weighing the conflicting hadiths and concluding that the practice is abrogated and thus only makruh. Understanding this ruling is important for proper prayer practice according to the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the listed places
Read through the list of places where raising hands is sunnah: at opening takbir, qunut in witr, Eid takbirs, seeing Kaaba, touching Black Stone, on Safa and Marwa, at Arafah and Muzdalifah, after first and middle jamrah. Note that the list includes both prayer and non-prayer acts.
Raising hands in prayer is part of sunnah, not fard.
2
Examine the hadith evidence
The author cites a hadith from Tabarani that restricts raising hands to seven places. However, other transmissions (Hakim, Bayhaqi) do not mention a number, allowing addition. Understand the Hanafi method of dealing with conflicting transmissions.
Hanafis use the principle that a non-restricted transmission can expand the list.
3
Analyze the ruku issue
The text discusses raising hands at ruku. Al-Kamal notes that both raising and not raising are transmitted, so tarjih (preponderance) is needed. The Hanafi view is that raising at ruku is abrogated, similar to other actions that were later prohibited in prayer.
Abrogation argument is key: since other similar actions were abrogated, this likely was too.
4
Note the intra-madhhab difference
Abu Yusuf allows raising hands in rain prayer but gives option to point with fingers. This shows some flexibility within the Hanafi school.
5
Understand the ruling and its implications
Raising hands at ruku is considered makruh, not invalidating prayer. The text refutes those who claim it nullifies prayer, citing agreement of imams on raising in Eid takbirs as a counterargument.
The final ruling: raising at ruku is makruh, not haram or invalidating.

ما يفسد الصلاة.
Except when opening every prayer, and when pronouncing the takbir of qunut in witr, and the extra takbirs in the two Eids, and when one sees the Kaaba, and when one touches the Black Stone, and when one stands on Safa and Marwa, and when standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah, and after the first and middle Jamrah. So I said: Raising hands is not sunnah except at the opening of every prayer, and when pronouncing the takbir of qunut in witr, and the extra takbirs in the two Eids – due to agreement of reports and consensus – and the manner of raising in all these is opposite the ears. (And) it is sunnah to raise them spread toward the sky when one sees the honored Kaaba, i.e., at the time of seeing it... because supplication at seeing it is answered... (And) it is sunnah to raise them when one touches the Black Stone, facing it with the inner sides of his hands. (And) it is sunnah to raise them spread toward the sky while supplicating when one stands on Safa and when one stands on Marwa. (And) it is sunnah similarly when standing at Arafah, and standing at Muzdalifah, and after throwing the first Jamrah, and the middle Jamrah – based on what al-Tabarani narrated with his chain from Ibn Abbas from the Prophet (peace be upon him) who said: 'Hands are not raised except in seven places: when opening the prayer, when entering the Sacred Mosque looking at the House, when standing on Safa, when standing on Marwa, when standing with the people on the evening of Arafah and at Jam' (Muzdalifah), and the two stations when throwing the Jamrah.' And al-Hakim and al-Bayhaqi narrated it without restricting to a number, which indicates he did not intend restriction, so it is permissible to add others based on evidence. And it is mentioned in al-Mabsut and al-Muhit regarding rain prayer: from Abu Yusuf, if he wishes he raises his hands in supplication, and if he wishes he points with his fingers, because raising hands in supplication is sunnah – end. As for raising at ruku, al-Kamal said: Know that the athar from the Companions and the ways are very many, and discussion therein is vast. But the established fact after all that is the confirmation of transmission of each of the two matters from him (peace and blessings be upon him): raising at ruku and not raising. So tarjih is needed due to the existence of mu'arid. And what we adopt is preponderant, because it is known that there were permissible sayings and actions of this type of raising in prayer, and their abrogation is known, so it is not unlikely that this also is included in abrogation, especially since what opposes it is established in an undeniable way, unlike its absence, which does not admit the possibility of lacking legitimacy – end. In this is an indication to refute what some later scholars said regarding the invalidity of prayer by raising at ruku, and he has a treatise on that. And what refutes it necessarily is the agreement of the imams on raising hands in the extra takbirs, for if raising invalidated prayer it would invalidate the prayer of the two Eids, because there is no specification of invalidation to other than the two Eids, but it is makruh, as we will mention in the chapter on what invalidates prayer.
Source pages p. 300

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Sharh of Nur al-Idah. It lists the places where raising the hands is sunnah in prayer and worship, based on a hadith from Tabarani and other sources. The list includes: opening takbir, qunut in witr, Eid takbirs, seeing the Kaaba, touching the Black Stone, standing on Safa and Marwa, standing at Arafah and Muzdalifah, and after the first and middle jamrah. The hadith mentions seven places, but since other transmissions do not restrict to seven, additional places can be added by evidence. The author then discusses the issue of raising hands at ruku, favoring the Hanafi view that it is not sunnah and that raising at ruku is makruh, refuting those who claim it invalidates prayer.

Key Terms
رفع اليدين (raf' al-yadayn): Lifting the hands to the ears or shoulders during specific acts of worship, considered sunnah in designated places.
تكبير القنوت (takbir al-qunut): The takbir said in the witr prayer before the qunut supplication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on raising hands during ruku in the Hanafi school?
A) Sunnah muakkadah
B) Makruh
C) Haram and invalidates prayer
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Raising hands is sunnah in specific places; raising at ruku is makruh, not invalidating.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Sitting Posture and Recitation of Tashahhud
Describes the sitting posture and tashahhud with its proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi sunnah sitting posture for men and women, recite the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, and explain the sunnah of pointing the index finger during the shahadah.

Core Idea
The sitting posture and tashahhud are sunnah acts affirmed by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, with pointing the finger during the shahadah.

In prayer, after the second prostration, the worshipper sits. The Hanafi school prescribes specific postures for men and women and a specific recitation. This lesson examines these rulings, the evidence from the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and the practice of pointing with the index finger. Understanding these details ensures one's prayer follows the sunnah and omitting them may require sajdah sahw.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that the sitting posture and tashahhud are sunnah acts. For men, it is iftirash (sitting on the left foot, right foot upright). For women, it is tawarruk (sitting on both feet to the right side). The tashahhud is the specific supplication recited during the sitting.
These are not pillars (arkan) or obligations (wajibat) but sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, where the Prophet (ﷺ) taught him the tashahhud. This hadith is narrated in Bukhari and Muslim. The phrase 'فليقل' (let him say) indicates a command.
Hanafis classify this as hadith ahad, but its transmission is sound (thubut qat'i).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'فليقل' indicates obligation (wujub) in principle, but Hanafis consider the tashahhud and posture as sunnah based on other evidence, including the practice of the Companions and the fact that the Prophet (ﷺ) did not command it emphatically in every prayer.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not fard or wajib.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some schools recite a different version of tashahhud (e.g., Shafi'is include 'wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuh' in the first part). There is also difference on pointing the finger; Hanafis consider it sunnah while others may not.
The Hanafi school follows the version taught by Ibn Mas'ud as the most authentic.
5
Apply the ruling practically
When sitting, assume the prescribed posture. Recite the tashahhud word for word. During 'la ilaha' raise the index finger, and lower it at 'illa Allah'. In the first sitting, do not add salawat or other prayers.
Omission of these sunan requires sajdah sahw.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند التسبيح عقب الصلوات، وإذا فرغ الرجل من سجدتي الركعة الثانية افترش رجله اليسرى، وجلس عليها ونصب يمناه، ووجه أصابعها نحو القبلة، ووضع يديه على فخذيه، وبسط أصابعه، والمرأة تتورك. وقرأ تشهد ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه. وأشار بالمسبحة في الشهادة، يرفعها عند النفي، ويضعها عند الإثبات، ولا يزيد على التشهد في القعود الأول. وهو: التحيات لله، والصلوات والطيبات، السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته، السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين، أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله، وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله. (و) يسن رفعهما مبسوطتين نحو السماء (عند) دعائه بعد فراغه من (التسبيح) والتحميد والتكبير الذي سنذكره (عقب الصلوات) كما عليه المسلمون في سائر البلدان.
And when performing tasbih after prayers. And when the man finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot and sits on it, and erects his right foot, and directs its toes toward the qibla, and places his hands on his thighs, and spreads his fingers, and the woman sits mutawarrikan. And he recites the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him). And he points with the index finger during the shahadah, raising it at negation and lowering it at affirmation. And he does not add to the tashahhud in the first sitting. And it is: 'Greetings to Allah, and prayers and good words, peace be upon you, O Prophet, and the mercy of Allah and His blessings, peace be upon us and upon the righteous servants of Allah. I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and Messenger.' (And) it is sunnah to raise them spread toward the sky (when) he supplicates after finishing the tasbih, tahmid, and takbir that we will mention (after the prayers), as the Muslims do in all lands.
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First: raising hands is sunnah when making tasbih (glorifying Allah) after the prescribed prayers. Second: the sitting posture in prayer. For men, the sunnah is iftirash: sitting on the left foot with the right foot upright and toes pointing to the qibla. For women, the sunnah is tawarruk: sitting with both feet to the right side. The tashahhud recited is that of Ibn Mas'ud, which is the most authentic according to the Hanafi school. During the shahadah, one points the index finger when saying 'la ilaha' (negation) and lowers it when saying 'illa Allah' (affirmation). In the first sitting (after two rak'ahs), one only recites the tashahhud and does not add the salawat or other prayers.

Key Terms
افتراش (iftirash): Sitting on the left foot with the right foot upright, for men in prayer.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The specific supplication recited while sitting in the prayer, bearing witness to the oneness of Allah and the prophethood of Muhammad.
المسبحة (al-musabbihah): The index finger, used for pointing during the tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the first sitting (qa'dah ula), what does the Hanafi school say about reciting the salawat (durood)?
A) It is wajib to recite it
B) It is sunnah to recite it
C) One does not add it to the tashahhud
D) One recites it if time permits

Key Takeaway
The sunnah sitting posture and tashahhud are affirmed by the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and pointing the finger during the shahadah is a sunnah practice in the Hanafi school.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings of Tashahhud: Posture, Gesture, Wording, and Concealment
Fiqh exposition of tashahhud acts with proof from hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for sitting posture, finger pointing, tashahhud wording, and concealment during the tashahhud in salah.

Core Idea
The tashahhud combines wajib recitation with sunnah actions: posture, pointing, and concealment, all anchored in the Prophet's teaching.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah details the physical and verbal acts of the tashahhud in prayer. Understanding these rulings is essential for performing salah correctly according to the Hanafi school. The text specifies different postures for men and women, the precise wording taught by Ibn Mas'ud, the gesture of the forefinger, and the sunnah of concealment. We will unpack each element and trace it back to its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
The passage covers four elements: sitting posture (iftirash/tawarruk), recitation of tashahhud, finger pointing, and concealment. Determine the hukm (wajib/sunnah) for each.
Recitation is wajib; the rest are sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud is cited. Identify its transmission (narrated by the six, deemed most authentic by Tirmidhi) and its key wording: the command 'if qa'ada ahadukum falyakul'.
The command indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
Apply the Hanafi principle that a command (amr) implies obligation (wujub). The phrase 'falyakul' is an imperative, so reciting the tashahhud is wajib.
The pointing and concealment are supported by separate hadith from Ibn Mas'ud.
4
Examine the subsidiary proofs
For sitting posture: the text describes the practice taught by the Prophet. For concealment: Ibn Mas'ud said 'It is from the sunnah to conceal the tashahhud' (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi).
These are sunnah, not wajib.
5
Note the ikhtilaf
While the Hanafi school follows Ibn Mas'ud's wording, other schools may use different versions (e.g., Ibn Abbas). The passage affirms this wording as the most authentic and widely practiced.
Ikhtilaf is legitimate; each school relies on authentic transmissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وعند التسبيح عَقِبَ الصلواتِ، وإذا فَرَغَ الرَّجُلُ من سجدتي الركعةِ الثانيةِ افْتَرَضَ رِجْلَهُ الْيُسْرَى، وجلَسَ عَلَيها ونَصَبَ يُمناهُ، ووجه أصابعها نحوَ القِبْلِةِ، ووَضَعَ يديهِ على فَخِذِيهِ، وبَسَطَ أصابعَهُ، والمرأةُ تَتَوَرك. وقرأ تَشَهدَ ابنِ مسعود رضي الله عنه. وأشار بالمُسَبِّحَةِ في الشهادة، يرفعها عند النفي، ويضعها عند الإثباتِ، ولا يَزيدُ على التشهد في القُعودِ الأول. وهو : التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ، وَالصَّلَوَاتُ والطَّيِّبَاتُ، السَّلامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، السَّلامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللَّهِ الصَّالِحِينَ، أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا اللَّهُ وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّداً عَبْدُهُ وَرَسوله.
(و) يسن رفعهما مبسوطتين نحو السماء ( عِنْدَ) دعائه بعد فراغه من (التسبيح) والتحميد والتكبير الذي سنذكره) (عقب الصلواتِ) كما عليه المسلمون في سائر البلدان. (وإذا فَرَغَ الرَّجُلُ من سجدتَي الرَّكعةِ الثَّانِيةِ: افْتَرَسَ رِجْلَهُ الْيُسْرَى، وجلَسَ عَلَيها. ونَصَبَ يُمناه، ووجه أصابعها نحو القبلة. ووَضَعَ يديهِ على فَخِذيهِ، وبَسَطَ أصابعه وجعلها منتهية إلى رأس ركبتيه كما قدمناه". والمرأةُ تَتَوَرَكُ) وقدمنا صفته (۳) ، (وَقَرَأ ) المصلي ولو كان مقتدياً (تَشَهدَ ابن مسعود) ويقصد المصلي بألفاظ التشهد معانيها مرادة له على وجه الإنشاء منه، وإن كانت على منوال حـكـايــة سـلام الله ورسوله، فكأنه يُحيي الله ورسوله ويسلم عليه وعلى نفسه وأوليائـه كـمـا سـنذكره. (وأشــار بالمُسَبِّحَةِ) من أصابع يده اليمنى ( في الشَّهَادَةِ على الصحيح، كما قدمناه ) ( يرفعها عند النَّفْـي، ويضعها عند الإثباتِ، ولا يَزيدُ على التشهد في القُعودِ (الأوّلِ لوجوب القيام إلى الركعة الثالثة، (وَهُوَ ) أي تشهد عبد الله بن مسعود كما قال: « علمني رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم التشهد كفي بين كفيـه كـمـا يعلمني السورة من القرآن» ()، فقال: إذا قعد أحدكم في الصَّلاة فليقل: (التَّحِيَّاتُ لِلَّهِ، وَالصَّلَوَاتُ والطَّيِّبَاتُ، السَّلامُ عَلَيْكَ أَيُّهَا النَّبِيُّ وَرَحْمَةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، السَّلامُ عَلَيْنَا وَعَلَى عِبَادِ اللهِ الصَّالِحِينَ) فإذا قالها أصابت كل عبد صالح في السماء والأرض، أَشْهَدُ أَنْ لا إِلَهَ إِلا اللَّهُ، وَأَشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدَاً عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُولُهُ ) ()، رواه الستة. قال الترمذي: أصح حديث عن النبي في التشهد حديث ابن مسعود، والعمل عليه عند أكثر أهل العلم من الصحابة والتابعين، وأخرج الطحاوي عــن ابـن عمـر أن أبـا بكر علمه الناس على المنبر، وإنما اخترنا رواية ابن مسعود؛ لأن فيها الأمر وأقله الاستحباب،
والألف واللام في السلام، وهما للاستغراق، وزيادة الواو، وهي لتجديد الكلام كما في القسم. وتأكيد التعليم والاتفاق عليه لفظاً ومعنى، واتفقوا على إخفائه؛ لقول ابن مسعوده « من السنة أن تُخفي التشهد » رواه أبو داود والترمذي كما في «البرهان» ، والتحيات أصلها أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما عرج به ليلة الإسراء بجسده الشريف المطهر لا بروحه فقط، لأن الإسراء تكرر، فمنه مرة بروحه، ومنــه مــرة بجسده تدلى الرفرف لمحمد حتى جلس عليه، قال ابن عادل في تفسيره : الـرفــرف مـا يجلس عليه كالبساط ونحوه. انتهى. وقال العارف بالله تعالى سيدي الشيخ عبد الوهاب الشعراني: الرفرف نظير المحفة عندنا، فقعد عليه الصلاة والسلام عليه وسلمه جبرائيل إلى الملك النازل بالرفرف، فسأله الصحبة ليأنس به فقال له جبرائيل: لا أقدر ولو خطوت خطوة احترقت، فما منا إلا لـه مقـام معلوم، وما أسرى الله بك يا محمد إلا ليريك من آياته فلا تغفل فودعه جبرائيل وانصرف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع ذلك الملك، والرفرف يمشي به إلى أن ظهر لمستوى سمع فيه صريف الأقلام، ثم زج به صلى الله عليه وسلم في النور زجة فأفرده الملك الذي كان معه وتأخر عنه، وقال أهل العلم لما تأخر جبرائيل عليه السلام عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نظر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فرأى صورة أبي بكر الصديق الله فقال: يا رب أو سبقني أبو بكر إلى هذا المقام؟ قيل له: لا ولكن لما انقطعت عن الأجناس خلقنا لك صورة تؤنسك على صورة أبي بكر، كما كان أنيسك في الغار، ثم إنه ترقى وتجرد عن الأغيار، وانفــرد لـمـا زج به [ فـي ] النور واستفرغه الحال، فأخذ يترنح ذات اليمين وذات الشمال بسبب إيقاع تلك الأقلام وصريفها في الألواح، وإعطائها من النغمات المستلذة ما أداه إلى ذلك من سريان الحال فيه، فتقوى بذلك الحال، وأعطاه الله تعالى في نفسه علماً، علم به ما لم يكن يعلمه، قيل : ذلك عن وحي من حيث لا يدري وجهته، فطلب الإذن في الرؤية مع الدخول إلى الحضرة الاختصاصية، فأمر له بالدخول فرأى عين ما علم، وما تغير عليه صفة اعتقاده، ورأى الحق عياناً، وكلمه بلا واسطة شفاهاً، وسمع كلامـه بالصفة اللائقة به، وليس هو عن صمت متقدم، ولا سكوت متوهم، إذ هو قديم أزلي ليس من جنس الحروف والهجاء والنغمة والأصوات، وأقدره الله، وقواه سبحانه بقدرته على رؤياه بعين رأسه، كما قواه على سماع خطابه، والقدرة الأزلية لا تقصر عن ذلك قال : « لما فارقني جبريل عليه السلام وانقطعتِ الأصواتُ سمعت كلام ربي وهوَ يقولُ: لِيَهْدَأَ رَوْعُكَ يا مُحَمَّد، ادْنُ ... ادْنُ... فَلَمْ يَجِدْ أَينَ
And at the time of tasbih after the prayers, and when a man finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he sits on his left foot, sits on it, and erects his right foot, and turns its toes towards the qiblah, and places his hands on his thighs, and spreads his fingers. And a woman sits cross-legged (tawarruk). And he recites the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, may Allah be pleased with him. And he points with his forefinger in the testimony, raising it at the negation and lowering it at the affirmation. And he does not add to the tashahhud in the first sitting. It is: 'At-tahiyyatu lillahi, was-salawatu wat-tayyibatu, as-salamu 'alayka ayyuha n-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, as-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi s-salihin, ashhadu alla ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh.' And it is sunnah to raise them open towards the sky at the time of supplication after finishing the tasbih, tahmid, and takbir that we will mention after the prayers, as is the practice of Muslims in all lands. And when a man finishes the two prostrations of the second rak'ah, he spreads his left foot, sits on it, erects his right foot, and turns its toes towards the qiblah, and places his hands on his thighs, and spreads his fingers, and makes them extend to the head of his knees as we previously mentioned. And a woman sits cross-legged (tawarruk), and we previously described its description. And the worshipper, even if he is a follower, recites the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, and he intends by the words of the tashahhud their meanings, as a construction from him, even if they are patterned after the narration of the greeting of Allah and His Messenger, so it is as if he greets Allah and His Messenger and sends peace upon himself and His saints, as we will mention. And he points with the forefinger of his right hand in the testimony, according to the correct view, as we previously mentioned, raising it at the negation and lowering it at the affirmation. And he does not add to the tashahhud in the first sitting due to the obligation of standing for the third rak'ah. And it is the tashahhud of Abdullah ibn Mas'ud, as he said: 'The Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, taught me the tashahhud, with my palm between his palms, just as he taught me a surah of the Quran.' He said: 'When one of you sits in prayer, let him say: At-tahiyyatu lillahi, was-salawatu wat-tayyibatu, as-salamu 'alayka ayyuha n-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu, as-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillahi s-salihin. When he says it, it reaches every righteous servant in heaven and earth. (Then) Ashhadu alla ilaha illallah, wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh.' Narrated by the six. At-Tirmidhi said: The most authentic hadith from the Prophet about the tashahhud is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud, and the practice is upon it according to most scholars from the Companions and Successors. At-Tahawi narrated from Ibn Umar that Abu Bakr taught it to the people on the pulpit. We chose the narration of Ibn Mas'ud because it contains the command, and its minimum is recommendation. And the alif and lam in 'as-salam' are for generality, and the addition of the waw is for renewing the speech as in an oath. And emphasis on teaching and agreement upon it in wording and meaning. And they agreed on concealing it because of the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'It is from the sunnah to conceal the tashahhud.' Narrated by Abu Dawud and At-Tirmidhi as in Al-Burhan. The origin of at-tahiyyat is that the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, when he was taken on the Night Journey with his noble purified body, not only with his soul, because the Isra' occurred multiple times: once with his soul, and once with his body. The rafraf descended for Muhammad until he sat on it. Ibn Adil said in his tafsir: Ar-rafraf is what one sits on like a mat or similar. End quote. And the knower of Allah, my master Sheikh Abdul Wahhab ash-Sha'rani, said: Ar-rafraf is like a litter (mahaffa) with us. So he, peace and blessings be upon him, sat on it, and Jibril handed him over to the angel descending on the rafraf. He asked for companionship to be comforted, but Jibril said: I cannot; if I take a step I would burn. 'There is none of us but has a known station.' And Allah did not cause you to ascend, O Muhammad, except to show you His signs, so do not be heedless. So Jibril bade him farewell and the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, proceeded with that angel, and the rafraf walked with him until he appeared at a level where he heard the scratching of pens. Then he was hurled into the light, and the angel who was with him left him and fell back. The scholars said: When Jibril, peace be upon him, fell back from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, the Messenger looked and saw the image of Abu Bakr as-Siddiq, may Allah be pleased with him. He said: O Lord, has Abu Bakr preceded me to this station? It was said to him: No, but when you were separated from material beings, We created for you an image to comfort you in the form of Abu Bakr, just as he was your companion in the cave. Then he ascended and was stripped of all else, and was isolated when he was hurled into the light and the state overcame him. He began to sway right and left due to the sound of those pens and their scratching on the tablets, and their giving of delightful melodies that led him to that from the flow of the state within him. He grew stronger by that state, and Allah gave him knowledge in himself by which he knew what he did not know. It is said: That was by inspiration from a direction he did not perceive. So he sought permission for vision with entry into the private presence. He was commanded to enter, and he saw exactly what he knew, and no attribute of his belief changed. He saw the Truth with clear sight, and He spoke to him without intermediary directly, and he heard His speech in a manner befitting Him, not from prior silence nor from imagined silence, for He is eternal and not of the genus of letters, letters of the alphabet, melody, or sounds. Allah enabled him and strengthened him with His power to see Him with his physical eyes, just as He strengthened him to hear His speech. The eternal power is not incapable of that. He said: 'When Jibril, peace be upon him, left me and the voices ceased, I heard the speech of my Lord, and He was saying: Let your heart be calm, O Muhammad. Draw near... draw near...' Then he did not find where...
Source pages p. 301

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) of Imdad al-Fattah on Nur al-Idah, explaining the tashahhud in the prayer. The author first quotes the matn regarding the posture after the second prostration: a man sits on his left foot (iftirash) and erects the right, while a woman sits cross-legged (tawarruk). The worshipper recites the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud, pointing with the forefinger during the testimony—raising it at the negation ('la ilaha') and lowering it at the affirmation ('illa Allah')—and does not add anything to the tashahhud in the first sitting because he must stand for the third rak'ah. The author then provides the full text of the tashahhud as taught by the Prophet to Ibn Mas'ud, and notes that according to Tirmidhi, this is the most authentic hadith on the topic and is acted upon by most scholars. The story of the Isra' is then related to explain the origin of the word 'at-tahiyyat': the Prophet was taken on the Night Journey bodily, and during his ascent he experienced the presence of Allah and heard His speech. This narrative emphasizes the spiritual significance of the tashahhud words. The passage also notes the sunnah of concealing the tashahhud (not raising the voice) based on the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. The commentator is reinforcing the Hanafi position that the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud is the preferred wording, and that the physical actions (posture, gesture) are established sunnahs.

Key Terms
التشهد (at-tashahhud): The testimony recited while sitting in prayer, consisting of the words beginning with 'At-tahiyyatu lillahi' and ending with the two shahadahs.
الافتراش (al-iftirash): Sitting on the left foot with the right foot erect, toes facing qiblah.
التورك (at-tawarruk): Sitting on the buttocks with the left foot protruding to the right and the right foot erect or similar; for women in Hanafi.
المسبحة (al-musabbihah): The forefinger (index finger) of the right hand, used for pointing during tashahhud.
التحيات (at-tahiyyat): The first word of the tashahhud, meaning all greetings, blessings, and salutations belong to Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, when does a man performing salah spread his left foot (iftirash) and sit on it?
A) After completing the two prostrations of the first rak'ah
B) After completing the two prostrations of the second rak'ah
C) After completing the final tashahhud
D) After completing the entire prayer

Key Takeaway
The tashahhud in Hanafi fiqh is wajib, performed with specific sunnah postures and gestures, and must be recited quietly using the wording of Ibn Mas'ud.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
