The Ruling and Origin of Reciting the Tashahhud Quietly
Explains the ruling, proof, and origin of the Tashahhud in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for reciting the Tashahhud quietly, cite the hadith proof, and explain the origin of the Tashahhud during the Mi'raj.

Core Idea
The Tashahhud is recited quietly as a confirmed sunnah, originating from divine inspiration during the Prophet's Mi'raj.

In this passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah, Imam al-Shurunbulali presents the legal ruling that the Tashahhud must be recited in a low voice, supported by a hadith of Ibn Mas'ud. He then narrates the miraculous origin of the Tashahhud during the Night Journey, emphasizing that the Prophet was directly inspired by Allah. Finally, he unpacks the meaning of 'al-tahiyyat' to show its comprehensive nature. This lesson will equip you with the ruling, its proof, and the rich background that elevates this prayer element.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and the precise hukm level. The act is reciting the Tashahhud in prayer; the ruling is that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) to recite it quietly.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
Find the textual evidence cited by the author. The proof is the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'It is from the sunnah to conceal the tashahhud.' This is a single-chain (ahad) hadith.
Reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
Understand how the hadith yields the ruling. The phrase 'min al-sunnah' indicates an established practice of the Prophet, and the verb 'tukhfi' commands concealment. Since the proof is not definitive (zanni), the ruling is sunnah, not fard or wajib.
4
Follow the origin narrative
Examine the story of the Mi'raj and identify the key points: the Prophet was inspired by Allah to say 'al-tahiyyatu lillah'; this refutes the idea that Jibril taught the wording directly. The author critiques alternative narrations.
This understanding resolves apparent contradictions in the sources.
5
Understand the meaning of 'al-tahiyyat'
Learn the linguistic background: 'al-tahiyyat' is the plural of 'tahiyyah', a greeting of long life derived from Arab custom. The phrase 'al-tahiyyatu lillah' directs all forms of greeting—used by various nations to honor their kings—solely to Allah, signifying complete devotion.
This combines all ways of showing honor into one phrase.

العلم لما تأخر جبرائيل عليه السلام عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم نظر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فرأى صورة أبي بكر الصديق الله فقال: يا رب أو سبقني أبو بكر إلى هذا المقام؟ قيل له: لا ولكن لما وليس هو عن صمت متقدم، ولا سكوت متوهم، إذ هو قديم أزلي ليس من جنس الحروف والهجاء والنغمة والأصوات، وأقدره الله، وقواه سبحانه بقدرته على رؤياه بعين رأسه، كما قواه على سماع خطابه، والقدرة الأزلية لا تقصر عن ذلك قال : « لما فارقني جبريل عليه السلام وانقطعتِ الأصواتُ سمعت كلام ربي وهوَ يقولُ: لِيَهْدَأَ رَوْعُكَ يا مُحَمَّد، ادْنُ ... ادْنُ... فَلَمْ يَجِدْ أَينَ يَضَعُ القَدَمَ إِلا فِي حَضْرَةِ القُدسِ وقال : التَّحِيَّاتُ اللهِ » إلخ ... وقد بسطنا الكلام على هذا في رسالة سميتها « إكرام أولي الألباب بشريف الخطاب». واعلم أني ذكرت هذا التعلم به صحة قول شارح ( المنية وغيره أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما انتهى في المعراج لمستوى سمع فيه صريف الأقلام، وقام في المقام الذي أراده الله تعالى للمخاطبة، قصد أن يُحيي ربه سبحانه، فألهمه الله تعالى أن قال: التحيات... إلخ. ولتعلم أن هذا أظهر مما قاله في «مجمع الروايات» عن تفسير الإمام أبي الليث بلغ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع جبريل إلى سدرة المنتهى وقال له جبريل: لم أتجاوز هذا الموضع، فجاوز النبي حتى بلغ ما شاء الله، فأشار إليه جبريل بأن يسلم على ربه... إلخ. لأنه لما جاوز واختفى عنه الملك النازل بالرفرف أيضاً، كيف يقال: فأشار إليه جبريل بأن يسلم، فكون السلام كان بمجرد إلهام الله تعالى إذ ذاك أظهر، انتهى. ولتعلم أيضاً ما في «معراج الدراية » : وأصل التشهد ما روى زين الأئمة الفردوسي في ثواب العبادات عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: « لما عُرِجَ بِي لَيْلَةَ المِعْرَاجِ إلى السَّمَاءِ أَمَرَنِي جبريل عليه السَّلام أنْ أسَلَّمَ عَلَى رَبِّي فقلتُ: كَيْفَ أَسَلِّمْ؟ قال: قل: التَّحِيَّاتُ الله والصلوات والطيبات. قال: فقلتُ، فَقالَ جبريل عليه السلام: السلام عليك أيها النَّبي و ورحمةُ اللهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ، فقلت: السَّلامُ عَلَيْنَا وعَلَى عِبَادِ اللهِ الصَّالِحِينَ، فقال جبريل: أشْهَدُ أنْ لا إلَهَ إِلا الله وأشْهَدُ أَنَّ مُحَمَّداً عَبْدُهُ وَرَسُولُهُ » انتهى وحيث علمت أصل التشهد فلابد من علم معناه، والمراد به ومن صدر عنه شيء منه فالصادر من النبيل بإلهام من الله قوله: التحيات الله والصلوات الطيبات التحيات: جمع تحية، من حيًّا فلان فلاناً إذا دعا له عند ملاقاته، واشتقاقها من قول العرب عند ملاقاة بعضهم بعضاً: حياك الله، أي: أبقاك، ولكل قوم تحية، لأن ملوك الأرض كانوا يحيون بتحيات مختلفة يقال لبعضهم: أبيت اللعن، ولبعضهم: اسْلَم وانعم وعش ألف سنة، إلى غير ذلك. فقيل لنا: قولوا التحيات الله أعزّ الألفاظ التي تدل على الملك ويثني بها عنه فهي الله. وعن يحيى بن علي: معنى التحية هو : الفعل والقول الذي يحيي به العبد سيده فيظهر بكلامه وفعله عبودية نفسه والتعظيم لمولاه، وأجناس التحيات مختلفة هيآتها، متفاوتة صفاتها، فمنه: تحية العجم السجود، ومنهم: من ينحني بقامته، ومنهم من يضع يديه على صدره، ومنهم من يقول بلسانه أنعم صباحاً عش ألف نيروز وألف مهرجان، فأمر العبد أن يجمع هذا، فيقول: التحيات الله وبه تقول رأي زين
And the alif and lam in 'al-salam' are for generality, and the addition of the waw is for renewing speech as in the oath. And confirming the teaching and agreement upon it in wording and meaning, and they agreed upon concealing it (reciting quietly) due to the saying of Ibn Mas'ud: 'It is from the Sunnah to conceal the tashahhud' reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi as in al-Burhan. The origin of al-tahiyyat is that when the Prophet was taken on the night journey with his noble purified body, not only his soul, because the journey was repeated, once with his soul and once with his body, al-rafraf was lowered for Muhammad until he sat upon it. Ibn Adil said in his tafsir: al-rafraf is what one sits on like a carpet etc. And the knower of Allah, my master Sheikh Abd al-Wahhab al-Sharani said: al-rafraf is like a sedan chair, so he sat upon it and Jibril handed him over to the angel descending with al-rafraf, he asked for companionship to feel at ease, but Jibril said: I cannot, if I take a step I would burn, 'None of us has a station known' (Quran 37:164), and Allah did not take you O Muhammad except to show you His signs, so do not be heedless. Then Jibril bid farewell and the Prophet went with that angel, and al-rafraf walked with him until he appeared at a level where he heard the scraping of pens, then he was thrust into the light, so the angel with him left him and withdrew. The scholars said: when Jibril withdrew from the Messenger, he looked and saw the image of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq, and said: O Lord, has Abu Bakr preceded me to this station? It was said: No, but when you were separated from physical kinds, We created for you an image to comfort you in the form of Abu Bakr, just as he was your companion in the cave. Then he ascended and was stripped of otherness, and became alone when he was thrust into the light, and the state overwhelmed him, so he began to sway right and left due to the striking of those pens and their scraping upon the tablets, and the pleasant melodies they produced led him to that state. He became strong with that state, and Allah gave him knowledge in himself by which he knew what he did not know; it is said that was by revelation without knowing its direction. He asked permission to see and enter the special presence, and was ordered to enter, so he saw the essence of what he knew, and his belief was not changed, and he saw the Truth with his own eyes, and He spoke to him without intermediary, and he heard His speech in the manner befitting Him, not from prior silence or imagined silence, for He is eternal and not of the type of letters, sounds, or melodies. Allah empowered him to see Him with his head's eye, just as He empowered him to hear His address, and eternal power is not incapable of that. He said: 'When Jibril left me and the sounds ceased, I heard the speech of my Lord saying: Let your heart be calm, O Muhammad, draw near... draw near... and he could not place his foot except in the Holy Presence, and He said: 'Al-tahiyyatu lillah' etc. And we have elaborated on this in a treatise called 'Ikram uli al-albab bi-sharif al-khitab'. Know that I mentioned this teaching to confirm the correctness of the statement of the commentator of al-Munyah and others that when the Prophet reached in the ascension the level where he heard the scraping of pens, and stood in the station Allah intended for address, he intended to greet his Lord, so Allah inspired him to say 'al-tahiyyat...' etc. And know that this is more apparent than what is said in Majma' al-riwayat from the tafsir of Imam Abu al-Layth: the Prophet reached with Jibril to Sidrat al-muntaha and Jibril said: I have not passed this place, so the Prophet passed until he reached what Allah willed, and Jibril gestured to him to greet his Lord... etc. Because when he passed and the angel descending with al-rafraf also disappeared from him, how can it be said: Jibril gestured to him to greet? So the greeting being solely by Allah's inspiration at that time is more apparent. And also know what is in Mi'raj al-dirayah: The origin of the tashahhud is what Zayn al-a'imma al-Firdawsi narrated in Thawab al-ibadat from the Prophet: 'When I was taken on the night journey to heaven, Jibril ordered me to greet my Lord, I said: How should I greet? He said: Say: al-tahiyyatu lillah wa al-salawatu wa al-tayyibat.' He said: I said, then Jibril said: 'al-salamu alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuhu', so I said: 'al-salamu alayna wa ala ibadillahi al-salihin', then Jibril said: 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illallah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan abduhu wa rasuluhu'. End. Now that you know the origin of the tashahhud, you must know its meaning, and what was uttered by the Prophet was by inspiration from Allah: 'al-tahiyyatu lillah wa al-salawatu al-tayyibat'. Al-tahiyyat is plural of tahiyyah, from hayya fulan fulanan when he prays for him at meeting, derived from the Arabs' saying when meeting each other: hayyaka Allah, meaning may Allah keep you alive. Every nation has a greeting, because the kings of the earth were greeted with different greetings: some were said 'abayta al-la'na', others 'aslam wa an'am wa ish alfa sanah', etc. So it was said to us: say 'al-tahiyyatu lillah'—the most honored words that indicate sovereignty. And from Yahya ibn Ali: The meaning of tahiyyah is the action and statement by which the slave greets his master, showing his servitude and veneration. The types of greetings differ in form and character: some bow, some prostrate, some put hands on chest, some say 'good morning, live a thousand norooz and a thousand mihrajan'. So the slave was commanded to combine all this and say: 'al-tahiyyatu lillah'. And by this it is said...
Source pages p. 302

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Nur al-Idah discusses the ruling of reciting the Tashahhud quietly in prayer, its origin during the Mi'raj, and the meaning of its words. The author begins by confirming the agreement of scholars that the Tashahhud is to be recited in a low voice (ikhfa'), citing the hadith of Ibn Mas'ud: 'It is from the Sunnah to conceal the tashahhud' (reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi). This establishes the ruling as sunnah, not obligatory, but nonetheless a confirmed practice. The author then narrates the story of the Mi'raj, emphasizing that the Prophet recited the Tashahhud after being inspired by Allah, not taught by Jibril directly. He critiques a narration in Majma' al-riwayat that suggests Jibril gestured to the Prophet, arguing that it is more plausible that Allah inspired him directly. He also cites a hadith from Mi'raj al-dirayah where Jibril teaches the wording, but this is reconciled as the Prophet learning the words while the inspiration was from Allah. Finally, he explains the meaning of 'al-tahiyyat': it is a plural of tahiyyah, meaning a greeting of continuing life, derived from the Arab custom. The phrase 'al-tahiyyatu lillah' combines all forms of greeting used by different nations, directing them solely to Allah. This demonstrates the comprehensive worship of Allah through the Tashahhud.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of 'al-tahiyyatu lillah...' in prayer, also known as al-tahiyyat.
إخفاء (ikhfa'): Reciting in a low voice, audible only to oneself, as opposed to jahr (audible).
التحيات (al-tahiyyat): Plural of tahiyyah; all forms of greetings and expressions of sovereignty, directed to Allah in the tashahhud.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling (hukm) regarding reciting the Tashahhud in prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It must be recited loudly (jahr).
B) It is a confirmed sunnah to recite it quietly (ikhfa).
C) It is fard to recite it audibly.
D) It is mustahab to recite it in a moderate voice.

Key Takeaway
The Tashahhud is recited quietly as a confirmed sunnah, originating from Allah's direct inspiration to the Prophet during the Mi'raj, with the word 'al-tahiyyat' combining all forms of greeting for Allah.

Origin and Meaning of the Tashahhud in the Mi'raj
Explains the revealed origin of Tashahhud and defines its key terms

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the revealed origin of the tashahhud and define the three key phrases (tahiyyat, salawat, tayyibat) as acts of worship.

Core Idea
The tashahhud is a divinely inspired greeting comprising verbal, bodily, and financial worship.

In the Mi'raj, the Prophet ﷺ was taught the words of the tashahhud directly by divine inspiration. This lesson unpacks the origin of this crucial prayer element and clarifies the meaning of each phrase, showing how they correspond to Allah's response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of the tashahhud
Contrast the two narrations: one says Jibril gestured after Sidrat al-Muntaha, the other says direct divine inspiration (ilham). The author prefers ilham as more apparent.
The dispute is on the modality, not the revealed status.
2
Analyze the hadith from Mi'raj al-Dirayah
Read the full hadith where Jibril teaches the Prophet the phrases. Note the sequence: tahiyyat, salawat, tayyibat; then the Prophet's greeting; then the shahada.
This hadith establishes the wording of the tashahhud.
3
Define the key terms
Examine the lexical meanings of tahiyyat (verbal praise), salawat (bodily worship), and tayyibat (financial worship/good words). See how each corresponds to an act of worship.
Use the author's explanation from Gharibayn and Mustasfa.
4
Understand the correspondence with Allah's response
Notice how Allah responds to each phrase: salam matches tahiyyat, rahma matches salawat, barakat matches tayyibat. The singular/plural forms reflect the unity or multiplicity of the instruments.
This shows the tashahhud is a dialogue.
5
Appreciate the Prophet's extension to others
After receiving the greeting, the Prophet includes all righteous servants by saying 'al-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillah al-salihin'.
This reflects the Prophet's generosity.

واعلم أني ذكرت هذا التشهد بصحة قول شارح المنية وغيره أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما انتهى في المعراج لمستوى سمع فيه صريف الأقلام، وقام في المقام الذي أراده الله تعالى للمخاطبة، قصد أن يحيي ربه سبحانه، فألهمه الله تعالى أن قال: التحيات... إلخ. ولتعلم أن هذا أظهر مما قاله في «مجمع الروايات» عن تفسير الإمام أبي الليث: بلغ النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم مع جبريل إلى سدرة المنتهى وقال له جبريل: لم أتجاوز هذا الموضع، فجاوز النبي حتى بلغ ما شاء الله، فأشار إليه جبريل بأن يسلم على ربه... إلخ. لأنه لما جاوز واختفى عنه الملك النازل بالرفرف أيضاً، كيف يقال: فأشار إليه جبريل بأن يسلم، فكون السلام كان بمجرد إلهام الله تعالى إذ ذاك أظهر، انتهى. ولتعلم أيضاً ما في «معراج الدراية»: وأصل التشهد ما روى زين الأئمة الفردوسي في ثواب العبادات عن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قال: «لما عرج بي ليلة المعراج إلى السماء أمرني جبريل عليه السلام أن أسلم على ربي فقلت: كيف أسلم؟ قال: قل: التحيات لله والصلوات والطيبات. قال: فقلت، فقال جبريل عليه السلام: السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته، فقلت: السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين، فقال جبريل: أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله». انتهى. وحيث علمت أصل التشهد فلابد من علم معناه، والمراد به ومن صدر عنه شيء منه فالصادر من النبي بإلهام من الله قوله: التحيات لله والصلوات الطيبات. التحيات: جمع تحية، من حيا فلان فلاناً إذا دعا له عند ملاقاته، واشتقاقها من قول العرب عند ملاقاة بعضهم بعضاً: حياك الله، أي: أبقاك، ولكل قوم تحية، لأن ملوك الأرض كانوا يحيون بتحيات مختلفة يقال لبعضهم: أبيت اللعن، ولبعضهم: اسلم وانعم وعش ألف سنة، إلى غير ذلك. فقيل لنا: قولوا التحيات لله أعز الألفاظ التي تدل على الملك ويثني بها عنه فهي الله. وعن يحيى بن علي: معنى التحية هو: الفعل والقول الذي يحيي به العبد سيده فيظهر بكلامه وفعله عبودية نفسه والتعظيم لمولاه، وأجناس التحيات مختلفة هيآتها، متفاوتة صفاتها، فمنه: تحية العجم السجود، ومنهم: من ينحني بقامته، ومنهم من يضع يديه على صدره، ومنهم من يقول بلسانه أنعم صباحاً، عش ألف نيروز وألف مهرجان، فأمر العبد أن يجمع هذا، فيقول: التحيات لله. وبه تقول رأي زين الله المشايخ: أن التحية ما يحيي به الرجل أخاه عند الملاقاة كالسلام، والمراد بالتحيات في التشهد كل ثناء حميد وكل عبادة قولية لله تعالى. وأما الصلوات فقال في «الغريبين»: قال أبو بكر: الصلوات الترحم، قال تعالى: ﴿إِنَّ اللَّهَ وَمَلائِكَتَهُ يُصَلُّونَ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ﴾ [الأحزاب:56] أي: يرحمون، وعن الأزهري نحوه، وعن ابن المبارك في قوله تعالى: ﴿أُولَئِكَ عَلَيْهِمْ صَلَوَاتٌ مِنْ رَبِّهِمْ﴾ [البقرة:157] أي: رحمات، وعن ابن الأعرابي: الصلاة من الله رحمة، ومن المخلوقين من الملائكة والجن والإنس القيام والركوع والسجود والدعاء والتسبيح، ومن الطير والهوام التسبيح. انتهى. فالمراد بالصلوات في التشهد العبادات البدنية ونحوها. وأما الطيبات فقد قال في «الغريبين»: الطيبات من الكلام مصروفات إلى الله أحسنه وأفضله. وفي «المستصفى»: الطيبات العبادات المالية. قال الله تعالى: ﴿كُلُوا مِنْ طَيِّبَاتِ مَا رَزَقْنَاكُمْ﴾ [البقرة:57]. وهذا على مثال من يدخل على عظماء الملوك، فإنه يثني ثم يخدم ثم يبذل المال، فلما قال ذلك النبي بإلهام من الله سبحانه رد الله عليه وحياه بقوله: السلام عليك أيها النبي ورحمة الله وبركاته. فقابل التحيات بالسلام الذي هو تحية الإسلام، وقابل الصلوات بالرحمة التي هي بمعناها، وقابل الطيبات بالبركات المناسبة للمال لكونها النمو والكثرة، وأفرد السلام والرحمة؛ لأن كلاً من التحيات والصلوات متحد باعتبار اتحاد آلته من اللسان والبدن، فوحد الله تعالى ما يقابله، بخلاف العبادات المالية، فإن آلتها متعددة وهو أنواع الأموال من النقود والحيوانات والنبات فجمع ما يقابلها، ثم لما أفاض الله تعالى بإنعامه على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بالثلاثة مقابل ثلاثته، والنبي أكرم خلق الله وأجودهم أعطى من هذه الكرامة لإخوانه الأنبياء والملائكة وصالح المؤمنين من الإنس والجن، فعمهم به كما شهدت به السنة الصحيحة حيث قال: «إنكم إذا قلتموها أصابت كل عبد صالح في السماء والأرض». منحهم وعمهم بالإضافة من ذلك، على ما هو مقتضى سجيته الكاملة في الكرم وشيمته التي هي أكرم الشيم، وعطف بإحسانه من ذلك عليهم فقال: «السلام علينا وعلى عباد الله الصالحين»، والعباد جمع عبد، قال بعضهم: ليس شيء أشرف من العبودية من صفات المخلوقين، ولذا وصف الله بها نبيه في مقام الامتداح والامتنان: ﴿سُبْحَانَ الَّذِي أَسْرَى بِعَبْدِهِ﴾ [الإسراء:1]، ﴿فَأَوْحَى إِلَى عَبْدِهِ مَا أَوْحَى﴾ [النجم:10]، وهي الرضى بما يفعل الرب تعالى، والعبادة ما يرضي الرب، والعبودية أقوى منها لأنها لا تسقط في العقبى بخلاف العبادة، والصالحين: جمع صالح وهو القائم بحقوق الله وحقوق العباد، ولذا وصف به الأنبياء نبينا.
Know that I have mentioned this tashahhud with the correctness of the statement of the commentator of al-Munyah and others that when the Prophet ﷺ reached during the Mi'raj a level where he heard the screeching of pens, and stood in the station that Allah intended for address, he intended to greet his Lord, so Allah inspired him to say: al-tahiyyat... etc. And know that this is more apparent than what was said in 'Majma' al-Riwayat' from the tafsir of Imam Abu al-Layth: that the Prophet ﷺ reached with Jibril to Sidrat al-Muntaha and Jibril said: I have not passed this place, so the Prophet passed until he reached what Allah willed, then Jibril gestured to him to greet his Lord... etc. Because when he passed and the angel descending with the rafraf also disappeared from him, how can it be said that Jibril gestured to him to greet? So that the greeting was by mere divine inspiration at that time is more apparent, end. And also know what is in 'Mi'raj al-Dirayah': The origin of the tashahhud is what Zayn al-A'imma al-Firdawsi narrated in Thawab al-'Ibadat from the Prophet ﷺ that he said: 'When I was taken on the night of the Mi'raj to the sky, Jibril ordered me to greet my Lord. I said: How shall I greet? He said: Say: al-tahiyyatu lillah, wal-salawatu, wal-tayyibat. He said: So I said, then Jibril said: al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuh. So I said: al-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillah al-salihin. Then Jibril said: Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah wa ashhadu anna Muhammadan 'abduhu wa rasuluh.' End. When you know the origin of the tashahhud, you must know its meaning. What is meant by it and who said something of it: what came from the Prophet by divine inspiration is his saying: al-tahiyyatu lillah, wal-salawatu, wal-tayyibat. Al-tahiyyat: plural of tahiyyah, from hayya fulanun fulanan when he prays for him upon meeting. Its derivation is from the Arabs' saying when meeting each other: hayyaka Allah, meaning: may He preserve you. Every people has a greeting, because the kings of the earth used to greet with different greetings. Some were told: 'abita al-la'na, others: islam wa an'am wa 'ish alfa sanah, etc. So it was said to us: say al-tahiyyatu lillah (the most honored words that indicate sovereignty and praise for it; it is Allah). And from Yahya bin 'Ali: the meaning of tahiyyah is the action and statement by which the servant greets his master, showing in his speech and action his servitude and glorification of his master. The kinds of greetings differ in forms and are varied in qualities. Among them: the greeting of the non-Arabs is prostration, some bow their stature, some place their hands on their chests, some say with their tongue: good morning, live a thousand Nowruz and a thousand Mihrajan. So the servant was commanded to combine this and say: al-tahiyyatu lillah. And by it say the opinion of Zayn Allah and the mashayikh: that tahiyyah is what a man greets his brother with upon meeting, like the salam. And what is meant by al-tahiyyat in the tashahhud is every praiseworthy praise and every verbal act of worship for Allah. As for al-salawat, it was said in al-Gharibayn: Abu Bakr said: al-salawat means mercy. Allah said: 'Indeed Allah and His angels send blessings upon the Prophet' [33:56], meaning: they show mercy. And similar from al-Azhari. And from Ibn al-Mubarak on His saying: 'Those are upon them blessings from their Lord' [2:157], meaning mercies. And from Ibn al-A'rabi: prayer from Allah is mercy, and from creatures – angels, jinn, and humans – is standing, bowing, prostrating, supplication, and glorification; and from birds and insects is glorification. End. So what is meant by al-salawat in the tashahhud is bodily acts of worship and the like. As for al-tayyibat, it was said in al-Gharibayn: al-tayyibat from speech are turned to Allah as the best and most excellent of it. And in al-Mustasfa: al-tayyibat are financial acts of worship. Allah said: 'Eat from the good things We have provided you' [2:57]. This is like the example of one who enters upon great kings: he praises them, then serves, then gives wealth. When the Prophet said that by divine inspiration, Allah responded and greeted him with His saying: al-salamu 'alayka ayyuha al-nabiyyu wa rahmatullahi wa barakatuh. So He made the tahiyyat correspond to the salam which is the greeting of Islam; He made the salawat correspond to mercy which is its meaning; and He made the tayyibat correspond to blessings appropriate to wealth because they are growth and abundance. He singled out salam and mercy because each of the tahiyyat and salawat is unified due to the unity of their instrument (tongue and body), so Allah unified what corresponds to them, unlike financial acts of worship whose instruments are many and are types of wealth – cash, animals, plants – so He pluralized what corresponds to them. Then when Allah bestowed these three upon the Prophet corresponding to his three, and the Prophet is the most generous of creation, he gave from this honor to his brothers the prophets, angels, and righteous believers from humans and jinn, and included them as attested by the authentic sunnah where he said: 'When you say it, it reaches every righteous servant in the heaven and earth.' He granted them and included them by adding that, according to his complete generosity and most noble character, and turned with his goodness to them and said: 'al-salamu 'alayna wa 'ala 'ibadillah al-salihin.' Al-'ibad is plural of 'abd. Some said: there is nothing nobler than servitude among the attributes of creatures; therefore Allah described His Prophet with it in praise and gratitude: 'Exalted is He who took His servant by night' [17:1]; 'Then He revealed to His servant what He revealed' [53:10]. It is contentment with what the Lord does. Al-'ibada is what pleases the Lord, and al-'ubudiyya is stronger than it because it does not fall away in the hereafter unlike 'ibada. Al-salihin: plural of salih, who fulfills the rights of Allah and the rights of people; therefore the prophets are described by it, including our Prophet.
Source pages p. 303

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from Imdad al-Fattah explaining the origin and meaning of the tashahhud recited in prayer. The author begins by affirming that the tashahhud was revealed to the Prophet ﷺ during the Mi'raj through divine inspiration (ilham) when he reached a station where he heard the pens of destiny. The author argues that this understanding is stronger than the narration in Majma' al-Riwayat which suggests Jibril gestured to the Prophet to greet his Lord after the Prophet passed Sidrat al-Muntaha. The author finds the latter problematic because Jibril could not accompany the Prophet beyond that point. Then the author cites a longer hadith from Mi'raj al-Dirayah via Zayn al-A'imma al-Firdawsi that details the exchange: the Prophet is taught to say 'al-tahiyyatu lillah, wal-salawatu, wal-tayyibat,' then Jibril responds with 'al-salamu 'alayka...', then the Prophet adds 'al-salamu 'alayna...', and Jibril concludes with the shahada. Next, the author explains the lexical meanings. 'Al-tahiyyat' (plural of tahiyya) comes from the Arab practice of saying 'hayyaka Allah' upon meeting. Various nations have different greetings — non-Arabs prostrate, bow, etc. The command is to gather all such meanings and direct them exclusively to Allah. Hence the phrase means all verbal praise and worship. 'Al-salawat' is interpreted as mercy (from Allah) or acts of worship involving the body (for creatures). In the tashahhud, it refers to bodily acts of worship like prayer. 'Al-tayyibat' refers to good words or financial worship, as in spending good wealth. The author draws a parallel with a person entering upon a king: first praise (tahiyyat), then service (salawat), then giving wealth (tayyibat). Allah's response in the tashahhud corresponds precisely: tahiyyat is met with salam, salawat with rahma, tayyibat with barakat. The singular form of salam and rahma matches the unity of the instruments (tongue and body), while the plural barakat matches the multitude of wealth types. Finally, the Prophet's addition 'salamu 'alayna...' extends the greeting to all righteous servants, showing his generosity. The passage ends with a reflection on the nobility of servitude ('ubudiyya) as a description of the Prophet.

Key Terms
التحيات (al-tahiyyat): Plural of tahiyya; all forms of praise, greetings, and verbal worship directed to Allah. Derived from the Arab greeting 'hayyaka Allah' meaning 'may Allah preserve you'.
الصلوات (al-salawat): Plural of salat; in this context, bodily acts of worship such as standing, bowing, prostrating, supplication, and glorification. Also means mercy from Allah.
الطيبات (al-tayyibat): Plural of tayyiba; good and pure things, here meaning financial acts of worship (zakat, sadaqa) and good words. In the tashahhud, it refers to all that is good and acceptable to Allah.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The declaration of faith and greeting recited in the sitting position of prayer, consisting of the words taught to the Prophet during the Mi'raj.
الإلهام (al-ilham): Divine inspiration; the means by which the Prophet received the wording of the tashahhud directly from Allah without an intermediary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the preferred explanation for the origin of the tashahhud according to this passage?
A) The Prophet composed it based on Jewish prayers
B) Jibril gestured to the Prophet after Sidrat al-Muntaha
C) The Prophet was inspired by Allah directly (ilham)
D) The sahaba compiled it after the Prophet's death

Key Takeaway
The tashahhud is a divinely revealed greeting that encapsulates the essence of worship in all its forms—verbal, bodily, and financial—and remains a central wajib in every Muslim's prayer.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
6 min
The Rulings of the Second Sitting in Prayer: Sequence and Legal Status of Acts
Statement of the sunan and actions of the second sitting in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the order of actions in the second sitting of prayer (qa'dah) and state the ruling (wajib/sunnah) for each action according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The second sitting has specific actions: tashahhud and salam are wajib; Fatiha, salawat, and dua are sunnah.

In the later rak'ahs of prayer, after completing the first two, the worshiper enters a second sitting. The Hanafi school outlines a sequence of actions, some obligatory and some recommended. This lesson unpacks that sequence, identifies the ruling for each step, and clarifies a key point: the salam is not a report of Allah's greeting but an initiated greeting from the worshiper.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts after the first two rak'ahs
From the text, list the actions in order: recitation of al-Fatiha, sitting for tashahhud, sending salawat, making dua, and giving salam. Note that the Fatiha is recited in the remaining rak'ahs before the sitting.
The Fatiha in later rak'ahs is sunnah; in the first two it is wajib.
2
Determine the legal status of each act
Use the Hanafi sources to classify each: tashahhud and salam are wajib (obligatory, omission requires compensation); reciting Fatiha, sending salawat, and making dua are sunnah (recommended, omission is valid but discouraged).
The text does not explicitly state the ruling, but from Nur al-Idah and its sharh, these are established.
3
Examine the intention (niyyah) for the salam
The passage explicitly states that the worshiper intends the salam as an initiated greeting to those present (angels and fellow worshipers), not as a narration of Allah's greeting. This is a Hanafi distinctive position.
This counters a view that the salam is a report; the difference affects whether the salam is considered an act of worship with its own meaning.
4
Understand the difference of opinion on the salam's nature
Some scholars (mentioned as 'some') consider the salam as a mere narration of Allah's greeting. The Hanafi view emphasizes that the worshiper originates the greeting, which requires intention and makes the salam a genuine act of communication.
This difference of opinion is legitimate; the Hanafi position is mufta bihi.

وقرأ الفاتحة فيما بعد الأوليين، ثم جلس وقرأ التشهد، ثم صلّى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم دعا بما يُشبِهُ القرآن والسنة، ثم سلّم يميناً ويساراً، فيقولُ: السّلام عليكم ورحمة الله، ناوياً من معه، كما تقدم.
محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة الإسراء فقالوا: مرحباً بالنبي الصالح » ) ولذا قالوا: لا ينبغي الجزم بـه فـي حـق شخص معين من غير شهادة الشارع له به، وإنما يقال: هو صالح فيما أظن، خوفاً من الشهادة بمـا ليس فيه، فلما أن قال ذلك إحساناً منه شهد أهل الملكوت الأعلى والسموات وجبريل بأن قال كل منهم: أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله. قال ابن الأنباري: اشهد ها هنا: أعلم وأبين، وهكذا قال أبو عبيدة في قوله تعالى: ﴿شَهِدَ اللَّهُ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ﴾ [آل عمران: ١٨] أن معناه بين الله وأعلم الله، وجمع بين أشرف أسمائه لذكره في مقام الامتداح وبين العبودية أشرف وصف للمخلوق، وأرقى وصف مستلزم للنبوة وهي الرسالة، وقدم العبودية على الرسالة إظهاراً لمخالفة أهل الكتابين، حيث قالوا كما أخبر عنهم الباري سبحانه بقوله عز وجل: ﴿وَقَالَتِ الْيَهُودُ عُزَيْرُ ابْنُ اللَّهِ وَقَالَتِ النَّصَارَى الْمَسِيحُ ابْنُ اللَّهِ﴾ [التوبة: ٣٠] ذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُم بِأَفْوَاهِهِمْ يُضَاهِئُونَ قَوْلَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا مِن قَبْلُ قَتَلَهُمُ اللَّهُ أَنَّىٰ يُؤْفَكُونَ.
تنبيه: قدمنا أنه يقصد المصلي إنشاء هذه الألفاظ مرادة له قاصداً معناها الموضوعة لـه مـن الله - يحيي ويسلم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى نفسه وأولياء الله، خلافاً لما قاله بعضهم: أنه حكاية سلام الله لا ابتداء سلام من المصلي.
And he recites al-Fatiha in what comes after the first two (rak'ahs), then he sits and recites al-tashahhud, then he sends blessings upon the Prophet ﷺ, then he makes supplication with what resembles the Quran and Sunnah, then he gives salam to the right and to the left, saying: 'As-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah', intending those with him, as previously mentioned.
Muhammad ﷺ on the Night of Isra, they said: 'Welcome, O righteous prophet' – thus they said: It is not appropriate to assert (righteousness) for any specific person without the Lawgiver's testimony for him; rather it is said: 'He is righteous as I think', fearing to testify to what is not in him. When he said that with his kindness, the inhabitants of the Supreme Dominion, the heavens, and Jibril witnessed, each of them saying: 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah, and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and His Messenger.' Ibn al-Anbari said: 'Ashhad' here means 'I know and I declare'; similarly, Abu Ubayda said regarding His statement: 'Allah bears witness that there is no god but Him' [Al Imran:18] that its meaning is Allah declared and made known. And He combined between His most noble names mentioning it in a context of praise, and between servitude which is the most noble attribute of the created being, and the highest attribute entailing prophethood and message. And He placed servitude before the message to show opposition to the People of the Book, as the Exalted informed about them: 'And the Jews say Ezra is the son of Allah, and the Christians say the Messiah is the son of Allah' [al-Tawba:30]. That is their statement from their mouths; they imitate the saying of those who disbelieved before; may Allah destroy them; how are they deluded?
Alert: We have previously mentioned that the praying person intends to originate these words intended by him, intending their meanings placed for him from Allah - he greets and sends peace upon the Prophet ﷺ and upon himself and upon the friends of Allah, contrary to what some said: that it is a narration of Allah's greeting, not an initiation of greeting from the worshiper.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage presents the rulings for the second sitting (qa'dah) in prayer, specifically after the first two rak'ahs (or after the first two in a four-rak'ah prayer, including Maghrib). The matn states: the worshiper recites al-Fatiha in the remaining rak'ahs, then sits (with tawarruk for men, tashahhud posture), recites the tashahhud (the version of Ibn Mas'ud as previously detailed), then sends salawat upon the Prophet, then makes a dua that resembles Qur'anic and prophetic supplications, and finally gives salam to the right then left, saying 'As-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah' with the intention of greeting those present (humans and angels). The commentary then includes a digression discussing the meaning of 'righteous' (salih) and the testimony of faith, linking to the story of the Prophet on the Night of Isra. It emphasizes that one should not positively assert that a specific person is righteous without explicit textual evidence. Finally, it includes a clarification (tanbih) that the worshiper intends to originate the words of salam and praise himself, not merely to report Allah's greeting. This is an important Hanafi view: the worshiper is actively greeting the Prophet and the righteous, not just narrating. The passage thus combines practical fiqh rulings with theological and linguistic nuances.

Key Terms
الفاتحة (al-Fatiha): The opening chapter of the Quran, recited in the third and fourth rak'ahs of prayer after the first two.
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The recitation of 'al-tahiyyatu lillahi...' during the sitting, which includes the testimony of faith.
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat ala al-nabi): Sending blessings upon the Prophet Muhammad, e.g., 'Allahumma salli ala Muhammad...'
السلام (al-salam): The greeting of peace at the end of prayer, saying 'As-salamu alaykum wa rahmatullah'.
النية (al-niyyah): Intention, specifically intending to greet those present with the salam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which action in the second sitting of prayer is wajib?
A) Sending salawat upon the Prophet
B) Making dua
C) Reciting the tashahhud
D) Reciting al-Fatiha

Key Takeaway
The second sitting of prayer has a specific sequence of actions: tashahhud and salam are wajib, while Fatiha, salawat, and dua are sunnah; moreover, the salam is an initiated greeting requiring intention.

Actions After the First Two Rak'ahs: Sequence and Status
Ruling with proof on later rak'ah actions and salam dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of actions after the first two rak'ahs in Hanafi prayer and explain the legal status of each, distinguishing sunnah from wajib, and apply the requirement of intention for the salam.

Core Idea
Reciting Fatiha, tashahhud, salawat, and du'a are sunnah; salam with intention is wajib and an initiation.

After completing the first two rak'ahs of an obligatory prayer, the Hanafi school prescribes a specific set of actions including recitation, sitting, supplication, and the concluding salam. This passage from the commentary of Nur al-Idah details these actions and clarifies an important dispute about the nature of the salam. Understanding this sequence ensures the prayer is performed correctly according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sequence of actions
List the actions mentioned in the passage in order: reciting al-Fatiha, sitting, reciting al-tashahhud, sending blessings upon the Prophet (salawat), making du'a, and giving salam to the right and left.
The sequence is for obligatory prayers after the first two rak'ahs.
2
Distinguish sunnah from wajib
Determine the legal status of each action. Reciting Fatiha, sitting, tashahhud, salawat, and du'a are sunnah. The salam is wajib (not fard). The intention (niyyah) for the salam is also wajib.
Sunnah acts do not require compensation if omitted; wajib acts require sajdah al-sahw if omitted unintentionally.
3
Analyze the dispute over the salam
The passage refutes the view that the salam is a narration (hikaya) of Allah's greeting and affirms it is an initiation (insha') by the worshipper. Identify the opposing claim and the Hanafi response.
The proof is the explicit statement: 'قدمنا أنه يقصد المصلي إنشاء هذه الألفاظ'.
4
Apply the requirement of intention
Since the salam is an initiation, the worshipper must intend the meaning of the words when saying them. Explain why intention is not needed if it were a narration.
Intention distinguishes a meaningful greeting from mere recitation.

Source Text

وقرأ الفاتحة فيما بعد الأوليين، ثم جلس وقرأ التشهد، ثم صلّى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ثم دعا بما يُشبِهُ القرآن والسنة، ثم سلّم يميناً ويساراً، فيقولُ: السّلام عليكم ورحمة الله، ناوياً من معه، كما تقدم. محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم ليلة الإسراء فقالوا: مرحباً بالنبي الصالح » ) ولذا قالوا: لا ينبغي الجزم بـه فـي حـق شخص معين من غير شهادة الشارع له به، وإنما يقال: هو صالح فيما أظن، خوفاً من الشهادة بمـا ليس فيه، فلما أن قال ذلك إحساناً منه شهد أهل الملكوت الأعلى والسموات وجبريل بأن قال كل منهم: أشهد أن لا إله إلا الله وأشهد أن محمداً عبده ورسوله. قال ابن الأنباري: اشهد ها هنا: أعلم وأبين، وهكذا قال أبو عبيدة في قوله تعالى: ﴿شَهِدَ اللهُ أَنَّهُ لَا إِلَهَ إِلَّا هُوَ ) [النعمان: ۱۸] أن معناه بين الله وأعلم الله، وجمع بين أشرف أسمائه لذكره في مقام الامتداح وبين العبودية أشرف وصف للمخلوق، وأرقى وصف مستلزم للنبوة وهي الرسالة، وقدم العبودية على الرسالة إظهاراً لمخالفة أهل الكتابين، حيث قالوا كما أخبر عنهم الباري سبحانه بقوله عز وجل: ﴿وَقَالَتِ الْيَهُودُ عُزَيْرُ ابْنُ اللهِ وَقَالَتِ النَّصَرَى الْمَسِيحُ ابْنُ اللَّهِ ذَلِكَ قَوْلُهُم بِأَفوهة يُضَاهِئُونَ قَوْلَ الَّذِينَ كَفَرُوا مِن قَبْلُ قَتَلَهُمُ اللَّهُ أَنَّ يُؤْفَكُونَ ﴾ [التوبة: ٣٠]. عنده، كأنه يحيي تنبيه: قدمنا أنه يقصد المصلي إنشاء هذه الألفاظ مرادة له قاصداً معناها الموضوعة لـه مـن الله ويسلم على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وعلى نفسه وأولياء الله، خلافاً لما قاله بعضهم: أنه حكاية سلام الله لا ابتداء سلام من المصلي. (وَقَرأ الفَاتِحَة فِيمَا بَعْدَ الركعتين (الأوليين) من الفرائض وهو شامل للمغرب، وقراءتها سنة كما تقدم (ثُمَّ جَلَسَ) مفترشاً رجـلـه اليسرى ناصبـاً اليمنـي، والمرأة تتورك وقرأ التَّشَهدَ)، أي: تشهد ابن مسعود المتقدم بيانه ( ثمَّ صلّى على سيدنا النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم) وتقدم الكلام عليها (ثُمَّ دَعَا ) ليكون مقبولاً بعد الصلاة على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم (بما يُشبه) ( القرآن والسنة، وتقدم مثاله ودليله ) ( ثم سلّم يميناً) ابتداءً (وَيَسَاراً) انتهاء، فيقولُ: السلام عليكم ورحمةُ اللهِ، ناوياً مَنْ مَعَهُ) من القوم والحفظة ( كَمَا تَقَدَّمَ) (٣) بيانه بحمد الله ومنته.
And he recites al-Fatihah in what is after the first two [rak'ahs], then he sits and recites al-Tashahhud, then he sends blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), then he makes supplication with what resembles the Quran and Sunnah, then he gives salam to the right and left, saying: 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah', intending those with him, as previously mentioned. Muhammad (peace be upon him) on the night of al-Isra' they said: 'Welcome to the righteous Prophet.' So they said: It is not appropriate to be certain about a specific person without the Lawgiver's testimony for him; rather it is said: 'He is righteous as I think', out of fear of testifying to what is not in him. When he said that out of goodwill, the inhabitants of the highest dominion and heavens and Jibril testified, each saying: 'I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and I bear witness that Muhammad is His servant and messenger.' Ibn al-Anbari said: 'Ashhad here means: I know and I clarify.' Similarly Abu Ubaydah said regarding His statement: {Allah bears witness that there is no god but He} [Al Imran: 18] that its meaning is Allah made clear and made known. He combined the most noble of His names because it is mentioned in a context of praise, and servitude is the most noble attribute for the creature, and the highest attribute entailing prophethood which is messengership. He placed servitude before messengership to show opposition to the People of the Book, as the Exalted informed about them, {And the Jews say: Ezra is the son of Allah, and the Christians say: The Messiah is the son of Allah. That is their statement from their mouths; they imitate the saying of those who disbelieved before. May Allah destroy them; how are they deluded?} [At-Tawbah: 30]. With him, as if he revives. (And he recites al-Fatihah after the first two rak'ahs of the obligatory prayers, and it includes al-Maghrib, and its recitation is sunnah as previously mentioned. (Then he sits) with his left foot laid flat and his right foot upright, and the woman sits mutawarrikan, and he recites al-Tashahhud), i.e., the tashahhud of Ibn Mas'ud previously explained. (Then he sends blessings upon our master the Prophet (peace be upon him)) and the discussion on it has preceded. (Then he makes supplication) to be accepted after sending blessings upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), (with what resembles) the Quran and Sunnah, and its example and proof have preceded. (Then he gives salam to the right) initially (and to the left) finally, saying: 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah', intending those with him from the congregation and the recording angels, (as previously explained) by the grace and favor of Allah.
Source pages p. 305

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary of Nur al-Idah, explaining the actions performed after the first two rak'ahs of an obligatory prayer. The text states that the worshipper recites Surah al-Fatihah (which is a sunnah, as it was left out in the first two rak'ahs), then sits in the tawarruk posture, recites the tashahhud (the testimony of faith attributed to Ibn Mas'ud), sends blessings upon the Prophet (salawat), makes a supplication that resembles Quranic or prophetic phrases, and finally gives the salam to the right and left, intending the congregation and the angels. The author then digresses into a discussion about the testimony of faith: the phrase 'ashhad' means to know and declare, as illustrated by the angels' testimony in the Isra' event and by Quranic usage. He clarifies that one should not assert absolute righteousness for a specific person without divine witness. The commentary refutes a mistaken view that the salam is merely a narration of Allah's greeting; rather, the worshipper initiates the greeting himself. The actions described are the sunan (recommended acts) of the later part of the prayer, following the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The testimony of faith recited in the sitting position, specifically the version of Ibn Mas'ud: 'Attahiyyatu lillahi...'
السلام (al-salam): The concluding greeting of the prayer, said to the right and left: 'Assalamu alaykum wa rahmatullah', with intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of the salam at the end of prayer?
A) It is a fard (pillar) – omitting it invalidates the prayer.
B) It is a sunnah – omitting it is permissible without compensation.
C) It is wajib – omitting it does not invalidate the prayer but requires sajdah al-sahw if unintentional.
D) It is a narration of Allah's greeting without intention.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the salam is a wajib initiation (insha') requiring intention, while the preceding actions after the first two rak'ahs (Fatiha, sitting, tashahhud, salawat, du'a) are sunnah.

Imamah is Superior to Adhan and Congregational Prayer is Sunnah Mu'akkadah
States that leading prayer is better than adhan and that congregational prayer is sunnah for men

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the superiority of imamah over adhan and identify the ruling (sunnah mu'akkadah) of congregational prayer for men, along with the primary evidence.

Core Idea
Imamah outranks adhan; congregation is sunnah mu'akkadah, near-wajib in strength.

This lesson opens the chapter on leading prayer. The text establishes two key rulings: the imam's role is superior to the call to prayer, and praying in congregation is a strongly emphasized sunnah for men. Understanding these rulings helps clarify the Hanafi hierarchy of salah-related practices.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The text gives two rulings: imamah is superior to adhan, and congregational prayer is sunnah for men. Note the hukm levels.
Imamah is a role, not an act; its superiority is a preference. Congregational prayer is a sunnah mu'akkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? For imamah's superiority: prophetic constancy (muwazabah) and practice of caliphs, plus the interpretation of 'Umar's statement. For congregation: multiple ahadith on reward and virtue.
The hadith are from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof prove the ruling? The hadith show great reward, but the Prophet's constant practice without rebuke for leaving indicates sunnah mu'akkadah, not fard. For imamah superiority, the Prophet's consistency demonstrates its higher merit.
The explicit statement of 25/27 parts reward indicates virtue, not obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Some other schools (e.g., Hanbali) consider congregational prayer fard 'ayn. The text rejects that by emphasizing it is sunnah, not fard.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is relied upon and why? The Hanafi position is mufta bihi, based on the strength of the evidence and the fact that the Prophet did not rebuke those who prayed alone occasionally.
The authority is zahir riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإمامة هي أفضلُ من الأذان. والصَّلاةُ بالجَماعةِ سنّةٌ للرّجالِ. قدمنا شيئاً يدل على فضل الأذان، وعندنا (هي)، أي: الإمامة (أفْضَلُ مِنَ الأذان) لمواظبته صلى الله عليه وسلم عليها والخلفاء الراشدين بعده، وقول عمر له : « لولا الخليفي لأذنت» (١)، لا يستلزم تفضيلـه عليـهـا بـل مراده لأذنت مع الإمامة لا مع تركها، فيفيد أن الأفضل كون الإمام هو المؤذن وهذا مذهبنا وكان عليـه أبو حنيفة رحمه الله كما يعلم من أخباره. والصَّلاةُ بالجَماعةِ سنة) في الأصح مؤكدة، شبيهة بالواجب في القوة (للرِّجَالِ) لما ذكرنا من المواظبة ولقوله : ( صَلَاةُ الْجَمَاعَةِ أَفْضَلُ مِنْ صَلَاةِ أحَدِكُمْ وَحْدَهُ بِخَمْسَةِ وَعِشْرِينَ جُزْءاً " رواه الشيخان وفي رواية: ( درجة)، وفي أخرى: «صلاة الرَّجُلِ فِي جَمَاعَةٍ تضعف عَلَى صَلاتِهِ فِي بَيْتِهِ وَفِي سُوقِهِ خَمْسَاً وَعِشْرِينَ ضِعْفَاً، وَذَلِكَ أَنَّهُ إِذَا تَوَضًا فَأَحْسَنَ الوُضُوءَ، ثُمَّ خَرَجَ إلى المَسْجِدِ لا يُخْرِجُهُ إِلا الصَّلاة، لَمْ يَخْطُ خُطْوَةً إِلا رُفِعَتْ لَهُ بِهَا دَرَجَة وحُطَّ عَنْهُ بِهَا خَطِيئَةٍ، فَإِذَا صَلَّى لَمْ تَزَلْ المَلائِكَةُ تُصَلِّي عَلَيْهِ مَا دَامَ فِي مُصَلاهُ [ مَا لَم يُحْدِث فيه ] اللهُمَّ صَلِّ عَلَيْهِ، اللّهُمَّ ارْحَمْهُ، ولا يَزَالُ أحَدُكُمْ في صَلاة ما انْتَظَرَ الصَّلاةَ ، زاد أبو داود فيه: ( فإن صَلَاهَا فِي مُصَلَاهُ فَأَتَمَّ رُكُوعَهَا وَسُجُودَهَا بَلَغَتْ خَمْسِينَ صَلاةٌ ) وقوله : « مَنْ صَلَّى العِشَاءَ فِي جَمَاعَةٍ فَكَأَنَّمَا قَامَ نِصْفَ اللَّيلِ وَمَنْ صَلَّى الصُّبْحَ فِي جَمَاعَةٍ فَكَأَنَّمَا صَلَّى اللَّيلَ ) رواه مسلم. وفي أبي داود والترمذي : ( ومَنْ صَلَّى العِشَاءَ والصُّبْحَ فِي جَمَاعَةٍ فَكَأَنَّمَا قَامَ الليل كله . ورويا وابن
Chapter of Imamah: It (imamah) is superior to the adhan. And prayer in congregation is a sunnah for men. We have previously mentioned something indicating the merit of the adhan, but according to us (imamah) is superior to the adhan because of the Prophet's (peace be upon him) constancy upon it and the rightly guided caliphs after him. And the saying of 'Umar to him: 'If not for the caliphate, I would give the adhan' does not entail preferring it over imamah; rather his intent was that he would give adhan while also being imam, not with leaving imamah. Thus it indicates that the best is that the imam be the mu'adhdhin. And this is our madhhab, and Abu Hanifah (may Allah have mercy on him) was upon it, as is known from his reports. And prayer in congregation is a sunnah, in the most sound view, strongly emphasized, resembling a wajib in strength, for men, because of the constancy we mentioned and due to his saying: 'Prayer in congregation is superior to the prayer of one of you alone by twenty-seven parts' - narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. And in one narration: 'degrees'. And in another: 'A man's prayer in congregation is twenty-five times more excellent than his prayer in his house and in his market; that is because when he performs wudu' and does it well, then goes out to the mosque, nothing drives him out except the prayer, he does not take a step without being raised a degree by it and a sin being erased from him. Then when he prays, the angels continue to send blessings upon him as long as he is in his prayer place, as long as he does not break wudu', saying: 'O Allah, bless him; O Allah, have mercy on him.' And one of you remains in prayer as long as he waits for the prayer.' Abu Dawud added: 'If he prays in his prayer place and completes its ruku' and sujud, it reaches fifty prayers.' And his saying: 'Whoever prays 'Isha' in congregation, it is as if he stood half the night; and whoever prays Fajr in congregation, it is as if he prayed the whole night' - narrated by Muslim. And in Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi: 'And whoever prays 'Isha' and Fajr in congregation, it is as if he stood the whole night.' And they and Ibn...
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage begins a new chapter entitled 'Imamah' (leading prayer). The primary ruling is that the position of imam (leading prayer) is superior to giving the adhan (call to prayer). This is established by the Prophet's own practice and that of the caliphs. The author addresses a potential objection from the narration that 'Umar said he would give the adhan if not for the caliphate, clarifying that 'Umar meant he would do both, not that adhan is superior. Consequently, the best practice is for the imam himself to also give the adhan. This is the explicit position of Abu Hanifah. The second ruling is that salat al-jama'ah (congregational prayer) is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), which is so strongly recommended it resembles a wajib (obligation) in strength, though it is not actually fard. This applies to men. Evidence is provided in the form of several hadith: the reward for congregation is multiplied by 27 or 25 times; the virtues of walking to the mosque, the angels' prayers, and the reward of standing the night for 'Isha' and Fajr prayers. These hadith, mainly from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Tirmidhi, underscore the great merit of praying in congregation.

Key Terms
الإمامة (al-imamah): Leading the congregational prayer; the position of imam.
الأذان (al-adhan): The call to prayer.
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed by men together, led by an imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi ruling on salat al-jama'ah (congregational prayer) for men?
A) It is fard 'ayn (individual obligation).
B) It is sunnah mu'akkadah (emphasized sunnah), resembling wajib.
C) It is mubah (permissible) with no extra reward.
D) It is only for the 'Isha' and Fajr prayers.

Key Takeaway
Imamah is superior to adhan, and congregational prayer is a strongly emphasized sunnah for men, not an individual obligation.

Ruling on Congregational Prayer and Superiority of Imamah
Commentary on two rulings: superiority of imamah and ruling of congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer (sunnah mu'akkadah) and explain why the burning house hadith is interpreted as a deterrent rather than an obligation.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is an emphatic sunnah, not fard, because the Prophet's intended threat was never carried out.

This passage from Nur al-Idah discusses two related rulings: the superiority of leading prayer (imamah) over the call to prayer (adhan), and the ruling on congregational prayer itself. While the first point is settled, the second involves an important intra-madhhab discussion: is congregational prayer obligatory or merely a strongly recommended sunnah? The commentary provides extensive hadith evidence and clarifies the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two rulings
Read the matn statements: imamah is superior to adhan, and congregational prayer is a sunnah for men. Note that the commentary links them.
The superiority of imamah is established by the constant practice of the Prophet and the caliphs.
2
Examine the evidence for imamah's superiority
The author cites the story of Umar, who said he would give the adhan only if he could also lead prayer, showing that imamah is more important.
3
List the hadith proofs for congregational prayer's virtue
The commentary quotes several hadith: the 25 parts reward, the 50 prayers reward for perfect prayer, the night prayer equivalent, and the increasing reward with more worshippers.
These show great merit but not obligation.
4
Analyze the burning house hadith
The Prophet intended to burn the houses of those who missed congregational prayer but did not act. The Hanafis interpret this as a threat to emphasize importance, not as a legal command making it fard.
This is the key point of dispute with Imam Ahmad.
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon view is sunnah mu'akkadah, though some later Hanafis considered it wajib. The text uses 'fi al-ashah' (most correct) to endorse the sunnah position.
The dispute is about the legal classification, not the act's merit.

Chapter of Imamah: It is superior to the adhan. And prayer in congregation is a sunnah for men. Chapter of Imamah. We have already presented something indicating the virtue of the adhan, and according to us (it), i.e., imamah (is superior to the adhan) because of the Prophet's perseverance upon it and the rightly guided caliphs after him, and the statement of Umar to him: 'Were it not for the caliphate, I would have given the adhan' does not necessitate preferring it over it, rather his intention was 'I would have given the adhan along with imamah, not abandoning it,' so it indicates that the best is that the imam be the mu'adhdhin, and this is our madhhab, and Abu Hanifah, may Allah have mercy on him, was upon it as is known from his reports. And prayer in congregation is (a sunnah) in the most correct view, emphatically, resembling an obligation in strength (for men) because of the aforementioned perseverance and because of his statement: 'Prayer in congregation is better than the prayer of one of you alone by twenty-five parts' — narrated by the two shaykhs, and in one narration 'by twenty-five degrees,' and in another 'The prayer of a man in congregation is twenty-five times better than his prayer in his house and in his market. That is because when he performs wudu' and does it well, then goes out to the mosque driven only by the prayer, he does not take a step except that he is raised a degree and a sin erased. When he prays, the angels continue to send blessings upon him as long as he is in his prayer place [as long as he does not break his wudu], saying: O Allah, bless him; O Allah, have mercy on him. And one of you is considered in prayer as long as he awaits the prayer.' Abu Dawud added: 'If he prays in his prayer place and completes its bowing and prostrations, it reaches fifty prayers.' And his statement: 'Whoever prays Isha in congregation, it is as if he stood half the night; and whoever prays Fajr in congregation, it is as if he prayed the whole night' — narrated by Muslim. And in Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi: 'Whoever prays Isha and Fajr in congregation, it is as if he stood the whole night.' And they narrated and Ibn Majah that the Messenger of Allah said: 'A man's prayer with another man is more purifying than his prayer alone, and a man's prayer with two men is more purifying than his prayer with one man, and the more, the more beloved to Allah,' as in al-Burhan. And in al-Mudmarat, it is written in the Torah the description of the nation of Muhammad and their congregation, and that for every man in their ranks, an extra prayer is added to their prayer, meaning if they are a thousand men, each man is written a thousand prayers. And from the wisdom of its legislation is the establishment of the system of affection among the worshippers, and learning from the scholar, and it is among the characteristics of this religion. And we said: It is an emphatic sunnah in the most correct view, as a precaution against what was said that it is obligatory, and a group of shaykhs chose that due to his statement: 'I had intended to command the mu'adhdhin to give the adhan, then order a man to lead the people in prayer, then go with men carrying bundles of wood to people who do not attend the prayer and burn down their houses with fire' — narrated by the two shaykhs. And the meaning is not that they abandon prayer entirely; rather, they are absent from it, as evidenced by his statement in another narration: 'Then I would come to people who pray in their houses without any excuse and burn down their houses.' And with this, those who said it is fard 'ayn like Imam Ahmad argue. We said: He intended but did not do it, so it was a threat to manifest the rituals, not because it is fard. And it was said it is fard kifayah, which is the saying of al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi. Then congregation obtains its virtue with one person with the imam because of his statement: 'Two or more are a congregation,' even if the follower is a discerning child, a woman, or a slave, whether in the house or mosque, so if he prays in his house with his wife, his female slave, or his child, he has attained the virtue of congregation. As for Friday, it requires three or two according to them besides the imam, as we will mention. And we restricted it to men because the congregation of women is disliked as we will mention, and to their being free because the slave is occupied with the service of the master, and we restricted it to being without excuse because it is dropped by excuse as we will mention, so it is not permissible to abandon it except for an excuse. If the people of a town abandon it without excuse, they are commanded to perform it; if they accept, otherwise they are fought for it because it is among the rituals.
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on two rulings from the matn of Nur al-Idah. First, imamah (leading prayer) is superior to the adhan (call to prayer). The author argues this from the constant practice of the Prophet and the caliphs. The story of Umar saying he would give the adhan is interpreted to mean he would combine both roles, not that adhan is superior. Second, congregational prayer for men is a sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatically recommended), not obligatory. The author provides extensive hadith evidence for its great reward, including the famous hadith of 25 or 27 times reward. The hadith about burning houses is interpreted as a threat to emphasize the importance of attending congregation, not to make it fard. The author notes that some later Hanafi scholars considered it wajib, but the relied-upon position remains sunnah mu'akkadah. The passage also specifies conditions: for free men without excuse. The minimum congregation is two persons (one follower with the imam), and the follower can be a child, woman, or slave. Women's congregation is makruh. The text ends by noting that if an entire town abandons congregation without excuse, they should be fought, indicating its great significance as a sha'irah (symbol) of Islam.

Key Terms
إمامة (imāmah): Leading the congregational prayer; the position of the imam.
جماعة (jamā‘ah): Congregational prayer; praying with at least one follower behind an imam.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu’akkadah): An emphatically recommended act that the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, but is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, what is the ruling on congregational prayer for men without excuse?
A) Fard 'ayn (individual obligation)
B) Fard kifayah (communal obligation)
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah (emphatically recommended)
D) Mubah (permissible)

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer for men is an emphatic sunnah, not fard, and its great reward should motivate attendance, but missing it without excuse is not sinful in the sense of missing a fard.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

The Ruling of Congregational Prayer: Sunnah Mu'akkadah
Ruling with proof on jama'ah as sunnah mu'akkadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer, identify the primary proofs, and explain why it is classified as sunnah mu'akkadah rather than wajib or fard.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah, not obligatory—the Prophet's threat to burn houses was not carried out, proving it is not fard.

This lesson examines the Hanafi position on the ruling of jama'ah. We will study the primary proofs from hadith, the reasoning behind the sunnah mu'akkadah classification, and the counterarguments that consider it wajib or fard. By the end, you will understand why the relied-upon view is that it is highly recommended but not obligatory, and how the Hanafi school distinguishes between confirmed sunnah and wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its hukm level
The author states that jama'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) according to the most correct view. Note that this is the mufta bihi position.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Ibn Majah: 'A man's prayer with another man is more virtuous...' and the report from the Torah. Identify that this shows reward but not obligation.
The text also mentions wisdom: fostering brotherhood and learning.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith uses language of preference and increased reward, not imperative commands. This indicates recommendation, not obligation. Hanafi usul: al-amr yufidu al-wujub is not triggered here.
4
Consider the opposing proof and Hanafi response
The hadith of burning houses is used by those who argue for obligation. The Hanafi response: the Prophet only intended (hamm) but did not execute, so it is a threat to emphasize importance, not proof of fard or wajib.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf and the mufta bihi
Some Hanafis (al-Karkhi, al-Tahawi) said fard kifayah, others said wajib. The preferred view is sunnah mu'akkadah. The author also notes that jama'ah is required in the sense that abandoning it without excuse is sinful enough to warrant fighting.

الأحرار، بلا عذر. روي عن ابن ماجة أن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: « صَلاةُ الرَّجُلِ مَعَ الرَّجُلِ أَزْكَى مِنْ صَلَاتِهِ وَحْدَهُ وَصَلَاةُ الرَّجُلِ مَعَ الرَّجُلَيْنِ أَزْكَى مِنْ صَلَاتِهِ مَعَ الرَّجُلِ وَمَا زَادَ فَهُوَ أَحَبُّ إِلَى اللَّه »، كما في « البرهان»، وفي المضمرات مكتوب في التوراة صفة أمة محمد وجماعتهم وأنه بكل رجل في صفوفهم يزاد في صلاتهم صلاة يعني: إذا كانوا ألف رجل يكتب لكل رجل ألف صلاة. ومن حكمة مشروعيتها قيام نظام الألفة بين المصلين، والتعلم من العالم، وهي من خصائص هذا الدين. وقلنا: إنها سنة مؤكدة في الأصح، احترازاً عما قيل إنها واجبة، واختاره جماعة من المشايخ لقوله عليه السلام: « لَقَد هَمَمْتُ أَنْ آمُرَ بالمؤذِّن فيُؤذِّنُ ثُمَّ آمُرَ رَجُلاً فَيُصَلِّي بالنَّاسِ، ثُمَّ انْطَلِقُ مَعي برجال معهم حزم الحطب، إلى قوم يَشْهَدُونَ الصَّلاة، فأحرق عليهم بيوتهم بالنَّارِ » رواه الشيخان وليس المراد ترك الصلاة أصلاً يتخلفون عن بدليل قوله في رواية أخرى: «ثُمَّ آتِي قَوْماً يُصَلُّونَ فِي بِيُوتِهِمْ لَيْسَ بِهِمْ عِلَّةٌ فأحرق عليهم» وبهذا استدل من قال: إنَّها فرض عين كالإمام أحمد، قلنا: إنـه هـم ولم يفعل، فكان تهديداً لإظهار الشعائر لا لكونها فرضاً. وقيل: فرض كفاية، وهو قول الكرخي والطحاوي، ثم الجماعة يحصل فضلها بواحد مع الإمام لقوله عليه السلام : « الاثنَانِ فما فوقهما جماعةٌ » ولو كان صبياً يعقل أو امرأة أو عبداً، سواء فيه البيت والمسجد حتى لو صلى في بيته بزوجته، أو جاريته، أو ولده، فقد أتى بفضيلة الجماعة. وأما الجمعة يشترط لها ثلاثة أو اثنان عندهما، سوى الإمام كما سنذكره ، وقيدنا بالرجال لأن جماعة النساء مكروهة كما سنذكره، وبكونهم من الأحرار لأن العبد مشغول بخدمة المولى، وقيدنا بكونهم بلا عذر لأنها تسقط به كما سنذكره، فلا يسع تركها إلا لعذر، ولو تركها أهل مصر بلا عذر يؤمرون بها، فإن قبلوا وإلا يقاتلون عليها لأنها من شعائر الإسلام
... free men, without excuse. It is narrated from Ibn Majah that the Messenger of Allah ﷺ said: 'A man's prayer with another man is more virtuous than his prayer alone, and a man's prayer with two men is more virtuous than his prayer with one man, and what is more than that is more beloved to Allah.' As mentioned in al-Burhan, and in al-Mudmarat it is written in the Torah the description of the community of Muhammad and that for every man in their rows there is added to their prayer a prayer, meaning: if they are a thousand men, for each man is written a thousand prayers. From the wisdom of its legislation is the establishment of the system of familiarity among the worshippers, and learning from the scholar, and it is among the special characteristics of this religion. And we said: It is a confirmed Sunnah according to the most correct view, as a precaution against what was said that it is obligatory, and a group of scholars chose that view due to his statement ﷺ: 'I indeed intended to order the mu'adhdhin to give the call, then order a man to lead the people in prayer, then go with men carrying bundles of wood to people who attend the prayer, and burn their houses with fire.' Narrated by al-Bukhari and Muslim. And what is meant is not abandoning prayer altogether, but those who lag behind, as evidence from another narration: 'Then I come to people who pray in their houses without any excuse and burn their houses.' And with this, those who said it is fard 'ayn, like Imam Ahmad, argued. We say: He intended and did not do it, so it was a threat to manifest the rituals, not that it is fard. And it was said: fard kifayah, which is the saying of al-Karkhi and al-Tahawi. Then the virtue of congregation is attained by one with the imam due to his statement ﷺ: 'Two and above are a congregation.' Even if it is a child who understands, or a woman, or a slave, whether in the house or the mosque, so that if he prays in his house with his wife, or his female servant, or his child, he has attained the virtue of congregation. As for Friday, three or two, according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), besides the imam is required, as we will mention. And we restricted it to men because women's congregation is disliked, as we will mention, and to free men because the slave is occupied with the master's service, and we restricted it to being without an excuse because it is dropped by it, as we will mention, so it is not permissible to leave it except for an excuse, and if the people of a city leave it without an excuse, they are commanded to do it, and if they accept, otherwise they are fought for it because it is among the rituals of Islam.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on congregational prayer (jama'ah) from a Hanafi perspective. The author begins by affirming the virtue of jama'ah with a hadith from Ibn Majah, then discusses its wisdom and the fact that it is a sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah) in the most correct view. He distinguishes this from the opinion that it is wajib (obligatory) or fard (fard 'ayn or fard kifayah). The proof against wajib is the hadith of the Prophet's intention to burn houses—since he did not carry it out, it shows it is not fard but rather a threat to emphasize its importance. The author then explains that the reward of jama'ah is attained with just one follower, including a child, woman, or slave, and that it applies in both mosque and home. However, for Friday prayer, a higher number is required. The restriction to free men is because slaves are busy with their master's service, and women's congregation is disliked. The ruling concludes that jama'ah is not to be abandoned without an excuse, and if the people of a city abandon it, they are to be fought as it is a ritual of Islam.

Key Terms
جماعة (jama'ah): Congregational prayer; praying together with an imam.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah; an act the Prophet consistently performed and strongly recommended but not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the relied-upon Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer (jama'ah) for free men without excuse?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Fard kifayah
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah mu'akkadah) in the Hanafi school, supported by hadiths on reward and the Prophet's unexecuted threat.

Six Conditions for the Validity of Imamate
Lists and explains six conditions for the imam's validity in leading prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five conditions listed in this passage (Islam, puberty, reason, masculinity, reading ability) and explain the reasoning behind each, along with the implicit sixth condition of justice.

Core Idea
The imam must be Muslim, adult, sane, male, able to recite one verse, and of upright character.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains the conditions that must be present in the imam for congregational prayer to be valid. While the author lists five conditions explicitly, the sixth condition of 'adalah' (justice) is implied by the context. Understanding these conditions helps ensure the prayer leader is qualified, preserving the validity of the congregation's prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
List the conditions as mentioned in the text. The passage explicitly lists five: Islam, puberty, reason, masculinity, and reading ability. The sixth (justice) is implied through discussions on disbelief and sin.
The sixth condition is not explicitly numbered but is derived from the requirement that the imam be a just Muslim.
2
Understand the proof for each condition
For each condition, note the evidence provided: Quran, hadith, or reasoning. For example, puberty is proven by the hadith 'no boy who is not obligated by hudud should lead prayer.'
The proofs are dalil naqli (textual) for the first five; the sixth is based on the principle that a fasiq's testimony is rejected.
3
Analyze the exceptions and special rulings
Study the rulings on cases where the imam later admits disbelief or impurity. The text distinguishes between an imam who admits a known condition and one who may have been unaware.
4
Recognize the missing condition
Observe that the text lists five conditions but does not number the sixth. From the discussion on rejecting imams who deny basic beliefs, we infer that justice (adalah) is required.
Justice is a condition in all four Sunni schools; Hanafis treat it as a condition for the imam to be preferred.
5
Apply the conditions in practice
When selecting an imam, check each condition. If any condition is clearly missing, the prayer behind such an imam must be repeated if discovered.
