⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شروط صحة الإمامة للرّجالِ الأصحاء ستة أشياء: الإسلام، والبلوغ، والعقل، والذكورة، والقراءة. (الشرط الأول: الإسلام) وهو شرط لصحة كل عبادة، فلا يصح الاقتداء بكافر سواء علم به أو لم يعلم كمن يقول بعدم البعث، أو ينكر خلافة الصديق، أو صحبته، أو يسب الشيخين، أو ينكر الإسراء من مكة إلى بيت المقدس، أو ينكر الشفاعة، أو الرؤية، أو عذاب القبر، أو وجود الكرام الكاتبين، فإذا تبين له ذلك لزمه إعادة ما صلاه خلفه. وإذا أمهم زماناً ثم قال: إنه كان كافراً، أو مع نجاسة مانعة، أو بلا طهارة، ليس عليهم إعادة لأن خبره غير مقبول في الديانات لفسقه باعترافه، بخلاف ما إذا صلى ثم تبين له ساد صلاته بنجاسة، أو عدم طهارة، فإنه قد يغفل عن ذلك فيظن الطهارة، فافترق حاله عن حال الماجن الذي لا يبالي بما يصنع، فإذا قاله على وجه التورع والاحتياط كان مقبولاً فلزم الإعادة. (و) الثاني: (البلوغ) لما روي عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه: «لا يؤم الغلام الذي لا يجب عليه الحدود»، وعن ابن عباس: «لا يؤم الغلام حتى يحتلم»، وإنما قالاه بعدما علماه من النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، فلا يصح الاقتداء بالصبي في فرض ونفل. أما الفرض فلأنه متنفل ولا يبني القوي على الضعيف، وأما النفل: لأن نفل البالغ مضمون بالإفساد، بخلاف نفل الصبي لعدم إلزامه به فلا يصح الاقتداء به في الصلوات على المختار. قال عليه السلام: «الإمام ضامن» والصبي لا يصلح لضمان هذه العبادة العظيمة، وقيل: يصح الاقتداء به في التراويح والسنن المطلقة. (و) الثالث: (العقل) فلا يصح إمامة المعتوه والمجنون؛ لعدم أهليته بانعدام عقله، وهو شرط صحة التصرفات والالتزام، وكذا لا تصح صلاة السكران فلا يصح الاقتداء به. (و) الرابع: (الذكورة) فلا يصح اقتداء الرجل بالمرأة لقوله عليه السلام: «أخروهن من حيث أخرهن الله» يعني: في الصلاة، وهو نهي عن الصلاة خلفها وإلى جانبها، والخنثى كالمرأة للرجل والخنثى مثله. (و) الخامس: (القراءة) أي: حفظ ما تصح به الصلاة على الخلاف وهو آية عند الإمام، أو ثلاث آيات عندهما، كما تقدم، فلا يصح اقتداء القارئ بالأمي
Conditions for the validity of imamate for healthy men are six things: Islam, puberty, reason, masculinity, and reading ability. (First condition: Islam) and it is a condition for the validity of every act of worship, so it is not valid to follow a disbeliever whether one knows it or not, such as one who denies the resurrection, or denies the caliphate of al-Siddiq, or his companionship, or insults the two shaykhs (Abu Bakr and Umar), or denies the Isra from Mecca to Jerusalem, or denies intercession, or seeing Allah, or the punishment of the grave, or the existence of the noble scribes. So if it becomes clear to him, he must repeat what he prayed behind him. And if he led them for a time and then said that he was a disbeliever, or with an invalidating impurity, or without purification, they are not required to repeat because his report is not accepted in religious matters due to his transgression by his own admission, unlike the case where he prayed and then it becomes clear to him that his prayer was impure or without purification, because he may have been unaware of that and thought he was pure, so his case is different from the case of a reckless person who does not care about what he does. So if he says it out of piety and caution, it is accepted and repetition is required. (Second: Puberty) because of what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud: 'A boy who is not obligated by the hudud should not lead prayer,' and from Ibn Abbas: 'A boy should not lead prayer until he reaches puberty.' And they said this after they had learned it from the Prophet, so it is not valid to follow a boy in obligatory or supererogatory prayer. As for obligatory, because he is performing supererogatory and the strong cannot be built on the weak. As for supererogatory: because the supererogatory of an adult is guaranteed against corruption, unlike the supererogatory of a boy because he is not obligated, so following him in prayers is not valid according to the chosen view. The Prophet said: 'The imam is a guarantor,' and a boy is not fit to guarantee this great act of worship. It was said: it is valid to follow him in tarawih and absolute supererogatory prayers. (Third: Reason) So it is not valid for an idiot or an insane person to lead prayer due to lack of capacity because of lack of reason, and it is a condition for the validity of transactions and obligations, and similarly the prayer of a drunkard is not valid, so it is not valid to follow him. (Fourth: Masculinity) So it is not valid for a man to follow a woman in prayer because of his statement: 'Put them back from where Allah has put them back,' meaning in prayer, and it is a prohibition against praying behind her and beside her, and a hermaphrodite is like a woman for a man and a hermaphrodite is like him. (Fifth: Reading ability) i.e., memorizing what suffices for prayer according to the difference: one verse according to Imam Abu Hanifa, or three verses according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), as mentioned previously, so it is not valid for a literate person to follow an illiterate person.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for the validity of imamate (leading prayer). The text begins by stating six conditions for healthy men, but only five are explicitly enumerated: Islam, puberty, reason, masculinity, and the ability to recite. The sixth condition is not clearly listed in this text but is often understood to be 'justice' (adalah). Each condition is explained with proofs and rulings. For Islam, the imam must be a Muslim; following a disbeliever invalidates the prayer. Puberty is required because a child is not fully obligated. Reason is required because an insane person lacks capacity. Masculinity is required because a woman cannot lead men in prayer. Reading ability requires the imam to know at least what is necessary for the prayer to be valid according to the Hanafi school (one verse or three verses depending on the view). The passage also discusses exceptions and related rulings, such as the case where the imam later admits to being a disbeliever or having impurity.

Key Terms
إمامة (imamah): The act of leading others in prayer as the imam.
شرط (shart): A condition required for the validity of the imamate.
الذكورة (al-dhukurah): Masculinity; the imam must be male.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it invalid for a boy to lead prayer in obligatory prayers?
A) Because the boy is not circumcised
B) Because the boy is performing supererogatory prayer while the followers are performing obligatory, and the strong cannot be built on the weak
C) Because the boy does not know how to recite
D) Because the boy is not allowed in the mosque

Key Takeaway
The imam must fulfill five explicit conditions (Islam, puberty, reason, masculinity, reading ability) and the implicit condition of justice for the congregation's prayer to be valid.

Six Conditions for Valid Imamah
Lists and explains six conditions for imamah with proofs and ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six conditions for valid imamah according to the Hanafi school and explain the proof and ikhtilaf for each condition.

Core Idea
A valid imam must be Muslim, adult, sane, male, able to recite, and free from excuses — each condition has a proof and practical effect.

This passage from Imdad al-Fattah expands on the matn of Nur al-Idah, listing six conditions necessary for a man to lead prayer. For each condition, the author provides a scriptural or rational proof and notes differences within the Hanafi school. Understanding these conditions ensures that the congregation's prayer is valid and that the imam is capable of fulfilling his role.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six conditions
Read the passage and list the six conditions: Islam, adulthood, sanity, masculinity, ability to recite, and freedom from excuses. Note any subconditions mentioned (e.g., speech defects).
The conditions are all prerequisites for the imam's prayer to be valid for others.
2
Locate the proof for each condition
For each condition, find the proof cited: hadith (e.g., Ibn Mas'ud for adulthood, 'al-imamu dhamin' for guarantee) or rational argument (e.g., the excused imam's necessity). Identify the type of evidence (Sunnah, reasoning).
Some conditions like Islam are based on general principles of worship validity.
3
Note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text mentions differences: Abu Hanifa vs. the Two Companions on the minimum recitation (one vs. three verses). Also, some permit a minor leading tarawih against the relied-upon view. Record these differences and the chosen position.
The mufta bihi is stated: one verse for recitation, no minor leading.
4
Derive practical rulings
Apply each condition to a concrete scenario: e.g., a man with chronic nosebleed cannot lead a healthy man; a lisping imam can lead only if he cannot correct despite effort. Determine the ruling for the imam's own prayer and for the followers.
The sixth condition includes both physical excuses and speech defects.

شروط صحة الإمامة للرّجالِ الأصحاء ستة أشياء: الإسلام، والبلوغ، والعقل، والذكورة، والقراءة ....... الإسلام كما في ( الاختيار». وشروط صحة الإمامة للرّجالِ الأصحاء ستة أشياء: الإسلام) وهو شرط لصحة كل عبادة، فلا يصح الاقتداء بكافر سواء علم به أو لم يعلم كمن يقول بعدم البعث، و ينكر خلافة الصديق، أو صحبته، أو يسب الشيخين ) ، أو ينكر الإسراء من مكة إلى بيت المقدس، أو ينكر الشفاعة، أو الرؤية، أو عذاب القبر، أو وجود الكرام الكاتبين، فإذا تبين له ذلك زمه إعادة ما صلاه خلفه، وإذا أمهم زماناً ثم قال: إنه كان كافراً، أو مع نجاسة مانعة، أو بلا طهارة، ليس عليهم إعادة لأن خبره غير مقبول في الديانات لفسقه باعترافه، بخلاف ما إذا صلـى فـتـبـيـن لـه ساد صلاته بنجاسة، أو عدم طهارة، فإنه قد يغفل عن ذلك فيظن الطهارة، فافترق حاله عن حال الماجن الذي لا يبالي بما يصنع، فإذا قاله على وجه التورع والاحتياط كان مقبولاً فلزم الإعادة. (و) الثاني: (البلوغ) لما روي عن ابن مسعود الله : ( لا يؤم الغلام الذي لا يجب عليه الحدود ) عن ابن عباس : « لا يؤم الغلام حتى يحتَلِمَ (۳) وإنما قالاه بعدما علماه من النبي، فلا الاقتداء بالصبي في فرض ونفل . أما الفرض فلأنه متنفل ولا يبني القوي على الضعيف، وأما النفل: الأن نفل البالغ مضمون بالإفساد، بخلاف نفل الصبي لعدم إلزامه به فلا يصح الاقتداء به في الصلوات على المختار. قال عليه السلام: (( الإمامُ ضامِنٌ) () والصبي لا يصلح لضمان حبـة. كيف يصح منه ضمان هذه العبادة العظيمة، وقيل: يصح الاقتداء به في التراويح والسنن المطلقة. (و) الثالث: (العَقْلُ) : فلا يصح إمامة المعتوه والمجنون؛ لعدم أهليتـه بـانعدام عقله، وهـو شــرط صحة التصرفات والالتزام، وكذا لا تصح صلاة السكران فلا يصح الاقتداء بـه. (و) الرابع: اقتداء الرجل بالمرأة لقوله : ( أَخَرُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ أَخْرَهُنَّ الله » ) يعني: في الذُّكُورَةُ ): فلا يصح ) صلاة الجماعة، وهو نهي عن لاحتمال أنوثته وذكورة المقتدي (و) الخامس (القراءةُ ): أي: حفظ مـا تـصـح بـه الصـلاة علـى الخلاف وهو آية عند الإمام، أو ثلاث آيات عندهما، كما تقدم، فلا يصح اقتداء القارئ بالأمي الصلاة خلفها وإلى جانبها، والخنثى كالمرأة للرجل والخنثى مثله، لقدرته على ركن القراءة وعجز الأمي عنه. (وَ) السادس: (السّلامة منَ الأعْدَارِ): لأن المعذور إنما صحت صلاته لضرورة عذره فلا يصح الاقتداء بغيره به فإذا كان به عذر من الأحداث (كالرعاف) الدائم، والجرح الذي لا يرقأ، وانفلات الريح، والاستحاضة، لا تصح إمامته إلا لمثله، فإن اختلـف الـعــذر لا يصح أن يكون من به سلس بول إماماً لمن به انفلات ريح؛ لزيادة الخبث على الحدث ولا من به ريح وجرح لا يرقأ لمن به سلس بول؛ لأن الإمام صاحب عذرين. وأما المقتصد : فإن كان جرحه لا يخرج منه دم فتصح إمامته للأصحاء، فكما يشترط السلامة من الرعاف ونحوه يشترط سلامة نطقه (و) هي من نحو ( الفَأْفَأَةِ) الفأفأة: هو : الذي لا يقدر على إخراج الكلمة إلا بتكرير الفاء، (والتَّمْتَمَةِ) التمتام هو : الذي لا يقدر على إخراج الكلمة إلا بعد أن يديرها في صدره كثيراً، وكذلك كل من لا يقدر على إخراج حرف من الحروف إلا بمثل ذلك. ( واللثغ) بالثاء المثلثة والتحريك وهـو : الثغـة - بضم اللام وسكون الثاء : تحرك اللسان من السين إلى الثاء، ومن الراء إلى الغين، أو إلى اللام، أو إلى الياء، أو من حرف إلى حرف، والمختار للفتوى في صلاته أنه إن كان يجتهد آناء الليل وأطراف النهار في التصحيح ولا يقدر عليه فصلاته جائزة، فما دام في طلب التصحيح ولا يطاوعه لسانه فصلاته صحيحـة كـسـائـر الشروط إذا عجز عنها، وأما إذا ترك التصحيح والجهد فصلاته فاسدة، وإنما تجوز بعجزه عن الإصلاح، فصارت تلك الألفاظ لغته ولسانه فكأنه قرأ القرآن بلغته فيصير بمنزلة الأمي في حق تصحيح الحروف التي عجز عنها، فلا يجوز الاقتداء به، وإنما تجوز صلاته مع قراءة تلك الحروف إذا لم يقدر على ما تجوز به الصلاة، مما ليس فيه تلك الحروف؛ لأن جوازها مع تلك الحروف ضروري، فينـعــدم بــانعدام الضرورة بقدرته على ما ليست فيه بما تجوز به الصلاة، هذا هو الذي عليه الاعتماد، فلذا شرطنا السلامة مما ذكرناه (و) السلامة من (فَقْدِ شرطٍ كَطَهَارَةٍ) من خبث، فإن الذي به نجاسة مانعة إنمـا صحت صلاته لعجزه فلا يصح . إمامته للطاهر منها. (و) كذا حكم (سَتْرِ عورةٍ لأن فوات شرط الستر في حــق الـعــاري ضروري، فلا تصح إمامته بمستور العورة.
Conditions for validity of imamah for healthy men are six things: Islam, adulthood, sanity, masculinity, ability to recite... Islam as in al-Ikhtiyar. And conditions for validity of imamah for healthy men are six things: Islam – it is a condition for the validity of every worship, so it is not valid to follow a disbeliever whether one knows it or not, like one who denies resurrection, denies the caliphate of al-Siddiq, or his companionship, or insults the two shaykhs, or denies the Isra' from Mecca to Jerusalem, or denies intercession, or the vision, or punishment of the grave, or the existence of the honorable scribes. So if it becomes clear to him, he must repeat what he prayed behind him. And if he led them for a time then said he was a disbeliever, or with a preventing impurity, or without purity, they do not have to repeat because his report is not accepted in religious matters due to his transgression by his confession, unlike if he prayed and it became clear that his prayer was invalid due to impurity or lack of purity, for he may have overlooked that thinking he was pure, so his case differs from the reckless one who does not care. So if he says it out of scrupulousness and precaution, it is accepted and repetition is necessary. (And) second: (adulthood) due to what is narrated from Ibn Mas'ud (may Allah be pleased with him): 'A young boy who is not obligated to perform the prescribed penalties should not lead the prayer.' And from Ibn 'Abbas: 'A young boy should not lead until he reaches puberty.' And they only said this after knowing it from the Prophet. So following a minor is not valid in obligatory or supererogatory prayers. As for obligatory, because he is performing supererogatory prayer and the strong is not built on the weak. And as for supererogatory, because the supererogatory prayer of an adult is guaranteed against invalidation, unlike the minor's supererogatory because he is not obligated to perform it, so it is not valid to follow him in prayers according to the chosen view. He (peace be upon him) said: 'The imam is a guarantor' and a minor is not fit to guarantee even a grain. How can he guarantee this great act of worship? And it is said: it is valid to follow him in tarawih and absolute sunnahs. (And) third: (sanity): so it is not valid for an insane or mentally deficient person to lead due to lack of eligibility due to lack of sanity, and it is a condition for validity of transactions and obligations. Similarly, the prayer of a drunk person is not valid, so it is not valid to follow him. (And) fourth: (masculinity): so it is not valid for a man to follow a woman in congregational prayer, due to his saying: 'Put them behind where Allah has put them' meaning regarding congregational prayer, and it is a prohibition due to the possibility of her femininity and the follower's masculinity. And the hermaphrodite is like a woman for a man, and the hermaphrodite is like him. (And) fifth: (ability to recite): i.e., memorizing what makes prayer valid according to the difference: one verse according to Abu Hanifa, or three verses according to the two companions, as previously mentioned. So it is not valid for a reciter to follow an illiterate person because he is able to perform the pillar of recitation while the illiterate cannot. (And) sixth: (freedom from excuses): because the excused person's prayer is only valid due to the necessity of his excuse, so it is not valid for others to follow him. So if he has an excuse from constant events (like continuous nosebleed, a wound that does not stop, leaking of wind, istihadah), his imamah is not valid except for someone like him. If the excuses differ, then one who suffers from urine incontinence cannot be imam for one who has wind leakage because the impurity is greater than the minor impurity. And neither can one with wind and a wound that does not stop be imam for one with urine incontinence because the imam has two excuses. As for the muqtadi: if his wound does not let out blood, his imamah for healthy people is valid. So just as freedom from nosebleed and the like is required, so is freedom from speech defects. As for (fafa'ah): fafa'ah is one who cannot utter a word except by repeating the letter fa'. (And tamtamah): tammam is one who cannot utter a word except after turning it over in his chest many times. And likewise anyone who cannot utter any letter except similarly. (And luthgh): luthgh is thugha – movement of the tongue from sin to tha', from ra' to ghayn, or to lam, or to ya', or from one letter to another. The chosen view for fatwa regarding his prayer is that if he strives night and day to correct it and cannot, then his prayer is permissible. As long as he seeks correction and his tongue does not obey him, his prayer is valid like other conditions when one is incapable. But if he abandons correction and effort, his prayer is invalid. It is only permissible due to his inability to correct. So those words become his language and tongue, as if he recited the Quran in his language, and he becomes like an illiterate person regarding the letters he cannot correct. So it is not permissible to follow him. His prayer is only permissible with those letters if he cannot find what is sufficient for prayer without those letters. Because the permissibility with those letters is due to necessity, and necessity ceases when he can read something without them that suffices for prayer. This is what is relied upon. Therefore we required freedom from what we mentioned. (And) freedom from (lack of a condition like purity) from filth: verily one who has a preventing impurity, his prayer is only valid due to his inability, so his imamah is not valid for one who is pure from it. (And) similarly the ruling of (covering the private parts) because the loss of the condition of covering for a naked person is due to necessity, so his imamah is not valid for one whose private parts are covered.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the six conditions for the validity of imamah (leading the congregational prayer) for healthy men, as stated in the matn of Nur al-Idah. The author expands on each condition with proofs, rational arguments, and intra-Hanafi differences. First condition: Islam. Following a disbeliever is invalid, and the imam's confession of past kufr is not accepted due to his fisk unless he is voluntarily scrupulous. Second condition: Adulthood (bulugh). The author cites hadith from Ibn Mas'ud and Ibn Abbas that a minor should not lead because he is not obligated and cannot be a guarantor. Following a minor in fard and nafl is invalid according to the chosen view, though some permit in tarawih. Third condition: Sanity (aql). The insane or intoxicated cannot lead due to lack of eligibility. Fourth condition: Masculinity (dhukura). A man cannot follow a woman because women are ordered to pray behind men. Hermaphrodite is like woman. Fifth condition: Ability to recite (qira'a). The imam must memorize at least one verse (Abu Hanifa) or three (Sahibayn) to make the prayer valid. A qari cannot follow an illiterate (ummi) because he can perform the recitation pillar while the latter cannot. Sixth condition: Freedom from excuses (salama min al-a'dhar). This includes physical excuses like chronic nosebleed, wound that doesn't stop, wind leakage, istihadah. Such an imam can only lead those with the same excuse; if excuses differ, imamah is invalid. It also includes speech defects: fafa'ah (repeating the letter fa), tamtamah (hesitating to utter words), luthgh (lisp or substitution of letters). The relied-upon opinion for such an imam's own prayer is that if he strives to correct and cannot, his prayer is valid, but he cannot lead others who can pronounce correctly. Also includes lack of a condition like purity from filth or covering the private parts if the imam is excused and the follower is not, then imamah is invalid. The passage ends by listing the next topic: conditions for iqtida'.

Key Terms
فأفأة (fa'fa'ah): Speech defect where the speaker repeats the letter fa' uncontrollably.
تمتمة (tamtamah): Speech defect where the speaker hesitates and turns words over in the chest before uttering.
لثغ (luthgh): Lisp or substitution of letters in recitation.
أمي (ummi): Illiterate person who cannot recite any portion of the Quran properly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi relied-upon view, can a man with chronic nosebleed (ru'af da'im) lead a healthy man in prayer?
A) Yes, because his prayer is valid due to necessity.
B) No, because the excused imam can only lead others with the same excuse.
C) Yes, but only if the muqtadi also has an excuse.
D) No, because any excuse invalidates imamah completely.

Key Takeaway
The six conditions ensure the imam is capable and the congregation's prayer is valid; each condition is supported by a proof from Quran or Sunnah.

The First Condition of Iqtida': Intention (Niyyah)
Lists the fourteen conditions and explains the first condition (intention) with its requirements and a Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first condition for valid iqtida' (intention), explain the requirement of muqarana (connection), and apply the relied-upon Hanafi view on the sufficiency of intention to follow.

Core Idea
Intention to follow the imam suffices even without explicit prayer intention, provided it is connected to the takbir.

This passage begins a new section on the fourteen conditions for valid iqtida' (following the imam in congregational prayer). The author lists the number as fourteen and then immediately explains the very first condition: intention (niyyah) of the follower. Understanding this condition is essential, as it sets the basis for all other conditions. We will examine what intention is required, how it must be connected to the opening takbir, and a subtle intra-Hanafi debate about its scope.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fourteen conditions
The text states that there are fourteen conditions for valid iqtida'. While only the first is explained in this passage, you should note the number and the first condition: intention.
The complete list is found elsewhere in Nur al-Idah.
2
Understand the first condition: intention
The follower (muqtadi) must have the intention to follow the imam (al-mutaba'ah) at the time of his own takbirat al-ihram. This intention can be actual (haqiqiyya) or legal (hukmiyya).
Legal conjunction means no foreign act intervenes between intention and takbir.
3
Differentiate between actual and legal conjunction
Actual conjunction: intention coincides with the takbir. Legal conjunction: intention occurs earlier but no foreign act (like talking, eating) separates them. Both are valid.
This flexibility makes it easier for followers to maintain valid intention.
4
Apply the different levels of intention
The text gives three scenarios: intending both prayer and following, intending to start the imam's prayer, or intending only to follow. All three suffice according to the most sound view.
The ashah view is that intention to follow alone suffices.
5
Locate the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Some Hanafis required explicit intention of the prayer, but the relied-upon view (al-ashah) is that intention to follow is enough. This is the mufta bihi position.
The text states: 'ولو نوى الاقتداء به لا غير الأصح أنه يجزئه'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشروط صحة الاقتداء أربعة عَشَرَ شيئاً: نِيَّهُ المقتدي المتابعة مُقارِنَةً لتحريمته، إما مقارنة حقيقية أو حكمية بأن لا يفصل بفاصل أجنبي بينهما، كما تقدم، فينوي الصلاة والمتابعة أيضاً، فإن نوى الشروع في صلاة الإمام، أو الاقتداء به في صلاته يجزئه، ولو نوى الاقتداء به لا غير الأصح أنه يجزئه كما تقدم.
And the conditions for validity of following (the imam) are fourteen things: the intention of the follower to follow in conjunction with his own takbirat al-ihram, either actual conjunction or legal conjunction by there being no extraneous separator between them, as previously mentioned. So he intends the prayer and also to follow. If he intends to commence the prayer of the imam, or to follow him in his prayer, it suffices. And if he intends only to follow, the most sound view is that it suffices, as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage begins a new section on the fourteen conditions for the validity of iqtida' (following the imam in congregational prayer). The author lists the number as fourteen, though it is approximate. He then explains the first condition: intention (niyyah) on the part of the muqtadi (follower) to follow the imam. This intention must be closely connected (muqarana) to his own takbirat al-ihram (the opening takbir). The connection can be actual (e.g., immediately before or during the takbir) or legal (i.e., no foreign act intervenes between them). The follower must intend both the prayer itself and the act of following the imam. If he intends merely to start the prayer of the imam (i.e., to enter into the same prayer as the imam) or to follow the imam, that suffices. There is a difference of opinion: if he only intends to follow (without explicitly intending the prayer), the most sound view (al-ashah) is that it suffices because the intention to follow implies the intention to pray. This is consistent with earlier discussions in Nur al-Idah.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): The act of following the imam in congregational prayer.
نِيَّة (niyyah): Intention in the heart to perform an act of worship; here specifically to follow the imam and pray.
مقارنة (muqarana): Connection or conjunction of the intention with the opening takbir.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muqtadi intends only to follow the imam without explicitly intending the prayer itself, what is the Hanafi relied-upon ruling?
A) His prayer is invalid because he must intend both.
B) It suffices because the intention to follow implies the intention to pray.
C) It is makruh but valid.
D) He must repeat the prayer after the imam.

Key Takeaway
The first condition for valid iqtida' is intention (niyyah) to follow the imam, which suffices even without specifying the prayer, provided it is connected to the takbir.

Conditions for the Imam: Excuses and Missing Conditions
States conditions for the imam: freedom from excuses and missing conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the imam regarding personal excuses and missing conditions, and explain when an excused person's imamah is valid.

Core Idea
An imam with a valid excuse cannot lead those without the same excuse — necessity does not transfer.

In this passage, the author expands on the conditions for the imam from the matn. Beyond general conditions like purity, the imam must be free from certain excusable conditions that would make his own prayer valid by necessity but prevent him from leading others. The passage also addresses speech defects and provides the relied-upon ruling for when such a person can lead.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions
The passage lists two categories: freedom from excuses (ra'af, fa'fa'ah, tamtamah, luthgh) and freedom from missing conditions (taharah, satr al-'awrah). Note what each term means.
Excuses are permanent or continuous conditions affecting purity or speech.
2
Understand the rationale
The author states that the excused person's prayer is valid only due to necessity; therefore he cannot lead someone without that excuse, as the necessity does not transfer.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) based on the principle of necessity.
3
Differentiate between same and different excuses
If the imam and follower share the same excuse (e.g., both have chronic nosebleed), imamah is valid. If excuses differ (e.g., one has wind, another urine drip), it is not valid due to differing types and degrees of impurity.
Specific examples: urine drip vs. wind, and cases with multiple excuses.
4
Analyze speech defects
For speech defects like stammering (fa'fa'ah, tamtamah) and lisp (luthgh), the permissibility depends on effort. If the person strives to correct but cannot, his prayer is valid, but he becomes like the unlettered and cannot lead others. If he abandons effort, his own prayer is invalid.
The mufta bihi position is that such a person's imamah is not valid for those without the same defect.
5
Apply to missing conditions
If the imam is missing a condition like purity or covering due to necessity (e.g., cannot find water, clothes), his own prayer is valid but he cannot lead those who fulfill the condition.
This extends the same principle: necessity is personal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والسلامة من الأعذار، كالرُّعَافِ، والفَأَفَأَةِ، والتَّمْتَمَةِ واللَّفْعِ ، وفَقَدِ شرط، كطهارة، وستر عــورة. وشروط صحة الاقتداء أربعةَ عَشَرَ شيئاً: نِيَّهُ المقتدي المتابعة مُقارِنَةً لتحريمته، . انفلات لقدرته على ركن القراءة وعجز الأمـي عنه. (وَ) السادس: (السّلامة منَ الأعْدَارِ): لأن المعذور إنما صحت صلاته لضرورة عذره فلا . اقتداء يصح ا غيره به فإذا كان به عذر من الأحداث (كالرعاف) الدائم، والجرح الذي لا يرقأ، وانفلات الريح، والاستحاضة، لا تصح إمامته إلا لمثله، فإن اختلـف الـعــذر لا يصح أن يكون من به سلس بول إماماً لمن به انفلات ريح؛ لزيادة الخبث على الحدث ولا من به ريح وجرح لا يرقأ لمن به سلس بول؛ لأن الإمام صاحب عذرين. وأما المقتصد : فإن كان جرحه لا يخرج منه دم فتصح إمامته للأصحاء، فكما يشترط السلامة من الرعاف ونحوه يشترط سلامة نطقه (و) هي من نحو ( الفَأْفَأَةِ) الفأفأة: هو : الذي لا يقدر على إخراج الكلمة إلا بتكرير الفاء، (والتَّمْتَمَةِ) التمتام هو : الذي لا يقدر على إخراج الكلمة إلا بعد أن يديرها في صدره كثيراً، وكذلك كل من لا يقدر على إخراج حرف من الحروف إلا بمثل ذلك. ( واللثغ) بالثاء المثلثة والتحريك وهـو : الثغـة - بضم اللام وسكون الثاء : تحرك اللسان من السين إلى الثاء، ومن الراء إلى الغين، أو إلى اللام، أو إلى الياء، أو من حرف إلى حرف، والمختار للفتوى في صلاته أنه إن كان يجتهد آناء الليل وأطراف النهار في التصحيح ولا يقدر عليه فصلاته جائزة، فما دام في طلب التصحيح ولا يطاوعه لسانه فصلاته صحيحـة كـسـائـر الشروط إذا عجز عنها، وأما إذا ترك التصحيح والجهد فصلاته فاسدة، وإنما تجوز بعجزه عن الإصلاح، فصارت تلك الألفاظ لغته ولسانه فكأنه قرأ القرآن بلغته فيصير بمنزلة الأمي في حق تصحيح الحروف التي عجز عنها، فلا يجوز الاقتداء به، وإنما تجوز صلاته مع قراءة تلك الحروف إذا لم يقدر على ما تجوز به الصلاة، مما ليس فيه تلك الحروف؛ لأن جوازها مع تلك الحروف ضروري، فينـعــدم بــانعدام الضرورة بقدرته على ما ليست فيه بما تجوز به الصلاة، هذا هو الذي عليه الاعتماد، فلذا شرطنا السلامة مما ذكرناه (و) السلامة من (فَقْدِ شرطٍ كَطَهَارَةٍ) من خبث، فإن الذي به نجاسة مانعة إنمـا صحت صلاته لعجزه فلا يصح . إمامته للطاهر منها. (و) كذا حكم (سَتْرِ عورةٍ لأن فوات شرط الستر في حــق الـعــاري ضروري، فلا تصح إمامته بمستور العورة
And safety from excuses, such as recurrent nosebleed, stammering (fa'fa'ah), hesitation (tamtamah), lisp (luthgh), and absence of a condition, like purification and covering the 'awrah. The conditions for the validity of following (iqtida') are fourteen things: the intention of the follower to follow concurrent with his takbir. Outflow due to his ability on the pillar of recitation and the inability of the unlettered. (And) the sixth: (safety from excuses): because the excused person's prayer is valid only due to the necessity of his excuse, so his following of others is not valid. So if he has an excuse from the hadath (like permanent nosebleed, a wound that does not stop, wind leakage, istihadah), his imamah is not valid except for one like him. If the excuse differs, it is not valid that one with urine drip be imam for one with wind leakage due to increased impurity over hadath, nor one with wind and a wound that does not stop for one with urine drip because the imam has two excuses. As for the one who is moderate: if his wound does not produce blood, his imamah for healthy people is valid. So just as safety from nosebleed and similar is required, safety of his speech is required. (And) that is like (fa'fa'ah): fa'fa'ah is one who cannot utter a word except by repeating the fa. (And tamtamah): tamtam is one who cannot utter a word except after turning it around in his chest many times, and likewise everyone who cannot utter a letter except like that. (And luthgh) with the dotted tha and fatha, which is luthghah: movement of the tongue from sin to tha, and from ra to ghain, or to lam, or to ya, or from letter to letter. The chosen for fatwa regarding his prayer is that if he strives night and day to correct and cannot, then his prayer is permissible. As long as he seeks correction and his tongue does not obey, his prayer is valid like other conditions when one is incapable. But if he leaves correction and effort, his prayer is invalid. It is only permissible due to his inability to correct; those words become his language and tongue, as if he recited the Quran in his language, so he becomes like the unlettered regarding correcting letters he cannot. So it is not permissible to follow him (as imam). His prayer is only permissible with recitation of those letters if he cannot recite what would make the prayer valid without those letters, because its permissibility with those letters is by necessity, and the necessity ceases when he is able to recite without them. This is what is relied upon. Therefore we required safety from what we mentioned. (And) safety from (absence of a condition like purification) from impurity: for one who has a preventing impurity, his prayer is only valid due to his incapacity, so his imamah for one free from it is not valid. (And) likewise the ruling of (covering the 'awrah) because the loss of the condition of covering for the naked is by necessity, so his imamah for one covering the 'awrah is not valid.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions for the imam regarding personal excuses and missing conditions. It is an expansion of the matn. The author states that safety from excuses is a condition, listing examples: recurrent nosebleed, stammering, hesitation, lisp. The rationale is that the excused person's prayer is only valid due to necessity, so he cannot lead someone without that excuse. If the excuse differs, e.g., urine drip vs. wind leakage, the imamah is not valid. For speech defects, the relied-upon position is that if the person strives to correct but cannot, his prayer is valid and he is like the unlettered; he cannot lead others. Similarly, one missing a condition like purity or covering cannot lead those who fulfill it.

Key Terms
فأفأة (fa'fa'ah): A speech impediment where one repeats the letter fa
تمتمة (tamtamah): A speech impediment where one cannot pronounce a word without hesitation
لثغ (luthgh): A speech impediment where the tongue substitutes one letter for another

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Can a person with permanent nosebleed (ra'af) lead a person with urine drip (sals al-bawl)?
A) Yes, because both have excuses
B) No, because the excuses differ in type
C) Yes, because necessity makes it permissible
D) No, because the imam must be completely free from all excuses

Key Takeaway
An imam with a personal excuse or missing condition cannot lead those without the same excuse, as necessity does not transfer.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Fourteen Conditions for Valid Following (Iqtida')
Lists conditions for valid iqtida' with a proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the fourteen conditions for valid following in salah and apply the condition regarding the row of women with its hadith proof.

Core Idea
The follower's prayer behind an imam is invalid if any of the fourteen conditions is missing.

This passage from Nur al-Idah enumerates the conditions for valid iqtida'. These conditions ensure the congregation prayer is correct. Understanding them is crucial for every follower. The author also provides a hadith supporting one condition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Conditions
The act is iqtida' (following the imam in prayer). The passage lists approximately fourteen conditions (shurut) for its validity. Recognize that these are not exhaustive but cover the essentials.
The author says 'taqriban' (approximately).
2
Analyze the First Condition: Niyyah of the Follower
The follower must intend to follow the imam concurrent with his own takbir tahrimah. This intention can be real or virtual (no foreign interval). The text discusses variations: intending to enter the imam's prayer, intending to follow, etc. The correct view is that merely intending to follow suffices.
This condition has some ikhtilaf within the school.
3
Examine the Remaining Conditions
List the other conditions from the text: the male imam must intend to lead women, the imam's heel must be ahead, the imam must not be in a lower state (e.g., nafl behind fard), same fard, resident not leading traveler after time in four-rak'ah prayer, imam not being a masbuq, and no row of women between imam and follower.
Some conditions have exceptions; e.g., the condition about the imam's heel is for the follower's line being behind.
4
Study the Hadith Proof for the Row of Women
The condition that no row of women separate imam and follower is supported by a hadith narrated from 'Umar (marfu'). The hadith states that a river, road, or row of women between them invalidates the following. This is a dalil naqli (textual proof).
The hadith is zanni in thubut and dalala.
5
Apply the Conditions to a Scenario
Consider a scenario: a man joins a prayer behind an imam, but there is a row of women between them. According to the hadith and the condition, his following is invalid. Identify which condition is violated and state the ruling.
The prayer itself may be valid individually, but the congregational following is invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشروط صحة الاقتداء أربعة عشر شيئاً:) تقريباً لا حصراً حقيقياً، فيشترط (نِيَّةُ المُقتدي المتابعة مُقارنةً لتحريمته، إما مقارنة حقيقية أو حكمية بأن لا يفصل بفاصل أجنبي بينهما، كما تقدم، فينوي الصلاة والمتابعة أيضاً، فإن نوى الشروع في صلاة الإمام، أو الاقتداء به في صلاته يجزئه، ولو نوى الاقتداء به لا غير الأصح أنه يجزئه كما تقدم. ولية الرجلِ الإمامةَ شرط لصحة اقتداءِ النِّساءِ به، وتَقَدَّمُ الإمام بِعَقِبِهِ عن المأموم، وأن لا يكون أدنى حالاً من المأموم، وأن لا يكون الإمام مصلياً فرضاً غير فرضِهِ، ولا يكونَ مُقيماً لمسافر، بعد الوقتِ في رباعية. ولا مسبوقاً. وأن لا يَفْصل بين الإمام والمأموم صفٌ منَ النّساءِ..
(And the conditions for validity of following are fourteen things:) approximately, not strictly exhaustive. So it is required (the intention of the follower to follow concurrent with his takbir, either real or virtual concurrency, such that no foreign interval separates them, as previously. So he intends the prayer and the following as well. If he intends to enter into the imam's prayer, or to follow him in his prayer, it suffices. If he intends nothing other than to follow him, the correct view is that it suffices, as previously. The male's intention of imamah is a condition for the validity of women following him. And the imam's heel being ahead of the follower. And that he not be in a lower state than the follower. And that the imam not be praying a different fard than that of the follower. And that he not be a resident leading a traveler after the time in a four-rak'ah prayer. And not be a masbuq. And that no row of women separate between the imam and the follower.
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage enumerates and explains the conditions for the validity of a follower's prayer behind an imam according to the Hanafi school. The author states there are approximately fourteen conditions. The first mentioned is the follower's intention to follow, concurrent with his own takbir tahrimah. Other conditions discussed include: the male imam must intend to lead women, the imam's heel should be ahead of the follower, the imam must not be in a lower state (e.g., a nafl prayer behind a fard payer), the imam and follower must be praying the same fard prayer, a resident cannot lead a traveler after the time in a four-rak'ah prayer, the imam should not be a masbuq (one who missed part of the prayer), and there must be no row of women between the imam and the male follower. The condition about rows of women is supported by a hadith narrated from 'Umar, marfu' to the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer by intending to follow him
مسبوق (masbuq): One who joined the congregation late and missed one or more rak'ahs
نية المقتدي (niyyat al-muqtadi): The intention of the follower to follow the imam

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling if a row of women separates the imam from the male follower?
A) The prayer is valid but disliked
B) The follower's prayer is invalid
C) The imam's prayer is invalid
D) The follower must repeat the prayer only if there is a river

Key Takeaway
The fourteen conditions for valid following ensure the congregation prayer is correctly performed; each condition has a basis in the sunnah or school reasoning.
